# Region B

112
REGION B . 
A GOBLIN EMPIRE!
Designed unlike other prisons in this dungeon, 
Region B became known as ‚Äúthe laboratory‚Äù where 
celestials studied prisoners to research the nature 
of evil and understand how best to keep it in check. 
While many of the lawful good angels and archons 
frowned on this practice, the lawful neutral and 
chaotic good guardians were less reviled. In the end, 
the angels turned a blind eye to it, and allowed the 
‚Äúharmless‚Äù experiments to continue.
Like many areas in the dungeon, this Region is a 
maze of rooms and hallways. It remained unchanged 
over the centuries and even followed the chaos of the 
first earthquake. Though inhabitants fled when wards 
were dispelled, some occupants remain bloodthirsty. 
And while the Region did not change as drastically as 
others had, it did not escape unscathed.
The air is dry, dusty and unmoving, not unlike 
being in a tomb. PCs walking through these claus-
trophobic hallways hear strange echoes and moans 
everywhere, as drafts of hot and cold air cut through 
the corridors at irregular intervals. It is at 
once inhospitable and unnerving. Now home 
to three goblinoid races, as well as various 
wild beasts, the PCs have more to worry 
about than mere traps, spooky noises, and un-
explainable visions.
The inhabitants of the Region have added 
to the celestial‚Äôs magical traps with 
crude (but effective) traps of their own. 
Tripwire, scything blades, and pit traps 
make navigating this Region diffi-
cult for low-level PCs. All the while, clever 
goblinoids hunt the PCs at every turn. If there 
is one thing the Region is known for, it‚Äôs this 
flavor of chaos.
Before the Region‚Äôs newest visitors arrived, 
the dungeon contained a distorted hierarchy, 
where celestials guarded against potential 
escape from the demons inside and an-
gels stood vigilant against all manner of evil 
confined within. After the earthquake, all that 
changed. When the majority of rooms were 
emptied and the demons inside the remaining 
cells no longer had any hope of escape, the 
Region was abandoned. Many celestials lost 
their lives in the riots that erupted over the 
centuries that followed and the decision to seal 
Region¬†N was made.
And while the angels looked away, creatures 
migrated to Region B, looking for a new home 
where order was as common as justice.

113
Goblinoids arrived en masse, digging through 
whatever hole they could find, following the derro 
and drow. However, the northernmost reaches of the 
dungeon had already been ‚Äúclaimed‚Äù and the crea-
tures were quickly pushed south. As the years went 
by, more and more goblins arrived and migration to 
Region B became easier.
Once they arrived, camps formed quickly and the 
goblins skirmished with the bugbears and the bug-
bears warred with the hobgoblins. They returned to 
their way of life and fights over territory became as 
common as goblin tribe name changes.
Hundreds of years of warfare lead to the goblinoids 
trading control like currency. No single force ever 
stayed in power for more than a generation (and to 
goblinoids that‚Äôs more like 8 years) and the condition 
of the Region is in a state of flux, no matter what the 
goblin king (Room B75) says.
For centuries, the bugbears have fought a two front 
war against the goblins and hobgoblins, never allying 
with either and always seeking to route the other 
races from the Region. Their strength and ferocity 
easily dominated the goblins in battle and forced the 
hobgoblins into a remote corner of the region. They 
learned to use the traps built by the celestials to their 
own advantage, often luring the less intelligent gob-
lins into them. Only the sheer numbers of goblins 
and the tactics employed by the hobgoblins prevent-
ed the bugbears from totally dominating the Region 
as the sole goblinoid race.
The hobgoblins, currently the smallest group of 
goblinoids in the dungeon, try in vain to assert con-
trol over the Region. Their tactics and strategies are 
sound, but with their number diminished they are 
never able to claim more than a scant portion of the 
Region. Once, they ruled the northeastern portion of 
the dungeon but their rule was cut short by the earth-
quake. The damage done to their domain was stag-
gering, and their ranks decimated as a result. They 
were forced back towards the center of the dungeon, 
where they have been trapped between the goblins 
and bugbears ever since.
The goblins, led by their king Sug‚Äôkt in recent years, 
are by far the most numerous race in the Region. 
Their sheer numbers have allowed them to hold their 
ground against the bugbears for centuries. Surpris-
ingly, they had few overt clashes with the hobgoblins. 
The bugbears were a large enough threat that the 
smaller contingent of hobgoblins often went unno-
ticed. Over the years a stalemate has emerged, and 
an uneasy status quo has evolved.
None of the races are content, however. Far from it.
Recently, a force like none before arrived to alter 
the landscape and bring new order to the Region. If 
you query the goblins, they tell you: a new god has 
arrived. A statue of his likeness lies to the east and is 
nothing less than awe-inspiring. The goblins at last 
have a champion to smite their oppressors.
So great is the power of this faith in Norendithas 
Stoneshaper the Quickthinking, Smiter of Foes, that 
the goblins splintered and even with the goblin king‚Äôs 
power, he was unable to unite the fractured tribe. 
Forming their own brand of culture, the goblins now 
pay homage to their great god, who graces them with 
power and terror, promising to rain justice down 
upon their enemies.

114
Upon hearing news of this new deity the goblin 
king became enraged. As his kingdom became en-
tranced with the concept of a goblin god, he sensed 
his power and influence slipping. A close advisor to 
the king suggested he embrace the new religion.
The king would have none of it.
With Sug‚Äôkt set against the new god, his advisors 
rose up and imprisoned him for heresy. The supersti-
tious guards led the goblin king away and the charis-
matic advisor, known as Argliss, assumed the throne, 
proclaiming himself king and the direct messenger of 
their god. In one fell swoop, he reunited the troubled 
people and forged a new religion, one that could be 
used to create whatever laws he chose, through the 
will of their new god. And while no one noticed, the 
new king systematically changed the entire goblin 
culture in a few brief strokes, bending them in the 
direction of his personal ideals.
Argliss, the new goblin king, was and still is a dop-
pelganger. He wandered into this Region less than 
a decade ago and was amused by the goblins. Able 
to hide his form, his brilliant mind made the dop-
pelganger stand out. Soon he became an advisor to 
the king, and when the opportunity to become more 
presented itself, he seized it. Despite his brilliant, 
tactical, and plotting mind, he cannot see all things at 
once and the truth of this ‚Äúdeity‚Äù is not what it seems.
In truth, this deity was nothing more than a way-
ward hunter, turned to stone by a cockatrice (Room 
C16). Frightened by this unfamiliar creature, the gob-
lin‚Äôs eyes went wide and he raised his arms over his 
head in a meager attempt to protect himself. It was in 
this pose that he was most unfortunately petrified by 
the cockatrice. Goblins that followed, misinterpreting 
the stone goblin‚Äôs fearful expression, concluded that 
a new and powerful goblin god was looking down on 
them, demanding their favor and devotion. How else 
could they explain this awkward statue?
While the majority of the goblins follow their new 
god and king, a sizeable minority have broken off 
and formed a resistance movement. They continued 
to follow their old religion and despise the new king 
for usurping the throne. They are not alone in their 
opposition to the new regime.
The bugbears found themselves on the receiving 
end of ferocious attacks and canny strategy soon 
after Argliss claimed the throne. The new goblin king 
has struck a pact with the hobgoblins that remain, 
and now they serve the goblin king as instructors, 
advisors, and enforcers. Using worgs and howlers as 
mounts, they‚Äôve created a fast-attack unit like noth-
ing the goblins could even conceive of. With their 
new allies and tactics and their new god, the goblins 
have driven back the bugbears, asserting their con-
trol over the majority of the Region. Now the goblins 
under Argliss fight a two-front war for the first time 
in their history. The rebel goblins in the south and 
the bugbears in the north harass and chip away at 
Argliss‚Äô empire bit by bit, using every bit of cunning 
and trickery at their disposal. For all their bravado 
however, the zealous goblins under Argliss are firmly 
in control of the Region.
Dominated by an iron fist, the goblin empire will 
not (and cannot) be opposed.

115
WHAT ELSE
But the Region isn‚Äôt all goblins and mad religions. In 
addition to the goblinoids, a number of other beasts 
call this Region home. Dire wolves, a few undead, and 
so many traps that the goblins cannot see straight.
More than a few ethereal marauders were trapped 
in this Region around the time of the earthquake. For 
the most part they make their home in the northeast-
ern section of the dungeon.
Whether brought in by the celestials to curtail the 
activities of the goblinoids, or simply here due to the 
aftermath of the earthquake, this Region is home to a 
number of blink dogs. They can be found throughout 
the dungeon, except for in the domain of the goblin 
king. Here they are hunted as vermin by the goblins. 
The blink dogs are mainly found in the northern and 
northeastern sections of the dungeon.
The most unique creature in the dungeon is the 
goblin king‚Äôs mount: a yeth hound. How it came to 
be trapped in this Region is unknown. Shortly after 
Argliss‚Äô rise to power, it arrived and he immediately 
charged his hobgoblin taskmasters with capturing it 
and turning it into his personal mount.
While most of the traps were designed to contain 
and ‚Äúhold‚Äù the inhabitants of the dungeon, some 
take the form of puzzles that the unwary must solve, 
lest they suffer at the celestials‚Äô hands. And if that 
weren‚Äôt enough, Argliss has ordered more traps be 
made to secure his ‚Äúkingdom".
Lastly, somewhere in the darkness, a halfling 
adventurer searches for a powerful artifact that has 
slipped through the goblin king‚Äôs grasp.
THE HALFLING
Found throughout the Region is a halfling adventurer 
named Bartleby.
It is very likely the PCs will encounter him long 
before they find Toom B28. If they do, this is the Ran-
dom Encounter text.
BARTLEBY
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: Along with the goblinoids and other 
creatures that inhabit this dungeon, there is a 
solitary halfling named Bartleby. While the halfling 
normally is found in Room B28, he is by no means 
stationary. The PCs have a chance of encountering 
him anywhere in the dungeon.
How the halfling entered the dungeon is un-
known. He is in league with the goblin king and 
searches for a mysterious artifact of allegedly great 
power (see sidebar The Artifact). While the goblins 
know of the halfling, they don‚Äôt know much. Any at-
tempt to glean information from a captured goblin 
reveals that a halfling is in the dungeon and that 
they assist him if he is attacked. Otherwise, they are 
to leave him alone.
The halfling, Bartleby, is only concerned with his 
own well-being and his quest for the artifact. He is 
in league with the goblin king solely to garner the 
protection of the goblins. Once he finds his artifact 
he will leave the dungeon, presumably by the way 
he entered.
Encounter Condition: Ambush
Tactics: Bartleby fights as long as he needs to in or-
der to escape. He knows the dungeon very well and 
is confident he can lose any attackers as long as he 
can flee. If the PCs capture him, Bartleby becomes 
belligerent, hurling insults and curses at the PCs. 
He does not answer any questions and attempts to 
escape at the first possible opportunity.
Treasure: Aside from his possessions, Bartleby has no 
other treasure.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter 
use the improved versions of Bartleby‚Äôs rogue abili-
ties listed under ‚ÄúDifficulty Increase.‚Äù

116
THE KEY
During the chaos that resulted in the years following 
the second earthquake, the celestials sealed off this 
portion of the dungeon, locking all the doors leading 
north. None of the doors that lead to Region E can 
be opened or unlocked without the aid of a key found 
in Region C (Room C105 to be exact). The celestials 
entrusted the key to the lantern archon in Region C, 
who in turn hid it in a room full of false keys.
When this fake key is used to unlock any of the 
doors leading north, a sonic blast trap is triggered. In 
addition to the damage caused to the PCs, the sound 
automatically alerts all creatures in adjacent rooms.
 '
Thunderous Glyph of Warding Trap. As the incorrect 
key is inserted, the channels align with the trigger 
mechanism, setting off a series of ominous clicks 
and thuds. A magic hum whirrs for only a moment, 
during which time those who can perceive magic 
will bear witness to white hot runes searing the area 
around the lock. Seconds later a thunderous blast 
rips from the keyhole. Any creature within 5¬†ft must 
succeed a (DC¬†13) Dexterity saving throw or take 
8d4 Thunder damage and be knocked back 10¬†ft. 
Creatures that succeed the saving throw take half 
damage and are not moved.
The trap is ancient, with evocation magic inside 
only glowing faintly when idle, and invisible without 
detect magic. Succeeding an Intelligence (Investiga-
tion) check (DC¬†15) gives the player the impression 
that the lock is suspiciously made, appearing to 
accept false keys for an unknown purpose.
Dispel magic will eliminate the trap, but the door 
remains locked. After detonating or being dispelled 
the trap resets in 1d6 minutes.
PCs using the real key are allowed passage to 
Region E. Use the following encounter for every door 
that leads to Region F.
B0. LOCKED DOOR
This Encounter is not printed on the Map. Instead, 
anytime a PC attempts to leave the Region through 
doors to the north, read the following:
Before you stands a door. Bound in iron, and 
standing over 10¬†ft tall it is unlike any door you‚Äôve 
ever seen. The keyhole is a giant griffon head, its 
mouth agape.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This door is locked and cannot be opened 
by any means short of the key in Room C105. Any 
attempt to open it with either the wrong key, a 
Sleight of Hand, or knock triggers a Thunderous 
Glyph of Warding trap (see above). PCs that attempt 
to disable or dispel the trap find that it resets itself 
in 1d6 minutes.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: Any attempt to discern the properties of the 
door gives the impression of heavy amounts of 
abjuration magic, a complex (almost unbeatable) 
lock, and a magical trap that triggers when the lock 
is tampered with. The GM is more than welcome 
to assign DCs to the checks necessary to learn this 
information, but it is crucial that they learn it none-
theless. Allow them to spend 30 minutes study-
ing the door.
The door itself is sturdy, made of iron, and with 
hinges mounted on the other side from where 
the party is. The PCs should also realize that a key 
does exist for it (as the tumblers are exact and 
meticulous) and using the wrong key triggers the 
trap as well.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: It is not recommended that you increase or 
decrease the difficulty of this encounter. PCs who 
persist with this lock are asking for trouble. GMs 
should not ‚Äúkill‚Äù the PCs with this trap, but instead 
hint that it can‚Äôt be bypassed at the moment.

117
SOME THINGS TO KEEP IN MIND
The PCs should be 3rd or 4th level when they reach this Section of the dungeon. That means even twelve 
goblins won‚Äôt be much trouble.
In order to keep the challenge, the GM should try a few things.
One. Give your goblins a significant baseline edge. 
Throw a standing +4 to their initiative roles be-
cause this is their home turf. Add +2 to attacks 
for the well-defended backline in formation. 
Throw in some unexpected weapons scavenged by 
lucky raiders.
Two. Add toughness. What‚Äôs wrong with trained gob-
lins having a few extra hit points. It would be worse 
if you gave them extra levels, right?
Three. Add natural armor. A +2 or +4 AC bonus makes 
the goblins tougher but also means that rogues and 
clerics are going to be less useful.
Four. Aid Another. With so many goblins, the Help 
Action really adds up. Don‚Äôt be afraid to have a few 
of the goblins extend a helping hand.
Five. Dogpile. Goblins working together to tackle a 
dwarf or human barbarian severely weaken a group 
that‚Äôs grown too reliant on the 12 points of damage 
per round 19 Strength, two-handed great greataxe, 
raging, killing machine. Before the barbarian even 
thinks of raging, he‚Äôs on the ground, prone and 
weaponless.
Six. Give the goblins the benefit of the doubt. They 
know the PCs are on the move and they know how 
to lure them into traps. Triplines across doorways, 
nearby reinforcements ready to attack from the 
rear, and signal whistles add up to one memorable 
encounter.
Seven. Limit the PCs‚Äô options before they get here. 
Spells like fireball should be limited at this point in 
the campaign, so fighting in tight ranks won‚Äôt hurt 
the goblins. Don‚Äôt let a wizard with one spell spoil 
your adventures. Plan for it. Build around it.
Eight. Add a hobgoblin to every encounter. While not 
all of them need to be 4th-level fighters, a 1st-level 
fighter at the back of the ranks, directing the action 
and throwing alchemical fire or firing a heavy cross-
bow does more than increase the CR by 1.
Nine. Stagger the assaults. Eventually the barbarian 
tires out. His rage goes away and another wave 
of goblins arrive on the final round of his ‚Äúenergy 
boost.‚Äù How did that happen?
Ten: Add Encounter Conditions that we didn‚Äôt think 
of. Make the room pitch black in a 5¬†ft radius or 
add a stench effect (similar to troglodytes) that the 
goblins are immune to (or used to).
GOBLIN TACTICS, OR 20 WAYS TO DIE
Many of the rooms in this Region resemble one an-
other. This is intentional. Once the goblins descend 
on the PCs it is most likely they will be fighting wave 
after wave of reinforcements. And with 25% of the 
goblin population out patrolling at any given time, a 
battle in a hallway or room brings the goblins in the 
adjacent areas down upon the PCs quickly.
And because the goblins have been trained by hob-
goblins, they all carry similar weapons and fight with 
the same tactics. This makes the range of Encounters 
limited. PCs are likely to get bored after the third 
room. This is where the GM comes in.
If played out properly, a single goblin Encounter 
can take up half the evening. By having wave after 
wave of reinforcements pushing into the room, PCs 
are likely to tire quickly. Or at the very least, have 
their patience tested, when the door to the room 
opens for the fourth time with another wave of twelve 
goblins. Worse yet, the first three waves are there just 

118
Eleven. Improvise. Marines don‚Äôt plan. They adapt. 
Effective goblin assaults should be no different. If 
the tactics in this book don‚Äôt work, change them. 
Have them shore up a weak point, send in a smaller 
goblin to aid with flanks, or carry slings in addition 
to spears to take advantage of the second ranks.
Twelve: Add cool magical effects. Give the goblins 
potions of orc blood (the undercommon version of 
heroism) allowing them to rage for 3 rounds or gain 
+2 Strength for 2d6 rounds. Maybe their weapons 
are coated with a sleep poison or something that 
just deals 1 point on the following round, enough to 
make the PCs nervous. ‚ÄúHey. They‚Äôve got +1 wound-
ing spears. What gives?‚Äù
Thirteen. Make the religion real. The goblin‚Äôs faith is 
stronger than anything and thus they benefit from 
spells like guidence and shield of faith, despite the 
lack of clerics. Heck. Add a 1st-level cleric to each 
unit. If you don‚Äòt like clerics, add adepts, druids, or 
sorcerers with access to a domain spell list or grant-
ed power (or both).
Fourteen: Be smart. Don‚Äôt let the PC‚Äôs lure teams 
of goblins into stupid grease tricks. Anytime the 
PCs are backing up and don‚Äôt look injured, trained 
soldiers know that means trouble. The goblins 
should hold back, send for reinforcements, and 
batter the PCs later with some magical assistance or 
brute strength.
Fifteen: Pace the encounters. Don‚Äôt let the PCs charge 
from room to room wiping out all the goblins be-
fore they sound the alarm. Lock or bar a few doors. 
Make it tough for the PCs to get into the more 
protected areas.
Sixteen. Give the goblins advantage on all saving 
throws vs. spell effects.
Seventeen. Choose your battles. The goblins don‚Äôt 
have to fight the PCs every time. They can lure the 
PCs out of a room and force them to fight in a con-
fined space, where their larger weapons are useless.
Eighteen. Worgs. The goblins have dire wolves, 
howlers, worgs, and yeth hounds at their disposal. 
Give each goblin unit some firepower with a canine 
or lupine companion. Perhaps a blink dog was 
corrupted by the taint of the stables? Perhaps they 
found a destrachan from Region D?
Nineteen. Drop the anvil. Once the PCs are out of 
spells, potions, and wand charges, have the big 
boys show up and make the PCs rely on wits in-
stead of magic.
Twenty. Make the PCs work for it. If the PCs are 
smart about it, they can decimate the entire goblin 
army in less than a week, or become another in the 
long list of victims that have fallen under Haglar‚Äôs 
or Hammerfist‚Äôs boot. No encounter in this dun-
geon should be ‚Äúeasy.‚Äú Take the next step and show 
the PCs what you‚Äôre made of.
to weaken the PCs, using up their magic for the real 
final battle with Goblinbane.
To complicate matters, should the PCs successfully 
beat back everything you throw at them, they‚Äôll need 
to find a place to rest and that patrol or scouting par-
ty is due back any minute, more than ready to go for 
help, should they see the PCs standing knee deep in 
dead goblins. PCs on the run from goblins? Never.
And if word gets back to the goblin king that half 
his army is dead, a worg cavalry unit and a few hob-
goblin bodyguards can be hunting the PCs down in 
no time flat.
 

119
B1-B48 . THE ABANDONED  
HALLS OF THE CELESTIALS
Unlike the other Sections of the Region, this initial 
expanse is not lorded over by any one particular 
group. The earthquake damaged this section the 
least, and the celestials that survive in traps and 
puzzles make the goblinoids wary about settling here.
Blink dogs and dire wolves have taken advantage 
of the lack of goblinoids in the area, and many dens 
are scattered throughout these rooms. A few packs of 
howlers prowl the area, though most howlers live in 
the Wild Caverns (Rooms B119 through B133).
The celestials used this Section to study and 
document evil. It was a quiet place for the more 
scholarly angels to note anything unusual about the 
evil and unholy beasts they guarded. Several rooms 
recorded how demons and devils reacted to traps 
and puzzles.
In general, the air is musty. As few things live here, 
the odors of life and death are not as prevalent. While 
the PCs may not have to worry about encountering 
a staggering number of monsters, they need to 
keep their wits sharper than their swords. There is a 
reason the goblinoids merely patrol this Section‚Äî
the celestials‚Äô traps are daunting and difficult 
to overcome.
 '
Portcullis Trap. When 15 lbs. of weight are applied 
to the pressure plate on either side of the arch a 
portcullis slams down. Creatures underneath are 
skewered and crushed and must succeed a Dexterity 
saving throw (DC¬†13) or take 2d8 piercing and 2d8 
bludgeoning damage. Additionally, creatures that 
fail to save are pinned underneath, preventing 
movement until freed. Any creature that can lift 200 
lbs. of weight can reliably lift the gate 1¬†ft off the 
ground, with the weight requirement doubling for 
each additional foot of distance desired.
While not subtle, the trap still requires active 
attention to notice. Once found the plate can 
simply be stepped over, or disabled by wedging the 
pressure plate.
The pressure plates are clumsy and obvious, only 
requiring a (DC¬†10) Wisdom (Perception) check to 
spot. Disarming the gate is similarly trivial, only 
requiring a (DC¬†12) Dexterity (Thieves' Tools) check 
to pin the plates in place.
RAnDoM EnCoUnTERs
Roll for a Random Encounter once per hour.

(DC¬†13) each hour or be frightened of a 
random cardinal direction.

Four blink dogs wander the halls, sniffing 
for goblins. They are indifferent to the PCs 
unless attacked.

A bugbear sets up a tripwire. He may or may 
not notice the PCs. For the duration of 3d6 
seconds, Wisdom (Perception) checks are 
made at disadvantage, at which point he 
finishes setting up the tripwire.

2d4 goblins (half of which ride worgs) patrol 
the Section, looking for anything to report 
back to their king. When the PCs are spotted, 
one rides off for help while the others fight 
defensively to stop the PCs from getting 
further into the Region.

the encounter.

The PCs stumble upon a hallway trapped 
with burning hands.

Bartleby the Halfling (Room B28) is

120
They are thin enough for non-small PCs to 
simply step across. This trap resets only when the 
knock spell is cast on it, which is a preferred method 
of the celestial caretakers.
 '
Razor Wire. Difficult to spot (DC¬†14 Wisdom 
(Perception) check) filaments of magically 
sharpened wire are strung haphazardly across the 
hallway. Contact with which causes deep cuts and 
deadly tangling. Each creature caught in the trap 
receives 1d6 slashing damage and must succeed a 
Dexterity saving throw or be tangled.
Tangled creatures take 1d6 slashing damage 
each combat round (or every 6 seconds) and 
another 1d6 if they attempt to free themselves. A 
successful Strength save (DC¬†11) frees the affected 
creature, ending the effect. Other non-trapped 
creatures may spend an action to attempt to 
free them, requiring a (DC¬†10) Strength check 
to succeed. On a success or failure, the rescuer 
receives 1d6 slashing damage.
Once spotted disarming requires a trivial (DC¬†8) 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to sever the wires 
from the wall. The process is lengthy however, 
requiring 20 minutes of work to fully clear. 
Partially cleared (10 minutes of work at least) gives 
advantage on saves made to resist the trap‚Äôs effects 
for potential victims.
 '
Tripping Chain. Strung across the path is a thin 
chain. Robust enough to be a tripping hazard, and 
acting as a setup for a much nastier chain. Both 
are simple and crudely concealed (DC¬†11) Wisdom 
(Perception) required to spot). Stepping on the first 
chain will knock the victim prone unless they pass a 
Dexterity or Strength saving throw (DC¬†12), wherein 
they must make a second Dexterity saving throw 
(DC¬†14) to take half damage from falling onto the 
spiked chain.
Creatures that step onto the spiked chain 
receive 2d8 piercing damage as the wicked hooks 
and barbs rend at them. They may also trip from 
this, requiring the same saves as above but done 
with advantage this time. Reduce this damage 
by 1 for every point of AC the creature possesses 
over 12. Creatures that fall onto the chain receive 
an additional 1d8 damage for each size category 
they are above small (medium +1d8, large +2d8, 
huge +3d8).
Outside of adverse circumstances small and tiny 
creatures are not tall enough to fall onto the spiked 
chain and simply faceplant into the flooring.
Disarming the chains requires the removal 
of the interlocking pins that keep them taut and 
tossing them aside. No check is needed once 
spotted. The mechanism isn‚Äôt completely intuitive, 
however. Less mechanically inclined PCs might 
require a successful Intelligence (Investigation) 
(DC¬†10) check to understand.
 '
Burning Hands Trap. Odd pairs of ethereal blue 
hands dot the walls, their gestures queer to those 
not in the know. Magically inclined PCs, or those 
that pass an Intelligence (Arcana) (DC¬†13) check 
recognize these as somatic spell components frozen 
in time. The spells they would be casting are diverse 
and easily recognizable by those who know the 
spells. A knock here, a commune there; goodberry, 
raise dead, alter self. Of the 30 hands present, all 
save for one are ‚Äúcasting‚Äù harmless spells. Any 
Intelligence (Investigation) check by a magic-user 
should yield the above list as suggestions for the 
potential spells they might be casting, with burning 
hands added in if they roll a 13 or greater. Should 
they keep inquiring, simply consult the spell list for 
more harmless spells to have them ‚Äúcasting.‚Äù Given 
enough time and prodding the PCs would stumble 
across the burning hands pair.
Creatures that can see magic will see each hand 
enchanted with a faint glow corresponding to their 
assigned spell‚Äôs school.
Each pair can be permanently dispelled with a 
dispel magic cast (DC¬†12).
If you would like the hands to cast their 
associated spells go right ahead, but for now, 
the only pair capable of casting a spell are those 
forming burning hands. Creatures that cross an 
invisible line from between the fingers of the 
burning hands to the opposite wall trigger the 
casting. The burning hands spell is cast at level 1 
targeting the far wall each time the mechanism is 
triggered, resetting after 6 seconds while the hands 
perform the gestures to ready it again.
The mechanism cannot be disarmed with 
physical tools, though a clever rogue might realize 
it can be simply ducked under or triggered with 
objects given some experimentation and/or a 
successful Intelligence (Investigation) (DC¬†14) check.

121
THE ARTIFACT
The (doppelganger) goblin king, Argliss, has 
lost a powerful artifact. At some point during 
his rise to power over the goblins, the artifact 
disappeared. While it is not crucial to his 
reign, he does not wish for it to fall into the 
hands of his many enemies and rivals to his 
throne. His new position does not allow him 
to search, but a halfling, Bartleby, is more 
than happy to search for the artifact. He has 
gained the protection of the dominant faction 
in the Region and enjoys enormous freedom. 
He has no plans to turn the artifact over to 
Argliss, however. Anything that powerful is not 
something you give away lightly. Once he has 
found the artifact Bartleby plans to leave the 
Region entirely, using his newfound power as 
he sees fit.
What the artifact is, however, is strictly up 
to the GM. It could be something so truly 
powerful that whoever has possession of it can 
rule the Region, or it could be a red herring 
to draw the PCs‚Äô attention away from the real 
dangers in the Region.
POSSIBLE ARTIFACTS
 
Clay Golem Manual. The ability to craft golems 
gives the PCs a powerful tool for navigating 
the dungeon.
 
Medallion of Thoughts. Reading the thoughts 
and intentions of the more deceitful denizens 
the PCs could prove invaluable to their 
survival.
 
Necklace of Adaptation. Eventually the PCs will 
need to cross the Lake (Region L) and being 
able to breathe underwater might help.
 
Phylactery of Undead Turning. Useful for the 
ghouls and wights found in the later rooms 
of the dungeon.
 
Rod of Cancellation. The PCs are not the only 
group in the dungeon using magical items to 
aid them. The capacity to remove the power 
of their opponents‚Äô items could be key to 
their survival.
POSSIBLE LOCATIONS
 
Room B92, The Maze. With its constant 
dangers, placing the artifact in the maze 
makes for a harrowing quest. Due to the 
goblin‚Äôs superstitious fears of the maze, a 
legend has sprung up about a daring thief 
who fled with the king‚Äôs treasure into the 
maze, only to be punished by Norendithas 
Stoneshaper the Quickthinking, Smiter of 
Foes. The thief in question is eternally trapped 
in the maze, with the goblin king‚Äôs treasure 
lost in its confusing, dangerous confines.
 
Room B111, The Killing Grounds. Controlled 
by the undead of the Region, this room is 
a natural place for the artifact to have been 
misplaced. Whoever stole it fled here, only to 
be assaulted by the wights. It could be hiding 
in plain sight amongst the refuse in the room, 
or it could have been buried under the dirt 
floor. Fighting off the ghouls, as well as the 
dangers of the room itself, presents a unique 
challenge to any who seek the artifact here.
 
Room B136, Norendithas Stoneshaper the 
Quickthinking, Smiter of Foes‚Äô Shrine. 
Maybe the wayward hunter-turned-deity stole 
the artifact from the goblin king. If that‚Äôs the 
case it has been sealed in the now holy statue. 
Even Argliss would be hesitant to desecrate 
the source of his influence over the goblins in 
an effort to retrieve the artifact. The zealous 
nature of the goblins that guard the shrine 
presents unique issues for would-be treasure 
hunters.
 
Region C. Perhaps somewhere in Region C, 
the artifact has slipped through the hands of 
the goblins and into the clutches of the black 
dragon, giants, gnolls, or chaotic oozes that 
roam the corridors.
In the end, these are merely suggestions. The 
artifact can be anything and anywhere, or 
nothing and nowhere. It is solely up to the GM 
how he wishes to run the campaign.

122
B1. ENTRANCEWAY
This corridor is obviously old, but it is in fairly good 
shape. The air is musty, and a thin layer of dust 
coats the area. The walls are plain and free of mold 
or lichen. It stretches straight ahead for roughly 
30¬†ft. A second hall joins this corridor roughly 10¬†ft. 
from the entrance, while the corridor itself turns to 
the left at the end.
Encounter: The hall, while looking nondescript, 
holds the first of the celestials‚Äô traps, as well as a 
secret entrance to Room B3. A successful Wisdom 
(Perception) (DC¬†15) check reveals a stone door, 
flush with the northern wall. The door is trapped. 
Opening the door triggers the trap; a large double-
bit ax head that swings out towards the hallway. 
Before the door can be fully opened a successful 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) (DC¬†15) check is required 
to unlock it, allowing it to be opened and permitting 
the party to enter Room B3.
Ten feet into the room, where it meets the 
second hall, a pressure-triggered trapdoor awaits. 
It opens into a 10-ft-wide-by-20-ft deep pit filled 
with several sharpened spikes. It is triggered as 
soon as someone steps on the stone floor. Springs 
hidden under the trapdoor reset the trap once it 
is triggered. A Wisdom (Perception) check with a 
roll of 15 or greater alerts the PC‚Äôs that the floor 
above the pit has a thinner layer of dust than the 
surrounding area. See below for full trap rules.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the difficulty of this encounter, 
double the depth of the pit and roll 5d10 for the 
ax-trap instead of 2d20. To reduce the difficulty, 
double the amount of temporary hit points granted 
to players caught in the pit trap.
 '
Scything Blade Trap (door mounted). When pried 
open the door easily allows one inch of clearance. 
Doing so reveals the keyhole and arms the spring-
loaded ax. A specific key, which might be found on 
someone important, will disarm the mechanism 
and open the lock. Otherwise, simply picking the 
lock is doable, but results in the door flying free 
on spring-loaded hinges with the ax scything 
into the hallway. Creatures within 5¬†ft. of the 
door must succeed two separate Dexterity saving 
throws (DC¬†13).
The first save avoids the swinging door and 
allows them to stay in place. Creatures that fail this 
save take 1d8 bludgeoning damage, knocking the 
creature back 5¬†ft in any direction, out of the way of 
the axe. If there is no room for the creature they are 
hit and knocked prone instead.
Standing, Medium-sized creatures and above 
that remain within 5¬†ft of the trap after the door 
springs open must succeed their second save or be 
struck by the swinging ax. Pick the first to be struck 
and roll 2d20. Subtract that target's AC from the 
amount, and deal that much slashing damage to 
them. If more than zero damage is dealt, perform 
this again for each creature in line to be struck 
using the remaining damage instead of the initial 
roll for each subsequent hit. (e.g., GM rolls a 24, the 
first creature struck has 13 AC, they take 11 damage. 
The ax swings through, hitting the next creature 
who has 10 AC, which reduces the remaining 11 
damage they would take down to 1, continuing 
until zero).
To disarm the trap the door must remain locked 
and opened as much as it allows. The mechanism 
can be tripped from the inside with a (DC¬†13) 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check. As the guide pins 
pop loose the axe slams loudly into the closed door 
before the stress on the mechanism ruptures its 
hinges and it clanks worthlessly against the floor.
 '
Spiked Pit Trap. When 15 lbs. or more of weight 
are applied to the 10¬†ft. wide trap door panel the 
clutch releases, dropping the section on a hinge 
and plunging any creature atop it into a 20-ft 
pit. A feat of Dexterity (Acrobatics) or Strength 
(Athletics) would be required to mitigate the 
ensuing skewering on the spikes below. Creatures 
will choose which skill to use, and roll the check as 
normal. The resulting roll is gained as temporary 
hit points (representing their heroic attempts to 
grapple with the pit walls and dodge the spikes), 
before they take 3d10 piercing damage, in addition 
to fall damage.
These temporary hit points are lost when 
they exit the pit and stack with other sources of 
temporary hit points.

123
Disabling the trigger requires crossing to the 
far side (a 10¬†ft, jump) and wedging the hinge with 
something sturdy, which requires a (DC¬†7) Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand).
B2 . ABANDONED GUARD POST
This room is long and narrow. Toppled benches and 
tables lie in disarray throughout the space. Weapon 
racks stand empty in the western corner. Whoever 
used this room has long since deserted it. The 
dust is thicker in here than in previous rooms and 
you kick it up into the air with every step. Several 
burnt-out torches lie on the floor as well and the 
air has a slightly smoky quality to it. Strange 
carvings line the back wall, and an aged leather 
hide hangs on the eastern wall.
A secret door in the southeast corner can be 
discovered by a successful Wisdom (Perception) 
(DC¬†15) check. The door‚Äôs lock is jammed and requires 
a successful Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) (DC¬†15) check 
to open. The door leads to Room B4.
Encounter Condition: Haunted
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: Wedged between two stones in the 
corner of the room is a small tarnished and 
chipped silver dagger. It can be found by PCs who 
roll a 15+ on Wisdom (Perception) checks while 
examining the room.
Scaling: N/A
B3 . OBSERVATORY
The ax swings lazily in the doorway. Stepping 
around it you enter a stark chamber. Along the 
western wall is a table and chair, both built 
of stone. Along the northern wall rests a large 
bookcase. Only a few ancient leather-bound 
books remain on its shelves. Aside from these few 
furnishings, the chamber is empty.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room was built to observe the 
demonic and devilish prisons of this Region. The 
celestials crafted it to be as unobtrusive as possible. 
From here they could freely observe the unholy 
hordes closely. It has been abandoned for quite 
some time.
The leather books remaining are quite fragile. 
Unless the PCs are incredibly careful, the pages 
crumble when handled. Unless one of the PCs is 
fluent in Celestial, the text requires a successful 
Wisdom (Insight) check (DC¬†18) to translate. Even 
if a PC understands Celestial, the text is in such 
disarray, that another successful Insight check 
(DC¬†15) to translate is required to make sense of it.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: The few remaining journals, if deciphered, 
give the PCs a broad sense of the previous 
inhabitants in this dungeon. They primarily detail 
the demons and devils that were here 2,000 years 
ago. If this is the first the PCs have learned of the 
purpose of the dungeon, allow each person reading 
the tome a single question.
Scaling: N/A
B4 . SECRET ARMORY
The door slides inward, creaking loudly on rusty 
hinges. The interior is dark, but it is not impossible 
to see into the room. The walls are lined with racks 
and racks of simple weapons: spears, clubs, and 
slings. The spearheads are dull, but the dry air has 
prevented them from rusting. Two large barrels 
towards the back of the chamber are filled with 
small rocks, obviously ammunition for the slings. 
Someone is obviously stockpiling weapons for a 
prolonged conflict, and they might be back soon.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears that were formerly 
stationed in Room B2 kept their weapons in this 
hidden storage room. The weapons are crude and 
even a layman can tell they were hastily built.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: The room contains two dozen javelins. 
They are of inferior quality, but not to the point 
which causes any meaningful trouble. The two 
barrels, combined, hold roughly 170 lbs. of gravel 
suitable for use as bullets for the three dozen 
slings contained in the armory. The dozen clubs 
found here are not discernable in any way from 
other clubs.
Scaling: N/A

124
B5 . TRAP ROOM
As the PCs approach the door to Room B5, read the 
following.
The corridor wraps around a square structure in 
the center of this room. As you walk around it you 
notice a large stone door set in the center of the 
wall‚Äôs western side. The stone of the door is slightly 
darker than the walls and is carved with various 
indecipherable runes.
The door to this room is trapped.
 '
Falling Stone Trap. The trigger to the falling stone 
trap is embedded in the handle of the stone door. 
Attempting to open the stone door by grasping 
the handle causes the handle to pull outwards 
while the door remains shut. After an ominous 
click an enchanted slab of stone, pocked by time 
and use, silently falls. Its immense weight slams 
into anything within 10 feet of the door. Creatures 
must make a Dexterity (DC¬†14) saving throw or 
take 4d8 bludgeoning damage as they are caught 
underneath. Objects cannot make this save, and 
take double damage. Any that succeed are pushed 
to the edge of the falling block as they scramble out 
of the way. After ten seconds the block raises and 
resets. Opening the door by prying the gap safely 
avoids the crushing. While the door is open the trap 
will not trigger so as to not damage the door itself.
When the PCs enter the room, read the following.
The room is large and empty apart from a pedestal 
resting against the far wall. The floor is tiled in 
dark granite, with a line of polished white marble 
leading from the door to the pedestal. Upon the 
pedestal, there is a golden idol embedded with two 
emerald gems for eyes and a pearl set in its belly.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This is a particularly difficult encounter 
and if the PCs are smart, they will leave before it 
escalates.
The celestials that occupied Room B3 designed 
this room to test the intelligence of the prisoners. It 
contains a series of three traps, each slightly more 
advanced and deadly than the next. The room itself 
is 30 ft. wide by 40¬†ft long.
The first test is the door to the room. This is the 
most straightforward of the traps.
The second trap is built into the floor of the 
room. The floor tiles are the key to this trap. Each 
tile is 2-ft-by-2-ft The obvious path is straight down 
the middle, following the white marble. Of course 
any path that obvious must be a trap. The celestials 
took this into account. To circumvent this trap the 
PCs must travel down, staying on either side of the 
path, walking a thin line. The white and black tiles 
nearest each other represent the only safe paths 
to the pedestal. The PCs must stay within the 4-ft. 
wide path created by the joined black and white 
tiles. If they stray to either side of these paths, the 
trap triggers, raining metal shards and caltrops on 
the occupants of the room from concealed slots in 
the ceiling.
A successful Wisdom (Perception) (DC¬†12) check 
reveals the paths are slightly more worn than the 
surrounding tiles while a roll of 16+ reveals the 
nature of the trap.
If the PCs can make it to the idol, they must 
circumvent a third trap to claim the prize. This is 
a simple pressure plate under the idol. If the PCs 
do not disable it before they remove the idol, the 
plate triggers spring-loaded poisoned darts hidden 
behind the eastern wall. Once the PCs have the idol 
they can safely leave the room.
 '
Raining Shards. When the appropriate tile is 
depressed by more than 10 lbs. of force the room-
wide trap triggers. Slots in the ceiling drop metal 
blades onto every inch of the space beneath them. 
No amount of dodging can save those caught in the 
gale of sharpened metal. Creatures within the room 
take 4d10 slashing damage, minus the victim‚Äôs AC 
(minimum zero), and an additional 2d10 if they are 
not wearing any head-covering.
Creatures with shields have resistance to the 
damage dealt by this trap.
If a creature is within 5¬†ft. of another that is at 
least a size larger than them they can attempt a 
Dexterity saving throw (DC¬†14) to halve the damage. 
This trap fires once per room reset.
 '
Spring-loaded Darts. When half the idol‚Äôs weight 
is added to or removed from the pedestal a spray 
of darts snap across the room. Starting from the 
east wall any creature not completely obscured by 

125
another must succeed a Dexterity (DC¬†13) saving 
throw or take 2d8 piercing damage and be poisoned 
until their next long rest.
The trap-holes can be found with a DC¬†16 
Intelligence (Investigation) check, and disabled 
with a further DC¬†16 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand). 
Undoing this mechanism leaves the darts open for 
the taking. The first time a dart deals damage it 
loses its poison and poisons the target if they fail a 
Constitution (DC¬†14) save.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: As soon as the idol passes beyond the 
doorway it instantly turns to dust, the traps reset, 
and the door closes. This was the final test the 
celestials had‚Äîto determine if demons would 
continually pursue a futile goal.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
upgrade the spring-loaded darts trap to a fusillade 
of spears trap, increasing the damage dice to d12s. 
To decrease the challenge, reduce the damage of 
the raining shards trap to 6d4.
B6 . HALL OF MIRRORS
The floor and walls of this large room are covered 
in mirrors. As soon as you enter, a stone door 
slams down from the ceiling, sealing the entrance 
behind you.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room is a single huge trap. With 
every surface covered in mirrors, it is impossible to 
find a way out. The door the PCs entered through 
is sealed and is no longer an exit. Only by finding 
the trap‚Äôs trigger and disabling it are the PCs able 
to leave this room. If they cannot, they are trapped 
here until they expire. The trigger is located in 
the northwestern corner, near the floor. A hairline 
crack (DC¬†14 Wisdom (Perception) or Intelligence 
(Investigation) check to spot) in a mirror is the only 
hint the PCs have to the trigger‚Äôs location. The 
crack is actually the edge of a removable panel that 
reveals the trigger. Succeeding a Dexterity (Sleight 
of Hand) check (DC¬†14) flips the switch and swings 
all four doors open.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase all of the DCs for the hall of mirrors trap by 
+2. To decrease the challenge, decrease the DCs by 
-3 or merely have the door open after 24 hours.
B7 . WATERFALL
This room is rough in appearance. The walls are 
pitted and uneven, as if acid vapor eroded the 
finish. The floor is covered in discs, each two ft. in 
diameter. The discs sit higher than the floor and 
wobble slightly.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The discs in this room are the key to the 
PCs successfully navigating their way across it. They 
are designed to shift and are each mounted on a 
compact spring. The PCs must carefully make their 
way across the room, which requires a successful 
Strength (Athletics) or Dexterity (Acrobatics) (DC¬†13) 
check. If the PCs stumble, or in any way touch the 
floor under the discs, the trap triggers. The doors to 
the room seal and torrents of water gush into the 
room from slots near the ceiling. The water pours 
in from both the east and west walls. The PCs have 
two minutes to disarm the trap or they drown. 
The release for the trap is located on the center 
of the middle wall requiring a DC¬†10 Intelligence 
(Investigation) or Wisdom (Perception) check to 
spot, and requires a successful Strength (Athletics) 
check (DC¬†12) to pull. Once the trap is disabled the 
water drains through grates under the discs and 
both doors to this room.
Encounter Condition: Extreme Cold, [Flooded]
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the difficulty of the encounter, 
players make the Strength (Athletics) check at 
disadvantage when the timer reaches 1 minute 
remaining as the water impedes their attempts to 
pull it. To decrease the difficulty, reduce the DCs to 
spot the lever by 5.

126
B8 . GOLD MINE
The walls of this room are flecked with gold. 
The roughly square room is filled with mounds 
of dirt and rubble. Crude picks, shovels, and the 
bones of several small goblinoids lay scattered 
on the ground. The gold flecks glow and entice 
you forward.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room, while clearly attractive to 
greedy PCs, is as much a trap as anything else 
in the Region. Touching the gold flecks releases 
poison gas into the room. As the door seals them 
in, the PCs have little choice but to disable the trap 
to survive. As long as the PCs do not touch the gold 
flecks, the trap does not trigger. There are no flecks 
on the floor at all.
If the PCs trigger the trap, they have to act 
swiftly to turn it off.
In the middle of the room is a squat stalagmite. 
A successful Intelligence (Investigation) or Wisdom 
(Perception) (DC¬†15) reveals a series of three knobby 
buttons. To disable the trap and open the door 
they must be pressed in the correct sequence. One 
attempt may be performed by the PCs each round. 
Each attempt they will roll 3 separate Intelligenc e 
(Investigation) checks (DC¬†15). Make note of each 
success and failure as a score.
When 3 failures have been noted across multiple 
attempts, reset the scores and start anew. When 
3 successes are recorded the PCs have found the 
correct sequence, the trap disarms, and the door 
opens. If a tie occurs (both hit 3 simultaneously) 
the state with any extra score wins. In the case of a 
perfect tie, reset the round as if they had failed, but 
have the PCs start with one success going into the 
new attempt.
After 24 seconds from the initial triggering 
the gas will start to leave lasting harm. Creatures 
caught in the room must succeed a Constitution 
saving throw (DC¬†8 + rounds elapsed) or take 
1d6 poison damage for each time they‚Äôve failed 
this save.
Encounter Condition: [Smoke]
Tactics: Once the trap is disarmed (or if it was never 
triggered), the PCs who make Wisdom (Perception) 
or Intelligence (Investigation) checks with a roll of 
17+ notice the transparent outline of angel wings on 
the back wall. Faint and depressed, these grooves 
are used to open the secret door leading to Room 
B13. If a PC you feel would be deemed ‚Äúgood‚Äù by 
the virtue locks used by the celestials touches the 
grooves by laying their palms flat, the wall rises up 
and remains open for 5 rounds. The secret door 
cannot be opened from the other side.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
replace the poison gas trap with an insanity mist 
vapor trap. Creatures that fail their Constitution 
saving throw must move toward and take an 
attack action against the nearest creature on their 
next turn, instead of receiving poison damage. To 
decrease the challenge, reduce the poison damage 
to a d4 or even a d2.
B9 . DIRE WOLF DEN
As the PCs approach the room, read the following.
As you make your way down the hall, you hear 
heavy breathing coming from behind the door up 
ahead. The air is dank with a discernible odor as if 
something were living here.
Once the door is open, read the following.
Your torches have trouble cutting through the 
darkness in the room. All that you smell is a dank 
odor that clings to everything. From the shadows a 
pair of large wolves rush out, fighting‚Äînipping at 
each other‚Äôs heels. Their hackles are raised as they 
would be when fighting for dominance. Turning 
and snapping, the two creatures snarl and lunge, 
attacking wildly.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: The PCs have stumbled onto a pair of dire 
wolves that were trapped in this room. They have 
been quarreling for some time, but now happily 
have something new to dominate. They attack the 
PCs on sight, fighting to the death if necessary.
If no one holds the door open, it slams behind 
the PCs. From the inside, the door is locked and 
requires a successful Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
or Strength (Athletics) (DC¬†17) check to escape. The 
other two doors are not locked, however.
Encounter Condition: Concealment, Deep Darkness, 
Fearless, [Stagnant Air]

127
Tactics: Light in this room is reduced to a 5¬†ft. radius, 
no matter how powerful the source. This puts PCs 
without darkvision at a major disadvantage.
The dire wolves have been trapped here for 
weeks, but do not fight as cohesively as pack 
animals normally do. They do not flank or aid one 
another or use any tactics to gain an advantage over 
an opponent. Instead, they simply choose a target 
and focus their energies solely on them.
If the PCs stumble around in the dark, they can 
find the carcasses of four other wolves littered here. 
Apparently, they turned on each other once they 
were trapped in this room. The two that survived 
were the largest and the strongest.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add two dire wolves. To decrease the challenge, 
reduce their hit points by -15 each.
B10 . BUGBEAR REFUGE
As the PCs approach the room, read the following.
A splintered wooden door blocks the entrance to 
this room. From behind it, you can hear a quarrel 
in a foul tongue. Something yells and a loud crash 
reverberates through the halls.
Removing the splintered wooden door without 
making a noise requires succeeding a Dexterity 
(Stealth) check (DC¬†12+ Bugbear‚Äôs Perception 
modifier). A DC¬†14 Strength (Athletics) check is also 
required to carefully move the door without scraping 
it against the stone walls.
If the PCs remain in the hallway for more than 
10 turns, have the PCs all make Dexterity (Stealth) 
checks. Then, roll a Wisdom (Perception) check for the 
Bugbear, using the lowest Dexterity (Stealth) check 
result as the DC.
If the PCs make a noise in the hall that a bugbear 
notices, the arguing coming from inside the room 
stops immediately. The bugbears take defensive 
positions behind makeshift cover and prepare to 
ambush the PCs as soon as one of the doors is 
pushed ajar.
If the PCs enter without being noticed, read the 
following.
Three furry goblinoids point and shout at one 
another, obviously engaged in a heated debate. The 
creatures are muscular and brutish, each standing 
about seven feet tall. Coarse hair covers their 
bodies and chipped and crooked fangs protrude 
from their snarling mouths. The largest spits as 
he screams at the smallest, who apparently isn‚Äôt 
backing down.
All around the room, debris and broken wood 
obscure the stone floor.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Three bugbears have made this room 
their refuge, but have been unable to leave for two 
weeks because of the dire wolves in Room B9. They 
are stir-crazy now and arguing with each other (in 
Common) about who cheated at a dice game that 
obviously isn‚Äôt being played.
If surprised, allow the middle bugbear a DC¬†16 
Wisdom (Perception) check to notice someone 
entering. The largest and smallest bugbears are 
automatically surprised if the PCs enter without 
making any noise.
Encounter Condition: [Ambush], [Cover], Echoes 3, 
Poor Footing 2
Tactics: If an encounter takes place in the room, the 
bugbears swarm the nearest PC, taking a defensive 
position until they have a handle on the situation. 
If the leader drops to zero hit points, flip a coin. 
Heads, the other two surrender. Tails, they become 

128
enraged (Barbarian rage feature, as if they were 
level 3s).
If the encounter takes place in the hall two 
bugbears engage the PCs, forcing them away from 
the entrance to the room, while the smallest runs 
around to the other side of the corridor, to wedge 
the PCs in.
Treasure: Hidden under the debris in this room is a 
small strongbox (Intelligence (Investigation) check, 
DC¬†18 to locate). The lock is simple and crude, but 
gummed up with grime, requiring a successful 
DC¬†20 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock, 
or DC¬†15 Strength (Athletics) check to smash the 
faulty mechanism and pry the box open. When the 
strongbox is opened, a thin wire running along the 
hinge pushes down, cracking a vial of acid hidden 
inside the box. The bugbears normally open the box 
slowly, preventing the glass from shattering. Allow 
the PC a Wisdom (Perception) check (DC¬†18). If they 
succeed, they hear metal scratching against glass 
and are allowed a DC¬†20 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
check to stop opening the box before rupturing the 
vial. If the PC makes no intimation that they are 
opening the box slowly, do not allow any checks.
If the vial cracks (which is automatic if the rolls 
fail or the PC is hurried), an alchemical reaction 
occurs and the acid inside, reacting with the 
surrounding air, becomes a fog that blankets a 5¬†ft. 
square in front of the strongbox. This lasts for 1 
minute and any creature starting their turn, ending 
their turn, or moving through the cloud receives 
2d6 acid damage.
Inside the chest are 46 sp, 24 gp, a dull pearl 
set into a gaudy necklace (25 gp), three healing 
potions, and a wand of light (spend an action to 
cast the light spell without any components, doing 
so costs 1 charge, wand is found with 2d12 charges 
remaining).
The largest bugbear keeps three keys on a ring 
on his belt. The first key goes to the strongbox 
in this room. The second is for the locked door 
leading to Room B12. The third is to the inside of 
the door in Room B9.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one bugbear. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one. These bugbears are considered the 
middle bugbear for the purposes of tactics and the 
encounter.
B11 . COLD IRON
The granite walls are dull and lifeless and the floor 
looks slick with ice. In the middle of the room are 
three pieces of iron, shaped like links in a chain. 
As you approach, the iron links shift position with 
an audible groan. They shudder and with a violent 
screech of metal on metal, finally settle.
If the links are left alone for longer than a minute 
they twist and shift of their own accord, their screech 
taking on an accusatory edge.
After the PCs step into the room, read the 
following.
The door slams behind you though the sound is 
well-masked by the iron links clattering in the room.
Attempts to catch the door require a DC¬†18 
Strength (Athletics) check to grab it and wrestle the 
door open. Any contact with the door before the 
puzzle is solved triggers a chill touch spell targeted at 
that creature (+7 to hit, 2d8 necrotic damage).
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Another of the puzzle traps placed by 
the celestials, this one is obviously a wrought iron 
riddle to be solved before the door will open.
The center of the three links holds the key to 
the door, but all three will lash out at any who 
approaches. Creatures ‚Äúattacked‚Äù by the links must 
succeed a Dexterity saving throw (DC¬†14) or take 
2d4 bludgeoning damage. The links will target the 
loudest creature in the room, straining to get at 
them even if they are out of reach, with no more 
than one link targeting someone at a time (the 
middle link is pulled around by the other two, and 
thus cannot lash out). The PCs must find a way to 
incapacitate, distract, or otherwise pacify the links 
to get the enchanted key that safely opens the door.
Encounter Condition: Extreme Cold, Fear 12
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the save DCs of the iron link by 5 and 
have it inflict 1d4 extra cold damage for each failed 
saving throw. To decrease the challenge of this 
encounter, decrease the trap DCs by 3 and reduce 
the chill touch effect to a 1st-level caster (+5 to hit, 
1d8 necrotic damage).

129
B12. SNAKE PIT
The southern door to this room is locked and 
requires a successful Dextertiy (Sleight of Hand) 
check (DC¬†19) to unlock. The door is locked.
The room is 20¬†feet wide, and 24 feet deep. A wide 
stone ledge is all you have to stand on, as the floor 
of the room drops off twenty feet into an unknown 
emptiness below. The floor writhes as dozens of 
snakes twist amongst sharpened metal spikes.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Having malfunctioned the last time this 
trap was sprung, it has not been reset. A DC¬†13 
Wisdom (Perception) check reveals the goblinoid 
skeletons scattered beneath the snakes. Unless the 
PCs can reset the trap, they are forced to maneuver 
their way around the edge of the ledge with a 
successful DC¬†17 Dexterity check.
On the south wall, the PCs see a small stone 
switch with a DC¬†13 Wisdom (Perception) check. If 
the PCs successfully strike the switch (AC 15) with a 
heavy blunt object (like a hammer) a small bridge 
springs out from the wall. Alternately, one PC can 
walk around and merely press the switch with a 
DC¬†8 Strength check. If the PCs entered from the 
south, then this is a no-brainer.
The bridge extends out at floor level and stops 
10¬†feet short of the ledge. A successful DC¬†12 
Strength (Athletics) check enables a PC to land 
on the bridge, but it cannot support more than 
one PC at a time. If a PC leaps onto the bridge 
with someone else standing on it, the bridge has 
a 50% chance of breaking, sending both PCs to 
the bottom of the pit. If a third PC jumps onto the 
bridge it automatically breaks.
PCs on the south side can attempt to repair 
the mechanism that drives the bridge, requiring a 
successful Intelligence (Investigation) and follow up 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check (Both DC¬†15) to 
salvage and replace the faulty gearing. Once fixed 
the bridge extends completely.
Failing the Dexterity check by more than 5 
causes a malfunction and retracts the bridge 5¬†ft.
Once fixed, the bridge extends all the way to 
the ledge and supports three PCs at a time. From 
here, they can shuffle along the ledge, requiring 
a DC¬†14 Dexterity check to reach the exit in the 
southeast corner of the room. Since the southern 
door is locked, a PC must succeed at a DC¬†16 
Dexterity check while trying to unlock the door. The 
mechanism is not overly complex, but the difficulty 
of trying to open the lock as well as maintaining 
balance makes the task difficult.
If the PCs try to pass one another on the 
ledge, everyone involved must succeed at a DC¬†15 
Dexterity check, +2 per PC. Failure on any balance 
check indicates the PC falls. Failure by more than 10 
means he takes someone else with him.
There is another, less obvious option, for getting 
across this room. five fee below the level of the 
floor, the PCs ‚Äì with a DC¬†14 Wisdom (Perception) 
check ‚Äì can discern a groove running along the wall 
of the room. Inside this groove is a 6-in.-thick floor 
that extends across the pit, if the PCs can disable 
the trigger to the trap.
The trigger is located to the left of the entryway, 
where the wall and floor would meet if the trap 
was set. The PCs can find it with a successful DC¬†22 
Wisdom (Perception) check. A DC¬†16 Dexterity 
check allows a PC to reach the trigger and two 
consecutive Dexterity (Thieves‚Äô Tools) are required 
to reset the trap (DC¬†14), and then disable it (DC¬†18). 
Once the floor is back in place, the PCs can walk 
across the room without fail.
If any PCs fall into the pit, their best course of 
action is to climb out. Since the walls are rough and 
provide handholds, the PCs can reach the ledge 
easily with a DC¬†14 Strength (Athletics) check.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: If any PCs fall into the pit, six snakes 
(medium vipers) attack each round. While there are 
dozens and dozens of snakes they do not have a 
true strategy and they tend to lash out blindly.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter 
increase Dexterity check DCs by +2 and add 20¬†ft, 
of depth to the fall. To decrease the challenge, 
decrease all Wisdom (Perception) DCs by -4.

130
B13 . WELL OF SLEEP
If the PCs approach from the hallway, read the 
following.
As you enter this chamber, you see four doors. In 
the southeast corner of the room is a silver door. 
Its shine nearly blinds you. In the southwest comer 
of the small antechamber stands a door of dark 
wood, stained with age. In the northwest corner is 
a simple stone door and in the northeast corner, a 
finely carved stone door catches your eye.
If the PCs entered from Room B8, read the 
following.
The stone door rises, awaiting your entry. As you 
enter the room, the stone door lowers behind you, 
gracefully.
Once the PCs open the door to Room B13, read the 
following.
The room is built with polished stone. The yellow 
hue is as clean as it is even. A simple wooden 
frame hangs above the well, and a frayed rope 
descends into the inky blackness below. Echoes rise 
from the pit, as you hear scurrying noises and a 
splash of water.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: This room is an enigma. What the 
celestials intended for it is known only to its creator, 
who is dead. It is now the home of a few vermin 
who climb up and down the wall of the pit. From 
time to time the goblins come here as well, hoping 
to catch something to play with.
If the PCs touch the rope, an alarm spell sounds, 
alerting the goblins that someone is here. Allow 
the goblin fighters in Room B70 a DC¬†14 Wisdom 
(Perception) check. If successful, they come running 
to the commotion in 8d4 seconds, expecting to find 
bugs and rats.
Encounter Condition: [Ambush], Stagnant Air
Tactics: The goblins swarm into the room expecting 
trouble, but instead find the PCs. The goblins suffer 
a -4 penalty to their initiative rolls for 1d4 minutes. 
The goblins gang up in pairs, however, and if any 
PC poses the largest threat, the goblins send their 
‚Äúextras‚Äù to deal with them.
When the goblins are dispatched the PCs are 
free to gather water from the well to replenish their 
stores, but it needs to be purified before it can be 
safely drunk. If the PCs imbibe the water before 
purifying it they must succeed a Constitution 
saving throw (DC¬†16) or have their maximum hit 
points reduced by 3d4 until their next long rest.
The secret door leading to Room B8 cannot be 
opened from this side.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
have the alarm sound when one of the doors is 
opened. To decrease the challenge, the alarm only 
sounds if the rope is pulled.
B14 . OBELISK OF SHAPES
As you enter this chamber, you encounter four 
doors. In the southeast corner of the room is a 
silver door, polished to a nearly blinding shine. In 
the southwest corner of the small antechamber 
stands a dark wood door, stained with age. In the 
northwest corner is a simple stone door, and in the 
northeast corner a finely carved stone door is the 
last to catch your eye.
Once the PCs open the door to Room B14, read the 
following.
The walls of this room are a dull gray granite. The 
floor and ceiling are granite as well, but are highly 
polished. An obsidian obelisk dominates the center 
of the room. Carved into the obelisk are various 
shaped holes‚Äîcircles, squares, and triangles 
among many others. In a swarm around it spin 
trinkets of varying shapes.
After the PCs step into the room, read the 
following.
The doors to the room slam shut as the shapes on 
the obelisk grind to a halt.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Similar to Room B6, this trap keeps 
the PCs in the room until it is reset. The puzzle is 
simple, meant to test the most basic of problem-
solving skills. Each hole on the obelisk has a shape 
that corresponds with it. Once it is filled the doors 
spring open.

131
Feel free to describe the puzzle in as agonizing 
detail as you like. Lead the players on with the 
depth and complexity of the strangely shaped 
necklaces and baubles that float around.
If someone wants to, they may perform whatever 
checks they deem fit for divining the nature of this 
obelisk. In case someone happens to roll higher than 
a 15 on an Wisdom (Insight) check, clue them in 
on the fact that there are an equal number of holes 
to objects.
The objects themselves are not magical, just 
held aloft with weak enchantments. The obelisk 
itself is not enchanted, instead hiding minuscule 
mechanical switches inside each slot that the 
correct object actuates.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: It is not recommended to increase the 
challenge of this encounter. It is a simple puzzle 
meant to foil creatures with animalistic minds. To 
decrease the challenge, merely have the door open 
after 24 hours.
B15 . BLINK DOG DEN
The stone door in the southeastern corner is jammed, 
requiring a successful DC¬†14 Dexterity (Sleight of 
Hand) check to unstick, followed by a successful DC¬†9 
Strenght (Athletics Check).
Musty odors permeate the air here. The floor is 
littered with bones and scraps of cloth. Near the 
southwestern corner, in front of a large stone door, 
are the bodies of three hounds and a few goblins. 
Broken spears and ruined shields are strewn about 
the floor here as well. In the northeastern corner of 
the room is yet another stone door. This area is free 
of detritus.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: One of many rooms that have been 
taken over as a den by the blink dogs, it was 
recently sacked by a goblin war party. Aside from 
the remains of the battle, there is little of note in 
this room.
Encounter Condition: Echoes 4, Distracting Visions
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: Amidst the debris, the PCs can find two 
wolf teeth, a very small, jagged gold tooth (from a 
goblin), and a severed, desiccated hand.
Scaling: N/A
B16 . HALL OF THE DIVINE
Constructed of blinding white marble walls, 
and highly polished black granite, this room‚Äôs 
southeastern corner is a mess of gears and pulleys. 
The marble wall has been smashed open and the 
innards of a complex trap spill out of it. A huge 
statue of a ferocious angel (obviously female) 
wielding an ornate spear, dominates the wall. The 
statue is masterfully crafted, it‚Äôs almost lifelike 
and the spear is real, placed into the right hand of 
the statue.
If the PCs examine the statue, read the following.
At the base of the statue is a plaque that reads, ‚ÄúI 
shall defend this prison against all manner of evil. 
I shall die to protect this world from the horrors of 
the abyss. I shall never waiver. I shall never stop 
my quest to liberate the world from the taint of 
chaos. I shall never concede defeat.‚Äù
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Ages ago, when the bugbears were far 
more prominent, they defended this room against 
intruders, considering the beautiful statue a herald 
of what was to come. Little did they know, the 
angel was actually buried in the room, her remains 
used to build the foundation of a shrine to their 
greatest warrior. When any PCs step within 5¬†ft. of 
the statue, they must succeed a Wisdom saving 
throw (DC¬†12) or be frightened of the statue for 24 
hours, followed by the summoning of two lantern 
archons, coming out of the eyes of the statue.
They immediately determine the alignment of 
the PCs. Either use the listed alignments on their 
character sheets, or judge for yourself what the 
party‚Äôs alignment predominantly leans towards. 
If they are deemed to have strayed too far from 
‚Äúlawful‚Äù or ‚Äúgood‚Äù then the archons summon a 
blink dog to defend the room.
Encounter Condition: Fear 14, Positive Energy
Tactics: The lantern archons are mindless drones, 
created by the spirit of the angel who died here. 

132
The blink dogs are also made of the same celestial 
energy and attack mindlessly. They attack evil PCs 
first, followed by chaotic neutral, neutral, and finally 
chaotic good PCs (of questionable character).
Lawful good, lawful neutral, and neutral good 
PCs cannot harm these creatures. Conversely, 
lawful good PCs are immune to the frightened 
condition in this room. If any PC moves toward 
the statue or touches the spear, the blink dog and 
lantern archons attack them, ignoring alignment.
If the creatures in this room are killed, they fade 
like mist. If you would like, consider any paladin, 
no matter their chosen alignment, to be ‚Äúlawful‚Äù 
alignment given their staunch adherence to their 
oath. An oath-breaker would be exempt for... 
obvious reasons. In fact the archons may judge an 
oath-breaker quite harshly.
Treasure: The statue is armed with a +1 ‚Äúaxiomatic‚Äù 
spear. Lawful good PCs can collect it, if they recite 
the sacred oath written at the bottom of the status. 
Should the PC ever fail in this oath, the spear 
disintegrates.
When rolling damage for an axiomatic item, if 
the target is of any chaotic alignment, remove an 
additional 1d4 hit points from that creature. Non-
lawful good PCs touching an axiomatic item suffer 
2d6 lightning damage per turn spent in contact.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
the lantern archons are summoned as soon as the 
PCs enter the room. To decrease the challenge, 
allow any PCs to fight the lantern archons and blink 
dog, but lose their immunity to the frightened 
condition.
B17. TRAPPED BLINK DOGS
As you open the door to this room, a sense of 
unease comes over you. The room is plain and 
square. It is dark, though your torches cut through 
the gloom easily enough. A musky scent wafts 
through the air, and you get the distinct impression 
you are not the only one in this room.
If the PCs enter without being noticed, read this:
Three yellow-brown dogs, nearly identical to the 
corpses in the other room, lie on the floor sleeping 
lazily., They haven‚Äôt noticed you yet, but something 
is unnerving them. The dogs shiver quietly with 
fear, whining softly from time to time.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Three blink dogs were driven into this 
room by a goblin scouting party a few weeks ago. 
The room‚Äôs Aura of Fear has them trapped.
 '
Aura of Fear. Creatures within the room must 
succeed on a DC¬†14 Wisdom saving throw every 
turn or be frightened of everything outside 
of the room.
If the dogs notice the PCs they immediately 
attack, taking out their frustrations on the party. 
If the party lingers in the doorway, the blink dogs 
have advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks to 
spot them. If the PCs make enough noise in B15 to 
draw their attention the dogs investigate. Should 
the PCs be spotted then, the blink dogs attack, 
mistaking the PCs for those who trapped them in 
the first place.
If killed, the blink dogs fade like mist.
Encounter Condition: Ambush, Fear 16
Tactics: The blink dogs launch themselves at the PCs 
indiscriminately. Where they would normally attack 
the PCs individually‚Äîconcentrating their attacks‚Äî
they lash out at the closest PC. Because of the 
nature of the dungeon, their blink ability is sporadic 
and has a 70% chance of failing. If successful, 
however, they flank the hapless PC. Blink dogs are 
lawful good creatures, and thus are easier to reason 
with using animal handling. If the PCs calm the 
blink dogs, the blink dogs leave the room, but do 
not become companions to the PCs. This ordeal 
has left them a little confused and they move on 
through the dungeon without much direction. If 
the PCs follow, the blink dogs investigate Room B14 
briefly, and then make their way through the rest of 
the Section.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one blink dog. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one.

133
B18 . ROOM OF FIRE
The door to this room is locked, requiring a successful 
DC¬†25 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. 
When a PC opens the door they are hit with a wave of 
heat that deals 1d2 points of fire damage. After that, 
the Extreme Heat condition takes effect if the PCs 
enter the room.
This room is hot, close to oppressively so. The walls 
are constructed of granite with large scorch marks 
and stains. The corners contain small piles of ash. 
Against the northern wall, a simple pedestal rests, 
with a scroll case on top.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The oppressive heat is a design of 
the room and should be an indication of the 
inhospitable conditions. While there is no illusion, 
detect magic reveals faint illusion magic on the 
walls and pedestal. This is meant to distract visitors 
and the GM should play up the illusion‚Äôs design 
with vague answers to the PC‚Äôs questions. Keep 
them in the room as long as possible, examining 
every corner.
With 1d6 minutes of examinations and a 
successful DC¬†20 Intelligence (Arcana) check reveal 
that no illusion actually exists and the heat is real.
Encounter Condition: Extreme Heat
Tactics: The scroll case is the only thing of interest in 
this room and touching it triggers a fireball trap that 
engulfs the room.
 '
Fireball Trap. When the cap of the scroll case is 
placed upon any surface other than the case itself 
it casts a fireball spell at 3rd level at its location, 
with a spell save DC of 14. Should the trap trigger, 
the scroll case is destroyed, along with the trap, 
and scroll if its still inside. A successful Intelligence 
(Arcana) check (DC¬†16) reveals the fireball spell‚Äôs 
runes etched into the cap‚Äôs rim. This trap may be 
disarmed by casting dispel magic on the scroll cap. 
Should the PCs succeed the Intelligence (Arcana)
check by a substantial amount you may opt to reveal 
the exact nature of the trigger, and that the trap and 
case might be saved for later use.
Seventy-two hours after being triggered and 
disintegrating the scroll case manifests again in the 
room, armed, and with a fresh fire trap scroll inside.
Treasure: Coincidentally, the scroll inside the case 
contains a stronger version of this rooms trap, a 
scroll of fire trap.
Fire trap is a variant of the alarm spell, with the 
twist that triggering the associated alarm casts 
the fireball spell at 3rd level at its location, with a 
spell save DC of 14. It requires a successful DC¬†16 
Wisdom (Perception) check to spot. Succeeding 
a DC¬†14 Intelligence (Arcana) check reveals the 
magical phrase to disable the fire trap for 5 
minutes. When spoken within earshot, the alarm‚Äôs 
trigger cannot activate for that time. Once triggered 
the trap cannot cast fireball again.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter,
