change the trap and scroll to cast flame strike. To 
decrease the challenge of this encounter, change 
the trap and scroll to cast burning hands.
B19 . ROOM OF ROT
The door to this room is locked, requiring a 
successful DC¬†25 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check 
to unlock. When a PC opens the door they are hit 
with a stench of decay that requires succeeding a 
DC¬†12 Constitution saving throw, lest the PC become 
poisoned. After that, the Stagnant Air condition takes 
effect if the PCs enter the room.
This room reeks of decay. The smell is 
overpowering, practically debilitating and the room 
is cramped. The stone walls are covered in decaying 
moss and dark stains. Across from the door, a 
pedestal stands with an ornate scroll case on it. 
As enticing as the scroll case may seem, the stench 
threatens to completely overwhelm you.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Like Room B18, this room suffers from 
an unexplained odor that chokes the PCs as they 
enter. The stench is actually a design of the room 
(or a malfunction of the magical wards), not residue 
from the trap located on the pedestal. It would be 
easy to say this room is an anomaly, but this entire 
Region plays upon the experimental traps to the 
point that nothing should shock the PCs.
Encounter Condition: Stagnant Air
Tactics: Aside from the Stagnant Air, the PCs also 
have to deal with a trap if they wish to remove the 
scroll case from the room.

134
 '
Noxious Vapor Trap. The scroll case has two caps, 
one on each end. Of the two, one spins freely, as 
if it wants to be opened, popping off easily and 
triggering the trap. The other produces a grinding 
sound when spun and can be depressed as well 
as pulled off. PCs that succeed a DC¬†10 Wisdom 
(Perception) check hear a soft click when pressing 
down on this cap.
If this cap is depressed while opening the other 
the trap is disarmed permanently. Opening from 
this end still triggers the trap.
Removing the case from the room without 
disarming the trap triggers a noxious vapor that 
floods the room, poisoning any PCs inside that 
fail a DC¬†15 Constitution saving throw. Once 
triggered the scroll case melts into a puddle of goo, 
ruining the scroll if it is still inside. After 72 hours 
have passed since it was triggered the scroll case 
manifests once more on its pedestal, loaded with a 
new scroll.
Treasure: The scroll case contains a scroll of 
stinking cloud.
B20 . LIMESTONE CAVERN
As the PCs approach this room, they can see water 
making out from under the door. The door to this 
room is locked, requiring a successful DC¬†25 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check to unlock.
The entire floor of the room is submerged. Looking 
about, you notice the lack of construction here. The 
walls are unfinished limestone and stalactites hang 
from the ceiling. Droplets of water fall from the 
high ceiling, and the walls are slick. Almost floating 
on the water, resting on a stone, is a gem set into 
the wall, pulsating with a bright-yellow glow.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The entire floor of this room is sunken 
and filled with 4¬†ft. of water, which is icy cold. A 6 
in. lip runs the course of the room, but standing or 
walking on it requires a successful DC¬†15 Dexterity 
(Acrobatics) or Strength (Athletics) check or the PC 
falls into the water. Falling into the water causes 
no damage, but it is extremely cold. Light does not 
penetrate the water either, but cupping it into one‚Äôs 
hand reveals that it is crystal clear. The bottom is 
uneven and rocky, making it difficult to cross easily.
Encounter Condition: [Extreme Cold], Flooded, 
Hazardous Footing 15
Tactics: Touching the jewel casts lightning bolt at 3rd 
level towards the PC. Due to the flooded condition 
of the room, the Dexterity save DC is 16. This 
happens only once, and dispel magic will remove the 
hostile enchantment without harming the item.
Treasure: The gem is a beautifully cut diamond, 
worth about 2,000 gp. While it does not radiate 
magic it grants resistance to cold damage, so long 
as the gem is held tightly in one‚Äôs hand. It can be 
safely removed once the trap is disabled.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
change the lightning bolt spell to chain lightning. To 
decrease the challenge, reduce the DC of Dexterity  
save of the lightning bolt trap by 4.
B21 . COLUMNS
The door to this room is locked, requiring a 
successful DC¬†25 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check 
to unlock.
Stone columns run from floor to ceiling. The 
columns are carved with symbols from an ancient 
language you can‚Äôt quite discern, as well as graffiti 
left behind by the vagabond goblinoid races. The 
rapid scrawling of goblins and the heavier script of 
bugbears can be easily discerned. The columns in 
the back of the room are in better condition than 
the ones closest to the door. The floor of the room 
is littered with debris and small rocks.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The carvings on the columns depict 
the story of how the Region was built from the 
perspective of a scholar. It is a signature (of sorts) by 
one of the celestial designers. The graffiti covering 
the columns was created by the goblins and 
bugbears, and in a way details their history, though 
it is difficult to read as they often overlap and 
obscure each other. To ensure the room remained 
a testament to their work, the celestial incorporated 
a trap into the columns. Apparently, the goblinoids 
have not been deterred from spoiling the unique 
architecture of the columns, trap or no. The PCs 
may freely examine the columns, so long as they do 
not touch them. Once a column is touched the trap 
triggers and the columns collapse on the PCs. The 
trap resets once the room is void of life.
 '
Collapsing Columns. While appearing steady, the 
columns are packed with magic and ready to fall at 
any moment. Any touch of a living creature triggers 

135
their descent. Creatures within 5¬†ft, including the 
offending creature, must succeed a DC¬†15 Dexterity 
saving throw or be struck by the stonework 
launched at them. Creatures that fail their save 
receive 4d8 bludgeoning damage.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: If the PCs spend 30 minutes searching the 
debris in this room, allow each of them a DC¬†17 
Intelligence (Investigation) check to find one of the 
following: 24 copper coins in a brown leather bag, a 
gold ring that radiates illusion magic but produces 
no effect, a masterwork silver dagger, a pair of 
rusted kukri, or a scroll of mending. Once all four 
items are found all the PCs find are pieces of wood, 
bone fragments, stones, and fungus.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
have a wall of the room collapse inward instead, 
striking all creatures within 10¬†ft. of that wall. To 
decrease the challenge, have the column instead 
drop a large brick from the ceiling, only striking the 
triggering creature.
B22 . DIRE WOLF DEN
This room is dark, so dark in fact that your torches 
cannot pierce the gloom. The few things you can 
makeout are merely shadows dancing in the corner. 
The smell of decay fills the air.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: The PCs have stumbled into another 
dire wolf den. Four dire wolves are on edge 
due to recent goblin raids, and are prepared for 
any intruders that enter their den. The wolves 
gain advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks, 
attacking the PCs on sight.
Encounter Condition: Ambush, Deep 
Darkness, Fearless
Tactics: The wolves use pack tactics, swarming 
over one PC at a time. They do not target any PC 
specifically, attacking whichever is most accessible. 
Two wolves attempt to flank the target, while the 
others assault the PC directly. Attempts to sway 
the animals through Animal Handling are done at 
disadvantage.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add two dire wolves. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one dire wolf.
B23 . THE PIT
A deep, circular pit dominates the center of this 
room. Leaning over it, you can see nothing but 
darkness down the treacherous well. The corpse 
of a bugbear lies against the northern wall, a 
gleaming battleaxe clutched loosely in its hand. In 
the other corner of the room, sunk halfway through 
the floor, is a sword. The echo of the wind gushing 
through the pit makes an ominous sound as you 
move cautiously about the room.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: There are two pits in this room. The first 
is obvious. The second is located directly behind 
the sword; it has become lodged between the two 
sections of the trap‚Äôs door. Unless they disable 
the trap first, any PC that steps within 10¬†ft. of the 
sword triggers the trap and they fall down into 
the 20-ft-deep pit. A successful DC¬†17 Dexterity 
(Acrobatics) or Strength (Athletics) check is required 
by any PCs who fall down the pit to escape from it.
PCs that roll higher than a 14 on Wisdom 
(Perception) checks in this room notice seams 
in the floor that a slight breeze wafts through. 
Disabling the hidden pit trap requires sabotaging 
the seams around the edge of it, performed by 
succeeding a DC¬†12 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
check with the right tools.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: The axe the corpse of the bugbear is a +1 
greataxe that always glows with a 5¬†ft. radius of dim 
light. No effort, physical or magical, succeeds in 
snuffing the light. If the PCs manage to recover the 
sword, it is a bastard sword, with the name Urthieln 
engraved in the blade (in Celestial runes).
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the depth of the hidden pit trap to 30¬†ft. 
To decrease the challenge, lower the DC of the 
climb by -4.

136
B24 . BLOCKED HALL
You see a collapsed door in the distance. It 
appears as if a large stone block fell from the 
ceiling and utterly crushed it. The ceiling, however, 
looks complete and lacks any distinguishing 
characteristics. The hallway branches both east and 
west in front of the door.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The PCs are near one of the celestials‚Äô 
observatories. In order to safeguard their private 
enclosure, the celestials installed a trap here. The 
trap only has one activation left and the goblins 
know to avoid it, having seen its devastating effect 
before. The eastern branch of the corridor leads 
to Room B22. The western branch terminates at 
a blank wall. A DC¬†19 Intelligence (Investigation) 
check reveals a small (3 in. diameter, 3 in. deep) hole 
in the wall (part of a secret door leading to Room 
B25) 4¬†ft. from the floor.
 '
Falling Block Trap. When the PCs enter this room 
have them roll a Wisdom (Perception) check. 
Anyone who rolls higher than an 8 notices 
primitive markings across the various tiles that 
make up the floor. PCs that roll higher than a 
14, or possess knowledge of goblinoid customs, 
find a pattern amongst them. It is spaced evenly 
enough to be walked by small folk. Straying from 
this path triggers the trap. If the PCs do not find 
the path, each roll 1d6. On a roll of 1-4 they have 
triggered the trap. Triggering the trap causes a 
huge block to fall from the ceiling, crushing any 
PCs who fail a DC¬†15 Dexterity saving throw for 6d4 
bludgeoning damage.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The secret door can only be opened by 
placing a dowel or iron rod into the hole in the 
wall and lifting up. No Strength check is required. 
Without a handle to lift, the PCs must succeed at 
a DC¬†18 Strength (Athletics) check to lift the secret 
door open.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the damage of the falling block trap to 6d6. 
To decrease the challenge, lower the damage to 6d3.
B25 . OBSERVATORY
The secret door leading to this room can only be 
opened by placing a 3-in.-diameter dowel or iron 
rod into a hole in the wall 4¬†ft. high and lifting. No 
Strength check is required. Without a handle to lift, 
the PCs must succeed at a DC¬†18 Strength (Athletics) 
check to lift the secret door open.
A few nondescript wooden benches are in the 
room. On the back wall a large map hangs limply. It 
looks old, though it is in good repair. The map details 
the layout of this entire section of the dungeon. 
There is a simple stone door to the south.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room was used as an observatory 
by the celestials. Aside from the map (see treasure 
below), it contains nothing of much interest or 
value. The air in the room is dry and fire spreads 
easily, consuming the benches and map within 
minutes if the fire cannot be extinguished. The 
door to the south leads to Room B26. It is locked, 
requiring a successful Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
(DC¬†16) to pick. The doorknob is covered in a thin, 
almost imperceptible, layer of contact poison. It 
must be dealt with if the PCs wish to open the door.
 '
Contact Poison. Touching the poison causes near-
instantaneous burning and vicious nausea. The 
victim loses 1d6 hit points immediately, and must 
succeed a DC¬†10 Constitution saving throw or lose 
another 2d6 hit points every 10 hours until their 
next long rest.
Encounter Condition: Echoes 4
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: The map on the back wall is a duplicate 
of Map B. It can assist the PCs in navigating the 
dungeon. It is quite old, and easily catches fire if 
the PCs are not careful. It is also large, measuring 
10-ft-by-10-ft The map does not show the location 
of secret doors, but it does show the location of 
every room in the dungeon. It is unlabeled.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
raise the DC of the Constitution save of the trap by 
5. To decrease the challenge, reduce the poison‚Äôs 
recurring damage to 1d6.

137
B26. OBSERVATORY LIBRARY
As you enter the room you notice it is similar to one 
of the rooms near the dungeon‚Äôs entrance. Along the 
back wall is a stone desk and chair, and a bookcase 
covers the eastern wall. In this room, however, the 
bookcase holds a number of tomes, not just one or 
two. A sheaf of papers lies on the desk, and the light 
glints off of something metallic under the chair.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The room is essentially a mirror of 
Room B3. The anteroom (Room B25) served as an 
observation post for the celestials, while this room 
was used to catalog their findings. The catalogued 
observations are stored on the bookshelf, written on 
ancient parchment. Not wishing for their records 
to fall into the wrong hands, this room was trapped 
by the celestial observers. The shiny object under 
the chair, which appears to be a silver brooch, is the 
trigger for a fire trap (see Room B18). Any attempt to 
move the broach triggers the trap, which destroys 
every book in the room beyond any hope of repair; 
the flames easily consume the ancient pages. The 
trap is also triggered if the PCs attempt to remove 
any of the books from the room without first 
disabling the trap.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: If the PCs do not trigger the trap, they are 
free to take as many books with them as they can 
carry. The books, and the sheaves of paper on the 
desk, chronicle events of the devils over centuries, 
though no specific dates are given. To understand 
the writing, a PC must speak Celestial and succeed 
a DC¬†20 Intelligence (Investigation check). The PCs 
are free to take the silver broach, which is worth 
approximately 100 gp, once the trap is disabled. If 
the trap is triggered, the broach is destroyed in the 
ensuing flames.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
change the fire trap to cast flame strike at 6th level. 
To decrease the challenge, change the fire trap to 
cast burning hands at 2nd level.
B27. HALL OF VINES
This room is covered in vines, lending it an earthy 
smell. Beneath the plants, you can barely make out 
a series of strange stones. The room is separated 
into three square sections and a layer of ash 
blankets the granite floor tiles. In the center is a thin 
pedestal with a bright gem affixed to it. The pedestal 
has strange sigils carved into its base, though they 
appear worn down and cannot be clearly read. The 
only apparent exit is the door you entered through.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The sigils under the vines, and on the 
pedestal, are glyphs of warding (3rd level, explosive, 
acid). If the PCs touch any wall, or the gem on the 
pedestal, the ward triggers, which withers the vines 
and ivy that have accumulated in the room over 
time. Each wall has its own ward, and each must be 
disabled individually to investigate the sigils.
Encounter Condition: [Safe]
Tactics: There is a secret door in the southwestern 
corner of the room that leads to a corridor which 
leads to Room B29. A successful DC¬†25 Intelligence 
(Investigation) check reveals a small, rough ‚Äúbutton‚Äù 
that blends in with the stone. However, a DC¬†25 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check dislodges the 
button from the surrounding moss and vines, 
without damaging the mechanism or triggering the 
glyph. Once the button is depressed, the wall slides 
down and into the floor, which also deactivates 
the glyphs for 6d10 seconds before the secret door 
closes again, and the traps reset.
Without the button, disabling any glyph of 
warding here requires a successful Arcana (DC¬†15) 
check, or just triggering them. The resulting acid-
blast only harms the vines... and the PCs who 
bumble into them.
Treasure: Once the trap on the pedestal is disabled, 
the PCs can remove the gem. It is a small sapphire 
worth approximately 600 gp. A PC spending an hour 
deciphering the sigils on the wall is rewarded a spell 
(that can be transcribed into a spellbook) if they 
succeed a DC¬†23 Intelligence (Arcana) check. The 
GM should choose an appropriate 3rd-level spell the 
PCs are lacking.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the damage of the glyph of warding trap 
to 7d8 acid. To decrease the challenge, lower the 
damage to 4d8 acid

138
B28 . EXCAVATED ROOM
The walls of this room are heavily damaged. Large 
sections of masonry are scattered all over the floor, 
and a few blunt pickaxes are left in the rubble. The 
room is musty and uninviting. 
If the PCs have not killed Bartleby the Halfling, read 
the following:
From the northwestern corner of the room you hear 
grunts and scratching. As you get closer the noises 
stop and the raspy, uninviting voice yells out, ‚ÄúGit 
outta here! This is my claim!‚Äù
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: Bartleby the Halfling has taken up 
residence in this room. If the PCs have encountered 
him previously, his attitude is Indifferent, though 
he is gruff and suspicious. He presumes the PCs are 
following him, hoping to find the treasure he seeks 
before he can. If the PCs have not encountered 
Bartleby before, he questions them intently, trying 
to determine their purpose in the dungeon. He 
is elusive with his answers, and does not give his 
purpose away. If the PCs do not attack Bartleby, he 
claims the room is empty and has no more secrets 
to be uncovered and leaves, heading towards Room 
B38. He wants nothing to do with the PCs and 
offers no assistance nor accepts any in return. Once 
Bartleby leaves the room, or has been killed, the 
PCs can investigate further. Bartleby has destroyed 
the surface of the walls. The innards of a trap can 
be seen in the northern wall, but it is obvious that 
Bartleby has ruined it beyond repair. A successful 
DC¬†23 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check reveals the 
trap was once a fire trap (Room B18), but otherwise 
it is unidentifiable. On the southern wall is a 
secret door that leads to Room B29. It is difficult 
to spot, requiring a successful DC¬†19 Intelligence 
(Investigation) check to find. Like the secret door 
in Room B27, a simple button lowers the door into 
the floor for 2d6 rounds, during which time the trap 
that used to be in this room would be disarmed. 
Despite the damage to the wall, the secret door 
opens easily.
Encounter Condition: Ambush, Concealment, Cover
Tactics: Bartleby attempts to scare off the PCs. 
He uses alchemical substances to distract them, 
such as acid, alchemical fire, and thunderstones 
(thrown weapons, dexterity to hit, deals 3d4 acid/
fire/thunder damage to creatures within 5¬†ft. of 
the target if it hits. DC¬†12 Dexterity saving throw 
halves the damage). If he cannot drive them from 
the room he flees deeper into the dungeon. Once 
in the dungeon, he heads towards Room B38. He 
knows the dungeon far better than the PCs and 
easily loses them once free of the room. Feel free to 
play this out, however, with Bartleby heading into 
trapped rooms and sneaking through secret doors.
Treasure: Bartleby keeps a bedroll, a small lamp, and 
a few pots and pans. However, any belongings of 
value are on his person.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter 
use the improved versions of Bartleby‚Äôs rogue 
abilities listed under ‚ÄúDifficulty Increase.‚Äù In 
addition, you may have Bartleby throw his 
alchemical weapons as a bonus action if you‚Äôd like.
B29 . THE ROOM OF WANDS
This room‚Äôs walls are covered with wands. Each one 
looks masterfully crafted. You can‚Äôt see any hooks, 
so magic must be holding the wands to the walls. 
The walls behind the wands are covered with thick, 
green moss. The floor and ceiling are free of the 
moss, and are polished blue marble.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Another in a series of maddening traps 
designed by the celestials, this room only has one 
useful wand: a wand of burning hands. The rest of 
the wands, while nicely crafted, are simple wooden 
decoys with an illusory magic aura. If the PCs cast 
detect magic, everything in the room radiates magic 
and every school of magic is present. PCs who roll 
higher than a 15 on Intelligence (Arcana) checks 
made to study the wands see through the illusory 
magic schools, and discern the wands to be all 
illusion magic. This reveals nothing further about 
them, just that the schools of magic they were 
enchanted with were fake. PCs that touch these 
fake wands who have proven themselves sufficiently 
chaotic or evil (or who bear those alignments if you 
prefer) have bestow curse (spell save DC¬†14) cast on 
them at 3rd level, choosing a random ability score 
to curse, and lasting for 24 hours.
The true wand is basically impossible to find 
amongst the multitude without testing each one. 
It is up to your discretion for how to handle that. 
Sufficiently stubborn PCs could brute force the 

139
hundreds of wands to find it. If a PC can see magic, 
and succeeds at a DC¬†15 (21 if they have yet to 
properly discern their spell schools) Intelligence 
(Investigation) check they find the odd one out.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The northern wall contains a secret door that 
leads to Room B28. A Wisdom (Perception) check 
rolls of 17 or greater within the room reveal the well 
hidden door. It is unlocked and opens easily.
Treasure: The PC can retrieve one wand of burning 
hands. It has 1 charge and casts at 3rd level.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
allow PCs to trigger the curse regardless of 
alignment. To decrease the challenge, change the 
bestow curse to bane. The duration and spell save DC 
remain the same.
B30 . GOBLINOID REMAINS
The moment you enter this room you find the 
remains of seven goblins and three bugbears 
littering the floor. From what you can discern, two 
scouting parties encountered each other here and 
laid waste to one another. Broken clubs and spears 
are strewn amongst the corpses and the scent 
of death hangs heady in the air. A bone-chilling 
screech suddenly echoes throughout the halls. 
Something is heading your way.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: The scent of death has attracted two 
vargouilles to this room. Roll for initiative, the PCs 
have 24 seconds before they arrive. The PCs can 
choose to lay in wait for the vargouilles or they can 
flee. When the vargouilles arrive they notice PCs 
who are not hiding instantly. They attack the PCs on 
sight, hoping to add to the pile of corpses already 
in the room.
Encounter Condition: Cover
Tactics: The vargouilles assault the PCs with 
diving attacks. They rely heavily on their shriek 
attack, which can paralyze the PCs. They attack 
any paralyzed PCs, using their poison and kiss 
attacks on them.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one vargouille. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one vargouille.
B31 . THE ROD IN THE ROCK
A squat stalagmite sits in the center of this coarsely 
carved room. The atmosphere is dank, but not 
overwhelming like some of the other rooms in the 
dungeon. Protruding straight up from the center of 
the stalagmite is a carved staff of dark stained oak. 
The top of the staff is fitted with a gleaming steel 
cap in the shape of an eagle claw.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: A quarterstaff is buried in the stalagmite, 
and it serves as the trigger to the room‚Äôs trap. 
Pulling the staff before the trap is disarmed triggers 
it, flooding the room with darts that shoot from 
recesses in the wall.
If the PCs disarm the trap, they can attempt 
to remove the quarterstaff; a DC¬†20 Strength 
(Athletics) check is required to free the quarterstaff 
from its prison. If the PC performing the check 
has proficiency in Animal Handling, they gain 
advantage on the check.
 '
Spring-loaded Darts. When the staff is fully removed 
from the pedestal a spray of darts snap across the 
room. Starting from the east wall any creature not 
completely obscured by another must succeed a 
Dexterity (DC¬†13) saving throw or take 2d8 piercing 
damage and be poisoned until their next long rest.
The trap-holes can be found with a DC¬†16 
Intelligence (Investigation) check, and disabled with 
a DC¬†16 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand). Undoing this 
mechanism leaves the darts open for the taking. 
The first time a dart deals damage it loses its 
poison and poisons the damaged creature if they 
fail a DC¬†14 Constitution save.
Encounter Condition: [Safe]
Tactics: The only door to this room is a secret door 
that closes 2d6 rounds after it opens. Opening 
the door from this side requires a DC¬†23 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. This DC increases 
by +5 if the PCs triggered the trap.
Treasure: The staff is indeed magical. A PC that 
retrieves it is the proud owner of a +1 defending 
quarterstaff. Defending items grant +1 AC to their 
wielder while they aren‚Äôt wearing armor.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
replace the dart trap‚Äôs poison with exhaustion. To 
decrease the challenge, reduce the DC for finding 
the trap by -4.

140
B32 . BLINK DOG DEN
As soon as you step into the room you are met 
with a chorus of growls. Four golden dogs, fangs 
bared, stare at you. You have obviously intruded 
upon their home, and you are not welcome here. 
Curiously, they make no move to attack you, as 
they wait for you to exit on your own.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: The PCs have entered another blink dog 
den. The blink dogs (hit points 35, 31, 28, 23) do 
not appreciate the PCs‚Äô presence and want them 
out of the room. They bare their fangs and growl 
at the PCs. However, due to their nature, the blink 
dogs do not attack the PCs; they only wish to scare 
them away. If the PCs make no move to leave, the 
blink dogs slowly advance on the PCs, hoping to 
drive them off. If any PCs attack the dogs, they 
immediately retaliate. Successful Wisdom (Animal 
Handling) (DC¬†14) checks calm the dogs for 2d6 
minutes. Success also allows the PCs to remain and 
investigate the room, though the blink dogs are 
obviously not happy with the PCs‚Äô presence. Failure 
of this check changes the blink dog‚Äôs attitude to 
Hostile; they do not like being manipulated. There 
is a secret door on the west wall, leading to Room 
B31. A successful DC¬†18 Intelligence (Investigation) 
check reveals a hollow stone that can be pried open 
with a successful DC¬†18 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
check. Once the hallowed stone is open, the PCs 
can see a lever that must be turned 90 degrees 
clockwise.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: If attacked, the blink dogs launch themselves 
at the PCs, focusing on the most aggressive PCs 
first (or in the case of a PC failing a Wisdom 
(Animal Handling) check, they are focused first). 
They concentrate their attacks, targeting one PC at 
a time. They use their blink ability to flank the PCs. 
Because of the nature of the dungeon, their blink 
ability is sporadic and has a 70% chance of failing. If 
successful, however, they flank the hapless PC.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one blink dog. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one blink dog.

141
B33 . BUGBEAR STORE ROOM
This is a simple granite room. Along the northern 
wall is a plain rack, covered with spears and a few 
clubs. The weapons are too large for goblins, or 
smaller creatures, so this is most likely a storeroom 
for the bugbears in the dungeon. The room does not 
seem to have been visited lately, and the hallway 
outside is as quiet as a tomb.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears used this room as a 
makeshift armory for a while. Although they rarely 
come here now, there are spears and greatclubs 
stored on weapon racks. To protect their cache, 
the bugbears have rigged a simple spear trap, 
which is easy enough to spot. Stepping within 5¬†ft. 
of the weapons rack triggers the trap unless it is 
first disabled.
 '
Crude Spear Trap. Any PC rolling higher than a 12 
on a Wisdom (Perception) check in the room easily 
spots the spears under tension near the rack. These 
spears spring forward if the trigger (a weave of 
wooden poles hidden under a hide on the floor, 
spanning the 5¬†ft area in-front of the weapon rack) 
is activated. Disarming it is as simple as knocking 
each of the two spears over, where their springs 
worthlessly engage and disarm themselves. PCs 
that fail to notice the spears or charge in heedlessly, 
thus triggering the trap, must succeed a Dexterity 
saving throw (DC¬†15) or receive 1d8 piercing damage 
per spear remaining.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: The PCs have their choice of four 
longspears, two greatclubs, one large warhammer, 
and one shortbow. Upon inspection, the weapons 
are simple and sturdy, but hardly special.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
have the crude spear trap fire four spears. To 
decrease the challenge, reduce the damage of the 
spear trap to 1d4.
B34 . SHRINE OF THE WARRIOR
Moss covers the walls and ceiling of the room. 
Against the eastern wall is a statue of a hobgoblin. 
The statue holds a gleaming short-sword in its 
right hand, and a sharp looking ax in its left. The 
overall pose gives you a sense that this was a 
mighty warrior, and this is hallowed ground.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: As the statue suggests, this room was 
converted into a shrine by the hobgoblins of the 
dungeon. Since the hobgoblins no longer inhabit 
this Section, this room has been abandoned. While 
the weapons are fitted snugly into the statue, they 
can be removed with minimal effort by the PCs. 
This requires a DC¬†14 Strength (Athletics) check for 
each weapon. Any attempt to remove the weapons 
triggers a deafening alarm. But, with no hobgoblins 
in the vicinity, no one responds.
Encounter Condition: Hallowed 2
Tactics: After the PCs trigger the alarm in this room, 
roll for two Random Encounters, and resolve them 
soon, but still somewhat apart.
Treasure: The ax in the statue‚Äôs left band is 
a +1 battleaxe and the sword in the statue‚Äôs right 
hand is a +1 shortsword.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
after the PCs trigger the alarm, roll for three 
Random Encounters, spaced 6d6 seconds apart. To 
decrease the challenge, remove the alarm.

142
B35 . THE PEDESTAL
Brightly polished marble tiles are intricately 
arrayed on the floor of this room. Dark granite 
walls and a high limestone ceiling frame it. A large 
pedestal with a bright red, velvet cushion placed 
upon it, sits majestically in the center of the floor. 
The floor surrounding the pedestal is covered with 
a tile mosaic that depicts a giant snake eating 
its own tail.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Whatever purpose this room once served, 
or what the pedestal held, has been lost. The room‚Äôs 
defenses, however, are still active. Any PCs that 
touch the pedestal trigger a hail of needles trap.
 '
Hail of Needles. When the pedestal is touched, 
a room-wide trap triggers. Slots in the ceiling 
drop fistfuls of needles into the room. Creatures 
within the room with no way to take cover (shields, 
helmets, nearby larger PCs) receive 1d8 piercing 
damage. From then on, every 5¬†ft. moved within the 
room deals another 1d4 piercing damage. This trap 
does not reset for a few weeks.
The mechanism can be spotted with a successful 
DC¬†14 Intelligence (Investigation) check, and 
disabled by succeeding a DC¬†14 Dexterity (Sleight of 
Hand) check.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: Whatever was on the pedestal is no longer 
there, and the pedestal contains no secret 
compartments. Invisible symbols have been drawn 
on the top of the pedestal, however, but these can 
only be found with detect magic (though once seen 
remain visible), which reveals a series of arcane 
marks, laid out in a replicating pattern. A DC¬†15 
Arcana check reveals that the sigils hint to a riddle 
or answer to a riddle. The PC may study the symbols 
for 1 hour, requiring another DC¬†20 Intelligence 
(Arcana) check success to maintain concentration 
that long. If successful, the arcane marks explain 
how to open the secret door leading to Room B55.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
change the hail of needles trap to the raining shards 
trap in Room B5 (with the trigger changed to the 
pedestal). To decrease the challenge, have the trap 
only deal its damage for every 10¬†ft. of movement.
B36 . WOODEN CAGE
The floor, walls, and ceiling of the room are covered 
with wood paneling. The paneling is smooth and 
even, but the smell of dry rot permeates the air. 
There is no discernable damage, however. Sitting in 
the middle of the room is a burlap sack. Gold coins 
spill out of the top of the sack and litter the floor 
around it. As you make your way towards the sack, 
the door behind you slams shut, sealing you in.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Similar to the Hall of Mirrors (Room B6), 
this room was designed by the celestials as a test of 
the prisoner‚Äôs intelligence. A sack, resting on a giant 
pressure-sensitive trigger, serves as bait. Anyone 
who steps within 10¬†ft. of the sack also steps on 
the trigger, and the trap activates. Once the trap is 
activated the door slams shut and is impossible to 
open without resetting the trap.
The reset mechanism is located behind a 
wooden panel in the northeastern corner. The 
panel must be removed carefully to reset the trap; 
if not, the PCs have another danger to contend 
with. Noxious gasses have built up behind the 
rotting wood and the PCs must take the proper 
precautions when removing the panel, or they‚Äôll 
flood the room with the toxic gas. The panel isn‚Äôt 
hard to find. While its purpose is not clear, PCs 
should be made aware of its existence when they 
start searching the room.
When pried open the gases inside burst forth. 
A DC¬†18 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) lets a PC reach 
in and flip the release lever once per hour. Each 
hour the gasses take their toll, dealing 1d8 poison 
damage to all creatures in the room if they fail a 
DC¬†15 Constitution saving throw. PCs reaching for 
the lever take double damage as they get a face full.
When the door opens the gasses quickly vent 
into the hallway and the room becomes safe again.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: The sack contains ten vials of holy water, 
which prisoners might find useless but the PCs may 
be able to put to use.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
change the trap into an acid fog, dealing 2d8 acid 
damage each hour. To decrease the challenge, lower 
the DC of the Constitution save of the trap by -2.

143
B37 . TRAPPED HOWLERS
As the PCs approach the door to this room, read the 
following.
The stone door in front of you doesn‚Äôt look right. 
All the other doors you have seen so far have 
been flush with the surrounding walls. This one, 
however, looks slightly cocked, as if it has been 
jammed shut. Loud whining howls pierce through 
the stone door, flooding the area directly in front 
of it with a cacophonous noise.
If the PCs put their ear to the door, they hear the 
moan of the howlers, forcing them to make DC¬†12 
Wisdom saves or be frightened of the howlers for 1 
minute. The door to this room has been locked and 
the lock damaged by rough hands. A DC¬†20 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check is required to open the door. 
After the PCs open the door, read the following.
As you open the door the noise grows louder as a 
pair of beasts jump from the shadows. The beasts 
resemble spiny-backed hounds, which are hard to 
make out due to the thick smoke filling the room. 
Your curiosity is cut short as the beasts lunge in 
your direction.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: A party of bugbears has trapped two 
howlers inside the room. They also left a fire 
burning in the center of the room in the hopes of 
suffocating the howlers. Sadly, the bugbears do not 
understand that howlers are not mammals from 
this plane and thus not subjected to the same laws 
for breathing. The howlers have not been trapped 
for long, but they are nevertheless eager to depart. 
As soon as the door is opened they rush in, hoping 
to escape. With the PCs in their way, however, they 
turn their attention to them, violently taking out 
their frustrations on the PCs.
Encounter Condition: Smoke
Tactics: The howlers attack the closest PC first, 
latching on with their jagged teeth. They thrash 
about, impaling the PC on their quills. The howlers 
fight ravenously for 2d4 turns, at which point they 
get their wits about them and fight more sensibly, 
flanking the PCs.
Treasure: Once the PCs have dealt with the howlers 
they are free to inspect the room. Aside from 
scratches on the walls, obviously the work of the 
trapped howlers, there is nothing of note. The wood 
in the center of the room has been smoldering 
for some time, however, blanketing the contents 
in ash. Allow the PCs DC¬†22 Wisdom (Perception) 
checks to locate a silver dagger, in the corner of the 
room, coated with ash.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one howler. To decrease the challenge, remove 
one howler.
B38 . RUINED OBSERVATORY
The door to this room has been smashed open, its 
remains strewn about the doorway. The interior is 
a now-familiar sight. The room contains a simple 
stone desk and chair, and a bookshelf against the 
back wall. A large pile of books lies in front of the 
shelf. An ear-piercing whine sounds from within the 
pile, and you spot a strange-looking lizard, with a 
triangular head, rifling through the refuse.

144
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: This room is identical to other celestial 
observatories, the major difference being that 
something has found it and ruined it. The ethereal 
marauder chanced upon the room and is tossing its 
contents, turning over books and chairs.
The ethereal marauder may not notice the PCs 
as they enter the room, busily digging through the 
room‚Äôs contents (suffering a -2 penalty to Wisdom 
(Perception) checks). If the PCs remain in the room 
for more than 30 seconds allow the marauder 
another Wisdom (Perception) check.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: If the ethereal marauder notices the PCs, it 
becomes startled and attacks. If the PCs attack it 
before it notices them, the ethereal marauder flees 
immediately.
Treasure: The books in this room are ruined. While 
they are mostly journals and textbooks, they offer 
no insight into what the celestials had observed 
from this room. Allow the PCs a DC¬†25 Intelligence 
(History) check to uncover information about the 
maze in Room B92. If successful the PCs uncover 
details about its twisting, impossible passages and 
the deadly nature of the maze. Despite its dangers, 
demons trying to escape the prison would run 
through the maze, quickly losing their bearings.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one ethereal marauder. To decrease the 
challenge, reduce the ethereal marauder‚Äôs hit 
points by 5.
B39. HALL OF THE HOBGOBLINS
The door leading to this room is locked, requiring a 
DC¬†20 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock it If 
the check fails by more than 10, roll a d20, on 1-3 the 
thieves‚Äô tools are jammed in the lock and ruined.
Rotted benches and tables fill this cavernous space. 
The floor is littered with scraps of cloth and bone, 
as well as less inviting piles of refuse. Something 
used this room as a meeting place or base of 
operations, but it hasn‚Äôt been used in quite some 
time. At the back of the hall, against the northern 
wall, is a large stone throne and dais.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Before the hobgoblins joined forces with 
their goblin cousins, they made their home here. 
While they have long since abandoned this room, 
some of their belongings, shortspears, and clubs 
scattered amongst the refuse and debris, remain. 
They also left behind the throne of their chieftain, 
and it still sits on its dais under a thick layer of dust.
Encounter Condition: Distracting Visions
Tactics: After the PCs spend 30 minutes in this room, 
roll for a Random Encounter.
Treasure: Hidden in the throne, behind a secret 
panel, is a +1 greatclub. A DC¬†20 Intelligence 
(Investigation) check is required to find the panel, 
while a DC¬†15 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check 
opens it. Scattered around the room are twelve 
javelins, two spears, six clubs, 14 arrows, and six 
poisoned arrows (basic poison).
Scaling: N/A
B40. HALLWAY
If you do not want to alert the PCs to the trap in this 
hallway, do not read the following.
You find yourself in a simple hallway. The walls and 
floor are smooth, and nothing is very out of the 
ordinary. Something prickles at the base of your 
neck, however, as things may not be exactly as they 
appear. At the far end of the hallway, you can hear 
a dull, roaring sound, like howling wind.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: A well-camouflaged pit lies in wait for 
any PCs traversing this expanse of a hallway. If the 
PCs travel more than halfway through the hall, they 
trigger the trap, falling into the 50¬†ft. deep pit.
PCs that roll higher than a 14 on Wisdom 
(Perception) checks in this room notice the 
suspicious nature of the floor. Each step is much 
more hollow than usual, the gaps where they 
shouldn‚Äôt be, etc. Disabling the trap requires 
wedging the hidden hinges along the sides of the 
walls, by succeeding a DC¬†12 Dexterity (Sleight of 
Hand) check with the right tools.

145
While intended to be a smooth deathtrap, time 
and nature have worn the pit enough to allow PCs 
to climb out, should they survive the fall.
Encounter Condition: Echoes 10
Tactics: At the east end of the hallway is a spotless 
room. On the west end is an open door leading 
to Room B41.
Treasure: At the bottom of the pit are a few piles of 
broken bones, one of which still clutches 3d6 gp.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
trigger the trap on a failed Dexterity (Sleight of 
Hand) check. To decrease the challenge, reduce the 
pit depth to 30¬†ft.
B41 . HOWLER DEN
The door to this room is open. If the PCs fell into the 
pit in Room B40, then the howlers hear them coming 
and are not surprised, taking cover in the room. 
Otherwise, the howlers make Wisdom (Perception) 
checks at advantage for the purposes of the PCs 
sneaking up on them.
As you approach the open door, deep growls 
escalate from inside. Something lives here. 
If the PCs succeed at DC¬†13 Perception checks, read 
the following.
Peeking your head in, you see three hounds, with 
fibrous quills on their backs.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: The PCs have entered a howler den, 
although (fortunately) the entire pack is not nearby. 
There are normally as many as ten pack members, 
but presently there are only three howlers. As soon 
as the PCs enter, the howlers unleash their mighty 
howls, wasting no time forcing the PCs from 
their sanctum.
Encounter Condition: Fearless, [Safe]
Tactics: The howlers attack as a pack, lashing out at 
the nearest PC and dragging them to the ground. 
If a PC presents themself as the biggest threat, 
the howlers deal with him first. The howlers bite 
the PCs, latching on with their jagged teeth. Once 
engaged, they use their quills to entangle their 
opponents.
Treasure: A small nest lies in the corner, against a 
stone that is slightly warmer than the others. In 
the nest are the remains of an elf skeleton that 
stumbled into this lair some 5 years ago. The bones 
have been thoroughly gnawed on and the finger 
bones lay about the nest. A golden ring can be 
found in the nest with a successful DC¬†16 Wisdom 
(Perception check). The ring is worth only about 
25 gp but has the name Ellinorith written on it. 
Ellinorith is an elven deserter and should the PCs 
mention the ring or his name to the elves in Region 
H, they confer that he got what was coming to him.
If the PCs investigate the stone, allow an 
Strength (Athletics) or Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
check (DC¬†15) check to pull one of the bricks from 
the wall. Some kind of tool will be needed. A thin 
piece of metal works, but shimmying it between 
the mortar takes some time. Once removed, the 
PCs find a piece of amber that gives off heat in a 
5¬†ft, radius. The heat is around 110 degrees and is 
perfect for putting under a blanket or in the bottom 
of a pot to heat water. The amber never stops 
radiating heat.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one howler. To decrease the challenge, remove 
one howler.
B42 . WELL OF HEALING
The room looks much like the others in this expanse 
of the dungeon but the floor is littered with rubble 
and rocks. At the back of the room is a simple stone 
well. The rope attached to the well‚Äôs frame extends 
straight down and is taut.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The well contains a small treasure and 
the room is designed to prevent anyone from 
retrieving it. The rubble on the floor shows the 
aftermath of the trap, and it is the only clue the PCs 
have regarding the nature of the room. The trap is 
triggered when the handle on the well is turned. 
Triggering the trap unleashes stone blocks from the 
ceiling, which fall down on the PCs. The trigger is 
located in the well itself, a discolored stone on the 
backside of the well marks the trigger location.
Triggering the trap causes a huge block to 
fall from the ceiling, crushing any PCs who fail a 
DC¬†15 Dexterity saving throw for 6d4 bludgeoning 
damage. This trap resets in 2 minutes.

146
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: Once the trap is disarmed, the PCs may 
haul up the bucket attached to the bottom of the 
rope. There is no water in the bucket (as there is no 
water at the bottom of the well), but it does contain 
three vials of shimmering blue liquid. Smart PCs 
should realize this is a great place to store supplies. 
Someone, perhaps Bartleby (Room B28), figured 
out the trap and placed the vials here for future use. 
The PCs should feel confident few people know how 
to get past the trap and can thus store items here 
safely. If the PCs store anything in the bucket, there 
is an 85% chance the items will be here when they 
return. For each week that passes, roll again for 
these items.
Treasure: In the bucket are three vials; each is a 
healing potion.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the damage of the falling block trap to 6d6. 
To decrease the challenge, lower the damage to 6d3.
B43. THE MASHER
The floor in this room is scuffed and heavily 
scratched. Aside from that, it is empty, framed by 
unmarked granite walls. Off towards your right is a 
simple wooden door leading to another room.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: While the room is empty, it is not without 
its perils. The walls conceal poisoned spikes that 
only trigger when the door to the adjoining room 
is opened. Once triggered the spikes spring out of 
the northern and southern walls, and the northern 
wall slowly moves toward the other. In addition, 
the doors to the south shut and lock, requiring a 
successful Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) (DC¬†17) check 
to pick. If the PCs trigger the trap it is still possible 
to reset it while it is moving, but the difficulty 
is increased. When the PCs disable the trap or 
manage to get the door open, they can enter the 
adjoining room to the east, which contains the 
remains of a few elves who died in here. The GM 
should feel free to give them a full complement of 
equipment though.
Encounter Condition: Negative Energy, Stagnant Air.
 '
Masher. When the handle to the door to the 
adjoining room is pulled the north and south walls 
sprout 1.5¬†ft. spikes and begin moving. Both doors 
close and lock if they were not already, sealing the 
PCs in. The mechanism swings with such force 
that any creature caught in the doorway is shoved 
inside. Once the room is sealed the walls slowly 
begin to push together, stopping only when they 
are 3¬†ft. apart.
A maintenance panel is hidden next to the 
door on the east wall, requiring a successful DC¬†15 
Intelligence (Investigation) check to find. When 
rolling Perception checks in the room take note of 
any PC that rolls greater than a 12 or 15. Those who 
roll a 15 or greater notice the trap box immediately. 
Similarly, those who roll a 12-14 notice the box, but 
only when the walls start moving. The soft clink 
and hum of gears inside giving the hidden panel‚Äôs 
position away.
Disabling the trap is only a matter of jamming 
the gears. PCs may attempt Strength (Athletics) 
(DC¬†14) with appropriate items to achieve this. 
Succeeding will halt the walls. Alternatively, a 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check may be attempted 
to tamper with the reset timer. The PCs get one try 
at it, taking the roll, reducing it by 5 (10 if the trap is 
in motion), then multiplying it by 3. That amount of 
minutes is taken off the 1 hour reset time.
Touching the spikes at any point deals 2d6 
piercing damage, and poisons creatures who do not 
succeed a DC¬†12 Constitution saving throw.
If an enterprising PC wishes to test their 
strength against the walls: A contested grapple 
check using Strength (Athletics) is performed 
against the wall. It possesses a strength score of 26, 
adding +13 to its check to contest the grapple. If the 
PC manages to succeed, the wall is halted for 3d10 
minutes, while the reset timer continues to run.
Each grapple attempt applies the spike damage 
twice as the grappler contends with not only the 
mechanism, but the barbs pressing against them.
Encounter Condition: [Negative Energy], 
[Stagnant Air]
Tactics: Once the walls press together, there is a 3¬†ft. 
gap from one to the other. They remain pressed 
together for 1 hour, during which time the PCs 
must succeed a Constitution save (DC¬†10, +1 per 

147
previous save) every 10 minutes to stave off the 
strain of balancing, or buckle and lean momentarily 
against the poisoned wall spikes (suffering damage 
each time).
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the trap‚Äôs damage by 1d6. To decrease the 
challenge, decrease the trap‚Äôs damage to 1d6.
B44. DEAD WORGS
This large room is nearly empty. The walls are black 
and gray, and very clean. However, three massive 
blood-covered wolves lay over the corpses of two dead 
dogs. Blood mats their hair and stains their mouths. 
Their skin is black and much of their hair has been 
singed. The heavy smell of burnt flesh fills the air.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The PCs have stumbled upon a trapped 
room that worgs and dogs were fighting in before 
triggering the fire spray trap. The trap is very potent, 
but with the dead bodies, easy to spot. However, 
if the PCs stumble upon the trigger without being 
careful, they suffer the same fate as the creatures.
 '
Fire Spray Trap. When triggered, a tiny hole in the 
wall flips open and releases a gout of alchemist‚Äôs 
fire. A cone of rapidly igniting liquid chars 
everything in its path. Creatures within the room 
must succeed a DC¬†15 Dexterity saving throw or 
take 5d6 fire damage. The trap resets in 5 minutes.
Tactics: The trigger for this trap is a single small stone 
set in the floor 6¬†ft. from the door, shaped like any 
other in the room. Careful PCs can easily avoid 
and disable it by wedging something underneath. 
Wisdom (Perception) checks that roll a 16 or higher 
notice scuff marks on the edges of adjacent stones 
that reveal its ability to move. The corpses are three 
worgs and two blink dogs that fought in this room, 
before one tripped the fire spray trap, killing them 
all. If the PCs clear the air of smoke, avoid the 
trigger (or disable it), and bar the door, the room is 
considered Safe.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
remove the bodies and add an empty backpack in 
the center of the room as a lure. To decrease the 
challenge, reduce the damage of the trap to 3d6.
B45. THE GOLDEN IDOL
This large room is lined with bright, shiny steel. 
Light bounces off the steel in every direction, 
blinding you. On columns throughout the room are 
ledges lined with lit candles. In the center of the 
room, on a simple wooden table, is a golden idol. 
The figure is about three feet tall, ornately carved, 
and resembles a beautiful angel, holding aloft a 
torch. The room gives off a peaceful feeling, as if it 
was a shrine at some point.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The idol is a tribute from one celestial 
to another; it honors the celestial‚Äôs sacrifices in 
constructing and defending the dungeon complex, 
though this is not readily apparent to the PCs. 
Inscribed on its base is a message (in Celestial). ‚ÄúIn 
darkness, I bring light, never straying from my path.‚Äù 
Removing the idol from the table triggers a trap.
 '
Chaotic Lightning Trap. Upon a platform sits a 
pedestal, with an idol upon a pressure plate. The 
PCs should be made aware of the plate moving as 
they take the idol unless they rush it. If 35 lbs. (half 
the weight of the idol) is removed from or added 
to the pressure plate under the idol, the trap casts 
a lightning bolt spell at 3rd level at the platform. 
Creatures that fail their saving throw against this 
are knocked prone. Once the spell resolves the 
bolt ricochets off the steel walls 1d4 times, striking 
the PCs once more each time. Prone PCs have 
advantage on Dexterity saving throws to avoid this 
trap, and take no damage on a success. The trap can 
be disabled by correctly weighing down the pressure 
plate. Lawful good PCs (or those you feel exemplify 
the alignment‚Äôs values) are immune to the damage 
of this trap.
Encounter Condition: Hallowed 5, Positive 
Energy, [Safe]
Tactics: If the PCs extinguish all the candles, the torch 
on the statue lights up, casting the daylight spell 
at 3rd level. This is true anytime the statue is taken 

148
into a dark room. This effect cannot be controlled 
and only turns off when there is a light source 
nearby. This room has an undoubtedly mysterious 
air to it. The GM should feel free to add whatever 
elements are lacking to keep the PCs in this room, 
examining every nook and cranny. If the PCs never 
disturb the idol, the room is considered Safe.
Treasure: The golden idol weighs about 70 lbs., and is 
worth approximately 1,000 gold pieces.
Scaling: To increase the challenge, change the chaos 
lightning trap to cast chain lightning and decrease 
the 1d4 ricochets to 1d2. To decrease the challenge, 
reduce the damage prone PCs take by half.
B46. BUGBEAR FORWARD POST
A crude map of the dungeon, written in rough, 
goblinoid script, is on the southern wall. It marks the 
locations of various rooms, and the rune for goblin 
is repeated over and over on its surface. Standing in 
the center of the room are three tall goblinoids, with 
sharp fangs and heavy coats of fur. They are armed 
and angry, roaring with a defiant battle cry.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: The PCs have stumbled upon a secret 
staging area of the bugbears, hidden among the 
trap-infested rooms of this section. Safe from their 
goblin enemies, they plan their attacks from here. 
This room provides easy passage to an expanse of 
claimed rooms (B1 through B45), but also to the 
last remaining bugbear stronghold (rooms B52 
through B68).
The room is currently occupied by three 
bugbears. If the PCs make any sound opening the 
door the bugbears gain advantage on Wisdom 
(Perception) checks. If the PCs go unnoticed allow 
the bugbears a second check after thirty seconds. If 
the bugbears notice the PCs, they become incensed 
by the intrusion and attack.
Encounter Condition: Echoes 2
Tactics: Caught off guard, the bugbears assault the 
PCs ferociously. The bugbears work individually, 
attacking the PC closest to them. While it is possible 
to parlay during battle, the bugbears are more 
concerned with silencing anyone that would report 
this room back to Argliss (Room B75).
Treasure: While there is no treasure, per se, the 
map drawn on the wall can easily be copied onto 
parchment, giving the PCs a much-needed help 
navigating the Region. A door near Room B6, 
to the north, is circled and marked (in Goblin), 
‚ÄúKneed Kee.‚Äù If the PCs spend an hour transferring 
the map to paper, give them proficiency in 
Dexterity (Stealth, Sleight of Hand), Wisdom 
(Perception), and Inteligence (Investigation) checks 
made anywhere in the Region. This map lacks 
Rooms B55, B57, and B59 through B62. PCs that 
have the map from Room B25 notice this after 
spending 2 hours comparing the two maps; or 
in 1 hour if they succeed at a DC¬†18 Intelligence 
(Investigation) check.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one bugbear. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one.
B47. CHAMBER OF ECHOES
Sounds echo from the walls of this vacant room. 
A series of noises follow giving the impression 
that footsteps are simply more unnatural sounds 
originating from this room. Human wailing 
surrounds you. Hanging from the ceiling is a rusty 
sword tied with a length of rotting rope.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The sword is a trigger for a crawling claw 
trap. If the PCs find a way to remove the sword 
and replace its weight with something else on the 
rope, they can disable the trap. Otherwise, the trap 
triggers as soon as the PCs lower the sword.
 '
Crawling Claw Trap. The trap is the rope itself. 
Enchanted with necromancy, it brims with latent 
magic, dying to be unleashed. It glows with a pale 
light when viewed by those with magical sight. It 
otherwise presents as mundane. Removing the 
sword without tying another object to the rope 
triggers the trap. Once triggered, 2d4 crawling 
claws burrow out from under the various stones, 
each echoing the alien sounds as they attack.
Encounter Condition: Distracting Noises, Echoes 10
Tactics: No sounds actually originate from this room, 
but instead are amplified from other Regions in the 

149
dungeon. This room has become a nexus for noise 
and the PCs are actually hearing conversations and 
battles going on in Regions E, G, I, and N.
Treasure: The sword is a featherweight longsword 
that needs to be cleaned and sharpened but 
otherwise has survived the ravages of age. The word 
‚Äúsanctify‚Äù is written along the blade in Celestial. 
Featherweight weapons weigh half that of weapons 
of the same type (in this case longswords), gain 
thrown (range 20/60), and use their versatile 
damage dice even when wielded with one hand.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add 1d4 crawling claws to the trap. To decrease the 
challenge of this encounter, halve the number of 
crawling claws created by the trap.
B48. RIDDLE ROOM
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†15 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to open.
Along the western wall of this room is an immense 
red tapestry, covered in silver and black arcane 
sigils, The cloth is silk, and in perfect condition as if 
untouched by the passage of time. On the floor are 
a series of tiles: white stones, mixed with red bricks 
and onyx plates. On the south wall is a strange 
diagram showing the layout of the room.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room is a complex puzzle requiring 
the PCs to make some intelligent decisions. 
ln order to reach the tapestry, the PCs must 
successfully navigate the tiles. The tiles are laid 
out thusly:
The diagram on the wall is wrong, designed to 
encourage interlopers to miss the order in which 
they stand on the tiles. PCs succeeding at a DC¬†20 
Intelligence (Investigation) check or DC¬†15 Wisdom 
(Insight) check are able to read the notes and 
decipher them accordingly.
According to the diagram, the PCs must step on 
the tiles in the order:
White. Red, Black, Red, Black,  
White, Red, Black, Black, White.
This of course is wrong and only if the PCs 
succeed at a DC¬†28 Wisdom (Insight) check 
or a DC¬†25 Wisdom (Survival) check can they 
determine the pattern is illogical and based on their 
knowledge of traps a trick. While this does not help 
them determine the actual order they know the 
diagram is incorrect.
In actuality, it doesn't matter what color they first 
stand on, but once a tile is touched, only that tile 
color should be stepped on (by that PC) from that 
point on. Reaching each stone of that color without 
touching any other stone requires succeeding a 
DC¬†15 Dexterity saving throw, unless the PC chose 
the red bricks which are narrower and require 
successful DC¬†18 Dexterity saving thows. If a PC 
takes the shortest route, they can clear the room 
in six jumps, reaching the tapestry on the other 
side. Longer routes take up to ten jumps, but all of 
them lead to a single 3-ft-wide bronze plate on the 
floor. The plate, which is below the tapestry is safe 
for the PCs to stand on, no matter what color tile 
they chose.
Encounter Condition: [Poor Footing 3]
Tactics: If the PCs step on the wrong tile, they suffer 
a small discharge of energy from the tile based on 
the color of a tile. 
Stepping on a red tile out of turn, reduces the 
PC's speed by 5¬†ft. until their next long rest.
Stepping on a white tile out of turn deals 1d4 
fire damage.
Stepping on a black tile out of turn poisons the 
PC unless they succeed on a DC¬†13 Constitution 
saving throw.
Treasure: Although it radiates no magic of any 
kind, if the tapestry is pulled from the wall and 
wrapped around a humanoid, it forms into a +1 
ghostly scale-mail, which permanently fuses to the 
wielder's body. It is not uncomfortable, able to 
be slept in and worn with little issue. Its ghostly 
nature makes it practically weightless. Anything 
short of dispel evil and good (break enchantment), 
or the wish spell, cannot remove the armor. 
Despite its weightlessness, it is quite loud and 
still manages to restrict movement, inflicting all 
the penaltieswearing scale mail would. wearing 

150
B49-B68 . THE BUGBEAR ENCAMPMENTS
For centuries, the bugbears dominated the other 
goblinoids in the Region. Neither the goblins nor the 
hobgoblins could match the ferocious attacks and 
cunning tactics of the bugbears. Where once their 
domain was extensive, the alliance of the goblins and 
remaining hobgoblins, coupled with the zealous new 
outlook the goblins wield, has driven the bugbears 
back to these few rooms in the western section of 
the Region.
During their reign of dominance, the bugbears 
spent a fair amount of time dismantling many of 
the celestials‚Äô traps. They took advantage of the 
damage the earthquake did to the Region. 
A few of the more complex traps were left 
standing, as the bugbears could simply not 
fathom how to disable them. The de-
stroyed traps have been replaced by sim-
pler ones of the bugbears‚Äô design, which 
they can reset and modify as they see fit.
The intimate knowledge and ever-changing 
array of traps have kept the bugbears safe in 
this domain, their final refuge. The tactics and 
numbers of their enemies may thwart them in 
the rest of the Region, but here on their home 
turf, they control the field and eagerly look 
forward to the day the goblin empire topples 
and they can reclaim their former greatness.
It is possible, however unlikely, for the PCs 
to gain the trust of the bugbears and ally 
themselves with them against the goblins and 
hobgoblins. This is quite difficult to accomplish 
as the bugbears view the PCs as yet another 
faction vying for power in the Region. If the 
PCs can gain the trust of the bugbears, they 
gain allies who know the Region very well and 
have the power to make the PCs‚Äô trek through 
the Region much easier. The simplest way 
to gain the bugbear‚Äôs trust is to show them 
the bodies of slain goblins. Deeds, not words, 
have the best chance of swaying the bug-
bears here.
There are surprisingly few bugbears in these 
encampments. Many are off on sorties against the 
goblin empire. The few that remain plan new raids 
and repair the traps they have laid for the goblins.
If the bugbears believe the PCs are allied with 
the goblins, however, they will not give the PCs any 
chance to prove otherwise.
the armor is reduced to 0 hit points, the armor fades into a red mist and reappears on this wall as a 
tapestry again.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, the penalty for red tiles should stack 3 times. The penalty 
for white tiles should have its damage increased to 1d8. And the penalty for the black tile should inflict 
exhaustion instead of poison.

RAnDoM EnCoUnTERs
Roll for a random encounter once per hour. No random encounters occur in (or around) the secret chambers 
of rooms B49 through B51.
D20encounter
1
This section of the dungeon is unnerving. It could be the air, or the shadows, or the way the sound 
plays off the walls, but something about this area is disturbing. [Haunted].
2
The sound of heavy footfalls echoes throughout the dungeon. A group of bugbears are out hunting 
goblins, or anything else invading their space. The PCs must succeed at three DC¬†14 ‚ÄúStealth‚Äù checks. 
These are not normal Dexterity (Stealth) checks, and are not contested rolls. If the PCs choose to 
spend extra time by not moving from where they are, they should have advantage on these checks, 
and should not suffer armor disadvantage. If they fail any of the checks, they encounter the bugbears, 
as if a 19 had been rolled on this table.
3-12Nothing.
13
A stone block falls from the ceiling, striking a random PC for 4d6 bludgeoning damage unless they 
pass a DC¬†14 Dexterity saving throw. Allow one PC a Wisdom (Perception) check (DC¬†17) to spot the 
brick before it has a chance to harm anyone.
14
A pack of 1d4+2 worgs wander the dungeon. They are not hunting the PCs, and have only a 25% 
chance of noticing them. If the PCs do not wish to confront the worgs, they must succeed at a 
DC¬†15 Dexterity (Stealth) check to avoid being noticed. If the PCs elect to stop for a time, grant them 
advantage on those checks, and remove armor disadvantage for them.
15
A pair of bugbears are resetting a scything blade trap (see room B1). The PCs notice the bugbears first 
if any roll higher than a 15 on a Wisdom (Perception) check. Otherwise, the bugbears get the drop on 
them. Whichever side loses this is surprised.
16
See 13, but instead of falling of their own accord the stone pieces are attached to a tripwire. 
Depending on the party‚Äôs formation more than one party member can be hit. The blocks now strike 
1d4 party members and deal 6d6 of damage on a failed saving throw.
17
A group of three ethereal marauders turn the corner and face the PCs. They are startled by the PCs‚Äô 
presence. They have a 50% chance of fleeing outright. Otherwise, they are Unfriendly to the PCs 
unless attacked.
18
The PCs chance upon a violent skirmish between the bugbears and goblins down the hall. 3d6 
goblins are engaged in furious combat with 2d4+1 bugbears. One of the goblins spots the PCs and 
both groups strike out and turn their attention to the PCs.
19
The noises of the PCs have attracted the attention of a nearby bugbear patrol. Impose a -2 penalty on 
the PCs‚Äô Wisdom (Perception) checks to notice the bugbears before they attack. The party is made up 
of 2d4+1 bugbears armed with short spears and swords. Aughkin (Room B62) leads the patrol.
20
Bartleby (Room B29) is inspecting a portion of the wall here. He seems intent on his work and 
doesn‚Äôt look up as the PCs arrive. Bartleby suffers a -4 penalty to his Wisdom (Perception) checks for 
30 seconds.
B49. SANCTUM
The door to this room was locked, requiring a 
Dexterity Sleight of Hand check (DC¬†19) to pick open.
This hidden room is in good repair. A simple desk 
and chair, and a large oak bookcase are the only 
furnishings. The desk is empty, but a number of small 
bottles are scattered over the shelves of the bookcase.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears never discovered the secret 
door in Room B51. They don‚Äôt know this place exists, 
leaving it free from their stench. Surprisingly, there 
are no traps or enchantments here, and Wisdom 
(Perception) checks of 15+ give an overwhelming 
confidence that the room is free of danger.

152
Encounter Condition: Safe
Tactics: Used as a sanctum years ago, the room is a 
perfect hiding place for the PCs. The time it takes to 
complete short or long rests here is halved, owing 
to the surprising comfort... or perhaps some celes-
tial enchantments.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: N/A
B50. SECRET CHAMBER
As the PCs near the secret door on the eastern wall of 
Room B59, read the following.
A sliver of light spills out into the hallway from a 
crack in the wall.
As the PCs near the secret door on the western wall 
of Room B50, read the following.
A sliver of yellow light spills out into the hallway 
from a crack in the wall. Grunting sounds can be 
heard from behind it.
Finding the secret door requires a DC¬†15 Intelli-
gence (Investigation) check and a DC¬†15 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check to slide it open. A small, 
rough stone doubles as a handle, allowing the PCs 
to simply lift the door open. The secret door on 
the western wall is jammed and requires a DC¬†14 
Strength (Athletics) check in addition to the Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check.
As the PCs enter the room, read the following.
An oddly shaped room opens. In the middle of 
the room, set into the northern wall, is a stone 
door. The room contains no furnishings other 
than a stack of four strongboxes, one on top of 
the other. Wherever the sound was coming from is 
gone for now.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room is more of a causeway, used 
by the celestials to shuffle about behind the scenes. 
There is nothing here to explore (except the strong-
boxes), but opening the doors could prove a chal-
lenge to the PCs.
This room contains three hidden doors. Which-
ever one the PCs came through stays open for 2d6 
seconds before closing. After that, they can easily 
find and open the door again.
The door on the northeastern wall leads to 
Room B49 and requires a DC¬†25 Investigation check 
to find and a DC¬†25 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
check to open. The same is true of opening it from 
the other side. This secret door remains open for 
2d6 seconds.
The secret door on the southeastern wall leads 
to a long corridor and the secret door on the west-
ern wall opens into a north-south corridor (that 
leads to either Room B52 or B53). Finding either 
secret door requires a DC¬†20 Intelligence (Inves-
tigation) check and a DC¬†20 Dexterity (Sleight of 
Hand) check to slide it open. A small, rough stone 
doubles as a handle, allowing the PCs to merely lift 
the door open.
The secret door on the western wall can easi-
ly be found from the inside but requires a DC¬†14 
Athletics check to open in addition to the Sleight of 
Hand check.
The door to the north is locked (from both sides) 
and requires a DC¬†22 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
check to open. The small interior chamber leads to 
another, similar locked door that is also locked on 
both sides.
Encounter Condition: Echoes 6, Safe
Tactics: The sounds the PCs heard were the dungeon 
playing tricks on their ears. There is no one here, 
but when the doors are closed and the PCs stand 
just outside it seems like there is.
Treasure: All four boxes are equally weighted and 
none make any sound when shaken. The third 
strongbox, however, is the only one with anything 
in it. All four are locked.
Each strongbox requires a DC¬†27 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check to open and each lock 
is trapped with a poison needle trap. If anything 
except a key is inserted, the needle springs forth, 
jabbing the intruder. Victims that fail a DC¬†13 
Dexterity saving throw take 2d8 poison damage and 
must succeed a DC¬†15 Constitution saving throw or 
be poisoned. They are easy to spot and should only 
get the most careless of thieves. The mechanism 
will not reset automatically once fired.
In the third box, strapped to the inside of the lid, 
are five potions: healing (x2), resistance, sanctuary, 
and gaseous form.
Scaling: N/A

153
B51. PRIVATE STUDY
The door leading to this room is locked, requiring a 
DC¬†27 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) to pick.
This is a simply furnished room, with a small cot 
and a table. A tattered pillow and blanket rest on 
the cot, and both reek of mold and mildew. Upon 
the table is a shiny, gold ring and a hefty book.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Before the doppelganger Argliss took over 
the goblin empire, he made this room his home. 
Well hidden, it proved a solid base of operations 
to fall back to. While he spent years living here, he 
never returned after becoming king. Knowing his 
journal was safe, he left the room as it was, hoping 
one day to trap something with his ruse.
The ring on the table is rigged to explode, con-
suming the book in a blaze and harming those who 
trespass. It is rigged with a fire trap (Room B18).
Encounter Condition: Safe
Tactics: If the PCs disable the trap on the ring (a hefty 
task), the ring and the book are theirs. The book is 
Argliss‚Äô journal. It details his encounters with the 
halfling Bartleby (room B28). The doppelganger 
is quite upset with the loss of the artifact Bartleby 
seeks. Bartleby is allowed to keep any other artifacts 
he finds in the Region as payment, provided the 
artifact is returned to Argliss.
While it does not say anywhere in the journal 
that Argliss is a doppelganger, it does allude to 
strange circumstances where he is not always a 
goblin. Allow the PCs a DC¬†15 Intelligence (Histo-
ry) check or a DC¬†20 Intelligence (Nature) check 
to deduce he is a barghest. If they succeed at a 
DC¬†21 History check or a DC¬†25 Intelligence (Na-
ture) check, they realize he is not a barghest, but a 
doppelganger. The GM should make these checks 
secretly so the PCs don‚Äôt know whose informa-
tion to trust.
Treasure: The last page of the journal is a scroll of fire-
ball. The ring radiates strong transmutation magic 
and appears to be a ring of invisibility if the PCs cast 
identify on it. It is actually a cursed ring with several 
side effects. First, it causes the wearer to automat-
ically fail saving throws against the scry spell. In 
addition, the wearer can never turn invisible, no 
matter the strength of the spell. It also causes the 
wearer to be constantly under the effect of a zone 
of truth. Lastly, while the wearer‚Äôs alignment does 
not change, they cannot willingly violate any lawful 
good tenets, including killing innocents, betraying 
a trust, or deceiving a fellow man. While they don‚Äôt 
have to always behave ‚Äúlawful good‚Äù, they do have 
to monitor more obvious actions. This powerful 
magic item was here when Argliss moved in and he 
never put it on, for fear of the celestial‚Äôs games.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the Investigation DC of the fire trap by +5. 
To decrease the challenge, reduce the Intelligence 
(Arcana) DC of the fire trap by -5.
B52. STRAY DIRE WOLF
You hear a low, deep growl as you approach an 
open chamber ahead. A wandering dire wolf 
stalks the hallways, its hackles raised. It snarls 
at you, baring its fangs menacingly from the 
darkness ahead.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: A lone dire wolf roams the hallways, 
apparently lost. It has been here for some time and 
grows more agitated as the hours roll on. When the 
PCs enter the room, the wolf attacks.
Encounter Condition: Ambush (darkness), Fearless
Tactics: This dire wolf is fast and agile. Having 
roamed these halls for some time, it is worked up. 
The dire wolf gains the effects of the Mobility and 
Alert feats. In combat, it attacks the closest PC and 
continues attacking until it is subdued or the PCs 
are dead. It trips PCs on each attack, moving onto 
the next PC, once one is down. If two PCs are down 
at the same time, it takes a round to bite a prone 
PC before moving on. Wisdom (Animal Han-
dling) checks involving the beast are performed at 
disadvantage.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one dire wolf. To decrease the challenge, re-
move the benefit of the Alert and Mobility feats.
