B53 . THE RESERVOIR
Towards the back of this large room is a low, 
circular well. The well‚Äôs placement is reminiscent of 
a town square fountain. The principle difference is 
that the well has no discernable bottom. In front of 
the well is a small sack with gems spilling out of it.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Whatever the original purpose of the 
room was has been lost. Now, the bugbears use 
this room to dispose of captured goblins and other 
creatures, having placed the gems here to lure 
goblin patrols. Lifting the sack triggers the pres-
sure-sensitive plate (which can be noticed by rolling 
higher than a 15 on a Wisdom (Perception) check) 
underneath. When triggered, the door to the room 
seals and it rapidly floods to a depth of about 4¬†ft. 
This is ultimately harmless, but after 3 minutes the 
room begins to drain. 
PCs must succeed two consecutive DC¬†14 
Strength (Athletics) checks or be sucked down the 
50¬†ft. drop into the well. The trip is rough and deals 
2d6 bludgeoning damage as they strike the walls 
on the way down. Climbing out is difficult but not 
impossible, requiring a successful DC¬†17 Strength 
(Athletics) check to perform well, otherwise they 
incur a level of exhaustion. Enterprising PCs might 
trigger the trap again to force a stuck PC out.
The door to the room has a stubborn seal that 
can be defeated with a wedge of some variety and 
a successful DC¬†25 Strength (Athletics), or a DC¬†18 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check. Unsealing the 
flooded room drains its contents into the nearby 
area and breaks its mechanism for good.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
change the room‚Äôs drain timer from 3 minutes to 
6d20 seconds. This is rolled each time the room is 
triggered. To decrease the challenge, reduce the DC 
of the Strength (Athletics) and Dexterity (Sleight of 
Hand) checks by -5.
B54 THE BUGBEAR PACK 
LEADERS' HALL
This massive room is furnished with hides and 
skulls, trophies of a more prosperous time for the 
bugbears. The walls are rough, and covered in crude 
runes and hairline cracks. The floor is stained badly, 
and littered with scraps of bone. In the middle of 
the room is a squat, wide table with a large map 
placed on it. Around the room are four bugbears. 
The largest snarls at you and reaches for his club.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: Unless the PCs have spoken with Aughkin 
(Room B62) the three bugbears in this room attack 
the PCs without hesitation. If the PCs have spoken 
with Aughkin, the bugbears‚Äô initial attitude is Un-
friendly instead and they do not attack the PCs.
While the bugbears‚Äô attitude is Unfriendly, the 
PCs can negotiate with them, deferring to their 
leader, Sharpfang. Sharpfang is particularly ornery 
and pays the barest amount of lip service to Augh-
kin‚Äôs ‚Äúpresumed‚Äù status within the encampment. 
He humors the PCs to increase his own stature and 
gain respect from his fellow bugbears.
His knowledge is limited to the goblin and 
bugbear war. Sharpfang does not give the PCs 
any insights about traps or what to expect in the 
dungeons. A successful DC¬†12 Intelligence (Insight) 
check reveals that Sharpfang does not care if the 
PCs fall victim to the traps in the dungeon or not. 
He could give the PCs valuable information, but he 
chooses not to.
Sharpfang and his raiding party created the map 
on the table. It details the bugbear encampment 
and the goblin empire (Rooms B52 to B91). While 
it‚Äôs marked with dots and splotches, the placement 
is incomprehensible to the PCs. Only Sharpfang is 
sure what the markings mean, and he refuses to tell 
them. If the PCs call him on this refusal to help, he 
gets angry. If they continue to push, he attacks.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: Sharpfang attacks the strongest PC, while his 
subordinates watch his flank, striking any PCs who 
get near him.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encoun-
ter, add one bugbear. To decrease the challenge, 
remove two.

B55. A BLACK PEARL?
The secret door leading to this has not been found in 
centuries. The PCs must succeed at a DC¬†25 Intelli-
gence (Investigation) check to find this secret door. 
It is completely flush with the stone and even if they 
know it‚Äôs there, they only gain advantage to locate the 
groove in the wall. If successful they pry open a 4¬†ft. 
wide door that allows access to the room.
This room is cramped due to a large pedestal that 
takes up the center of the room. The top of the 
pedestal is covered in black velvet. Nestled in the 
center of the velvet is a single, flat black stone. 
Oddly, there is no dust in the room.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: If the PCs aren‚Äôt paranoid about the traps 
in this Region, they haven‚Äôt tried hard enough. 
Chances are they believe the stone is trapped, 
seeing it resting on a pedestal, unguarded. In fact, 
it is not. The PCs merely need to walk up and lift 
the stone from the pedestal. But they don‚Äôt have to 
know that.
Encounter Condition: [Drafty]
Tactics: If the door to this room is left ajar, it creates 
a draft that sweeps through, threatening to blow 
out torches.
Treasure: The pearl on the pedestal is actually a bead 
of force. It lacks the ability to trap creatures inside its 
radius, instead dealing an extra 8d8 radiant damage 
on impact.
Scaling: N/A
B56. THE BUGBEARS' WORKSHOP
A large workbench stretches along the northern 
wall. Tools lie haphazardly on top of and 
underneath it. Shelves lying against the western 
wall contain scraps of iron, brass, and copper. Off 
in a corner of the room are piles of leather and rope.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Whether it is a new spear or a piece of 
a deadly trap, if the bugbears need it they make it 
in this room. The tools are hanGMade and crude, 
but they serve their purpose. The bugbears are not 
master craftsmen by any means, but they do good 
work and their cunning in devising traps has served 
them well. At the moment, the room is empty, but 
the bugbears in Room B57 are busy at work.
Encounter Condition: Echoes 2
Tactics: If the PCs succeed at DC¬†21 Wisdom (Per-
ception) checks, they hear grunts coming from the 
other side of the wall. While the secret door here is 
not obvious, there is enough of a gap for sound to 
come through.
The secret door leads to Room B57 and requires 
a DC¬†21 Intelligence (Investigation) check to find. 
It does not appear on the map in Room B25 and 
therefore the PCs do not get a bonus to find it. If 
the PCs make a great deal of noise, allow the bug-
bears in Room B57 Wisdom (Perception) checks to 
notice them.
Treasure: The workshop contains scraps of iron, 
brass, and copper as well as multiple shafts of 
wood. There is also a small pile of leather and rope. 
The tools themselves are worthless, simple things 
made for large hands.
Scaling: N/A

B57 . THE BUGBEARS' ARMORY
This room serves as the armory. Aside from the 
various weapons that adorn the racks and shelves 
in this room, you can‚Äôt help but notice a group of 
surly goblinoids, seven feet tall, and covered in fur. 
They are sorting through scrounged debris and piles 
of stones, as they look up to see you.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Unlike the majority of rooms in their 
domain, the armory of the bugbears is not aban-
doned. Three bugbears have just returned from a 
patrol and are sorting through some of the supplies 
they‚Äôve scrounged (rope, wood, etc.). They do not 
take kindly to intrusions, especially in one of their 
hidden caches. If they do not hear or see the PCs 
coming, they are surprised, but ready for battle 
nonetheless.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The bugbears attack the closest PCs, and 
stay in a tight group. They use their size to their 
advantage and do everything they can to push the 
fight into the hall. Weak PCs are easy targets and 
the bugbears hurl whatever they can find at pesky 
spellcasters who launch spells from the back of 
the party.
Treasure: The armory contains a dozen short spears, 
three long spears, six short swords, eight great-
clubs, and an assortment of rope, stones, wire, 
wood, and anything else they could manage 
to scrounge.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encoun-
ter, add two bugbears. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one.
B58 . SUPPLY ROOM
Empty barrels and empty shelves fill this room; 
a supply depot, in serious need of supplies by all 
appearances. Only scraps of iron and leather, and a 
few sticks, are currently in stock.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears store spare parts for their 
traps, as well as additional supplies for making 
weapons here. The current lack of supplies indicates 
how bad off the bugbears currently are in their 
campaign against the goblins.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: The supply room contains scraps of iron 
and leather, as well as a few bundles of short sticks 
that could possibly be used for spears.
Scaling: N/A
B59 . SLEEPING QUARTERS
Various animal hides and blankets cover the floor. 
You get the impression this is a communal sleeping 
room for the remaining bugbears. The room feels 
safe and secure, and you can understand why the 
bugbears chose it. Fortunately for you, it is deserted 
at present.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears, when not out raiding, re-
treat here to rest. They have claimed a great number 
of safe rooms in their small domain, and use them 
to their advantage. Other than the animal hides 
covering the floor, this room is empty.
Encounter Condition: Safe

B60 . ENTRANCEWAY TO THE 
INNER SANCTUM
The secret door can be found by the PCs with a DC¬†20 
Intelligence (Investigation) check. While the door is 
secret, it is also locked. Opening the secret door re-
quires a DC¬†25 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) to manipu-
late the hidden mechanism. Alternatively, the PCs can 
use Aughkin‚Äôs (Room B62) key, which requires them 
to encounter him as a Random Encounter.
Fine, almost powdery, rubble litters the floor of this 
room. Along the west wall are three separate doors. 
Based on the contents, it‚Äôs safe to assume this is a 
storeroom for the inhabitants of the dungeon.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears have utilized the resources 
left behind by the celestials well. They survive the

vicious goblin attacks mainly because their guerrilla

with the protection of a secret entrance, the bug-

B61 . THE HEALER
This room seems out of place. While other rooms in 
this stretch of the dungeon are either wide, empty 
halls or small, cramped cells, this room is... cozy. 
A large goblinoid sits placidly in the center of the 
room, adding to the overall strangeness of the 
scene. His hair is white, perhaps from age, and his 
manner is calm and unobtrusive.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent
Encounter: This bugbear, known only as Healer, is 
quiet, serene, and imposing. Standing a full 7¬†ft. 
high, Healer is white-haired and appears very wise. 
The Healer is not typical of the bugbears by any 
means. He has lived long enough to understand 
that war between the goblinoid tribes is unneces-
sary, but an irrefutable fact of their heritage. He has 
resigned himself to seclusion.
He couldn‚Äôt care less about the PCs‚Äô presence, 
but helps them out‚Äîgiving them medicinal herbs 
to heal their wounds‚Äîif asked. The Healer does 
not ‚Äúwaste‚Äù magical healing on the PCs unless 
the PCs have proven themselves to be stoic allies 
of the bugbears first. He reserves his magic for 
his comrades, unsure of when the goblins could 
attack next.
The PCs can ask Healer about the bugbears; he 
answers their questions to the best of his abilities. 
He is tired of the war and simply wishes to be left 
undisturbed in his sanctuary. If the PCs are in the 
room for more than one hour, the Healer starts to 
get agitated and his attitude shifts from Indifferent 
to Unfriendly.
The Healer never attacks the PCs first. If the 
PCs attack him, however, he will do his best to 
subdue them.
Encounter Condition: Hallowed 2, Safe
Tactics: The Healer calls upon his deity to protect him 
from the PCs, alternating between casting spells 
and attacking the nearest PC with his +1 morning-
star. He casts entropic ward before a fight breaks out 
and calm emotions once things get heated.
Treasure: The medicinal herbs Healer carries heal 
1d4+1 hit points each and he has enough medicine 
to make 2d12 doses for the PCs.
B62 . THE RETIRED PACK LEADER
Cramped and reeking of rotten meat, this small 
room is dominated by an aging goblinoid. Even 
seated, you can tell he is well over seven feet tall 
and a mass of fibrous muscles waiting to snap. His 
hair is gray and mottled, and deep scars line the 
bugbear‚Äôs face, chest, and hands.
If the PCs do not surprise the bugbear, add the 
following.
Staring at you from his perch, his one good eye 
searches deeply, curious about you. He seems to be 
having the same trouble reading you as you have 
reading him.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: The creature in this room is a bugbear 
named Aughkin. He is old and of no use in raid-
ing parties. However, he has lived a long time, an 
indication of intelligence to this bugbear tribe. The 
others keep him here and rely on his wisdom and 
stories of past adventures to help plan bolder raids 
into the goblin expanses. While he would rather be 
in the thick of a raiding party, he is content to guide 

158
the younger bugbears to victory over the accursed 
goblins. He does not advise in matters he consid-
ers suicide, and whether the true leader or not, 
still treats his ‚Äúmen‚Äù with the dignity and respect 
due soldiers.
With a DC¬†20 Charisma (Persuasion) check, 
the PCs can convince Aughkin they are not here 
to harm him or the bugbears. Aughkin and Heal-
er (room B61) are willing to hear the PCs out and 
perhaps reach an agreement, but this requires 
roleplaying, not die rolling, and ultimately is the 
decision of the GM. Should they reach an accord, 
word spreads amongst the bugbears that the 
PCs can be trusted and the two groups should 
work together.
If attacked, or enraged, Aughkin attacks the PCs.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: Aughkin would rather not fight, but he is not 
afraid of death. He has become a good advisor by 
thinking before he acts. If forced into battle, Augh-
kin does not hesitate, however. He launches himself 
at the PCs with a ferocity rarely seen in bugbears 
half his age. He gains the benefit of the barbarian‚Äôs 
Rage feature for the duration of combat, despite 
not being a barbarian, and grapples the nearest PC 
he can find. If he gets a PC on the ground, Aughkin 
grabs ahold of the PC‚Äôs neck and threatens to snap 
it if the others do not back off. Because of the size 
of Aughkin‚Äôs hands, he deals 1d4+1 bludgeoning 
damage each turn while successfully grappling.
Treasure: Aughkin does not keep anything in his 
chambers that does not serve him in warfare. 
Clothing and magical aid are given to his men and 
for himself, he‚Äôs kept a simple +1 dagger. If the PCs 
spend 30 minutes searching the room they manage 
to find an old journal (written in Goblin) that tells of 
his younger days as a soldier, and his recent years 
as a leader, unwilling to jeopardize his men.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add two bugbears. To decrease the challenge, have 
Aughkin surrender if his grapple fails.
B63 . GOTCHA!
Stark, this room is nearly identical to many rooms 
in the dungeon. The one feature that distinguishes 
it however is an intricate pattern of tiles on the 
floor. The tiles are covered in a layer of dust, 
however, and it is difficult to discern anything 
specific about them. Hanging on the wall, across 
from you, is a finely crafted spear.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears like to capture the occa-
sional goblin, as they sometimes prove to be reli-
able sources of information. While the rest of the 
traps the bugbears have laid out in their domain are 
lethal, this room is not. Any goblins captured in this 
room are brought to Room B53 for interrogation.
The tiles on the floor are the trap‚Äôs trigger, an 
alternating black and white pattern (like a checker-
board). PCs stepping on black tiles trigger a large 
net trap while stepping on white tiles is safe. To 
disable the trap the PCs must find a specific black 
tile in the southwest corner of the room where 
the trap‚Äôs reset is located. Finding the tile is easy 
enough, requiring a successful Intelligence (Inves-
tigation) (DC¬†14) check. However, lifting the tile and 
disarming the trap is another issue entirely. There 
are a series of twelve buttons, in three different 
colors (black, red, white) that must be depressed in 
a specific order. A successful DC¬†15 Intelligence (In-
vestigation) check indicates that the buttons must 
be pressed in pairs. Failure on this check indicates 
that the colors are directly related to the tiles on 
the floor.
A second DC¬†17 Intelligence (Investigation) 
check indicates that the buttons must be pressed in 
order‚Äîred, black, and white. Failure on this check 
indicates the order is black, white, and red.
Lastly, the PCs are allowed a third check (this 
time at a DC¬†20) to determine the exact pairs that 
need to be depressed. If the PCs fail this check, they 
choose the wrong pair.
If a button is ever pressed out of order (or 
pressed in correspondence to the incorrect pair), 
the PC triggers a cantrip targeting the but-
ton-presser based on the color. The black button 
triggers a chill touch, the red button triggers fire 
bolt, and the white button shocking grasp. The can-
trips are cast as if by a 1st level.

159
 '
Large Net Trap. When triggered a room-wide net 
made of bundled wire descends from the ceil-
ing, catching all beneath it. PCs must succeed an 
Strength (Athletics) check (with a DC equal to their 
AC) for every 10¬†ft they wish to move underneath it. 
If the trap is disabled while it is active the net rises 
once more.
If more than 2 hours pass after the net is trig-
gered a patrol of 1d3 bugbears investigates.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: PCs succeeding at a DC¬†20 Wisdom (Percep-
tion) check realize that the mechanism for protect-
ing the large net is more complicated than the net 
itself, hinting that at one time the trap was more 
than just a net. Once the trap is disabled, the room 
is safe until the bugbears reset it (in 2d6 hours). It 
is recommended that the GM make the checks in 
private, lest the PCs get wise to the trap‚Äôs function.
Treasure: The spear is a featherweight spear. It is the 
bait by which all goblins are tricked into entering 
this room. PCs that lifted the special black tile are 
allowed Wisdom (Perception) (DC¬†16) checks. Those 
who succeed realize that the buttons are built into 
a locking hinge that hides a compartment under-
neath. If they successfully disable all three traps, 
they can lift the mechanism (requires succeeding 
a DC¬†17 Strength (Athletics) check) to find a pair of 
magical daggers. One of the daggers is an angel-
bane dagger, while the other is a fairybane dagger.
Angelbane weapons are +2 and magical when 
used against creatures that speak Celestial. Fairy-
bane daggers are +2 and magical when used against 
creatures that understand Sylvan.
Featherweight weapons weigh half that of 
weapons bearing the same type, gain thrown (range 
20/60), and use their versatile damage dice even 
when wielded with one hand.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
change the large net trap to a camouflaged pit trap 
(Room B40). To decrease the challenge, change the 
large net trap to a portcullis trap.
 '
Portcullis Trap. When triggered a portcullis slams 
down in front of the exit. Creatures underneath are 
skewered and crushed and must succeed a Dexter-
ity saving throw (DC¬†13) or take 2d8 piercing and 
2d8 bludgeoning damage. Additionally, creatures 
that fail to save are pinned underneath, preventing 
movement until freed. Any creature that can lift 200 
lbs. of weight can reliably lift the gate 1¬†ft. off the 
ground, with the weight requirement doubling for 
each additional foot of distance desired. The gate 
will rise when the trap is reset.
B64 . A LONG WAY DOWN
This simple chamber is quite nondescript, except for 
a pair of high-quality long spears abandoned in the 
center of the room. Two gems, in the opposite wall, 
stare back at you, like a pair of red eyes.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Like Room B63, the bugbears set up a 
simple pit trap to snare goblin scouts. The long 
spears have been left to lure the unsuspecting 
goblins into a trap. If that doesn‚Äôt work, the gems 
in the wall will. The floor beneath the long spears 
(5-ft-by-5-ft square) can only support 10 lbs. before 
it opens, dropping the victim(s) into the 60¬†ft pit 
below if they fail a DC¬†15 Dexterity saving throw. A 
locking mechanism can be found, with a successful 
Intelligence (Investigation) check (DC¬†15), behind a 
panel in the eastern wall. Once the switch is flipped, 
the doors to the pit do not open and the PCs can 
travel across the room safely.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The gems are only painted glass, designed 
to lure goblins across the room. They cannot be 
removed from the wall, short of a DC¬†30 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check. If removed, the bugbears 
replace them in 1d3 days. This trap is either an 
indication that bugbears aren‚Äôt very inventive or that 
goblins aren‚Äôt hard to trick.
Treasure: The two spears are normal spears, which 
the PCs are free to take once they have circumvent-
ed the trap. The gems are worthless glass.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encoun-
ter, increase the depth of the pit trap by 20¬†ft. To 
decrease the challenge, reduce the depth of the pit 
trap by 20¬†ft.

B65. STORAGE
The door to this room is locked. A DC¬†25 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check is required to unlock it. 
The smell of death inside is evident before the PCs 
open the door.
As soon as you open the door, the smell of death 
assaults you. This small room has a pile of dead 
goblins, who are rotting. Flies and maggots fill the 
air, escaping past the PCs and into the open air. 
Stacked along the walls are all manner of wood 
beams, spikes, polearms, and tripwires.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room is filled with the tools and 
equipment for making traps (not to mention a 
half-dozen dead goblins). It looks as though it is 
regularly used, but how the bugbears endure the 
stench is another story.
Encounter Condition: Diseased (mindfire) 12, 
Stagnant Air
Tactics: While mindfire is normally inhaled, if the PCs 
avoid touching the goblins, they gain advantage on 
the Constitution saves to resist the mindfire.
Treasure: If the PCs have the stomach for it, they can 
search the dead bodies, finding a total of 36 sp, 
14 cp, a key to the door in Room B80, and a po-
tion of jump.
Scaling: N/A
B66. BUGBEAR HIDEOUT
The door to this room is locked, requiring DC¬†25 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock.
Unless the PCs succeed at a DC¬†25 Dexterity 
(Stealth) check while opening the lock, read the 
following:
This room is enormous. The vaulted ceiling and 
painted walls make this room appear larger than 
life. Standing, weapons at the ready, are eight tall, 
angry, grizzled goblinoids covered in mottled brown 
fur, their jagged teeth exposed.
If the PCs succeed in picking the lock quietly, read 
the following.
This room is enormous. The vaulted ceiling and 
painted walls make this room appear larger than 
life. Pacing about the room, sharpening weapons, 
and sifting through crates are eight tall, grizzly 
goblinoids covered in mottled fur, their jagged teeth 
exposed. They do not notice you.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly or Hostile
Encounter: Eight bugbears are using this room 
to plan a raid on the goblins. Normally, they are 
mobilized, moving about the halls, but these bug-
bears have a plan up their sleeves. They intend to 
gather their strength together, sneak through the 
maze (Room B92), and attack the sleeping goblin 
army from behind. By striking from the far end of 
the goblin empire, they hope to distract the main 
arm of the army and send a smaller force to kill 
the goblin king. If the bugbears do not notice the 
PCs, they continue planning their attack. However, 
every so often, allow one of them a Wisdom (Per-
ception) check to notice the PCs. If the PCs watch 
for too long, the bugbears assume they are spies 
and attack. If the PCs approach peacefully, however, 
there is an opportunity to work with the bugbears. 
Allow the PCs to role-play through the situation or 
use Wisdom (Persuasion) or Charisma (Deception) 
to diffuse the hostilities.
If attacked, or enraged, Oskin attacks the PCs.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: If the PCs try to strike a bargain with the 
bugbears, Oskin (the largest of the eight) listens 
to what the PCs have to say and, if he trusts them, 
invites them to help on the raid, asking them to 
attack from the north while they use the maze to 
disguise their approach. In combat, the bugbears 
fight to silence the PCs. Two rush to block the door, 
while the rest flank the PCs. Oskin directs the battle 
for two rounds before attacking the largest PC. 
They are tireless fighters and have no qualms about 
killing the PCs.
Treasure: All of the bugbears carry well-crafted weap-
ons and are prepared for battle. Oskin carries two 
potions of healing and a potion of the giant‚Äôs strength.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add two bugbears. To decrease the challenge, 
remove two.

161
B67. THE LAST LINE OF DEFENSE
This room is large and appears empty, but 
something about it bristles with menace. There 
are no signs of the goblins occupying this room, 
so it must still be in the domain of the bugbears. 
Why they have chosen to leave it empty is a 
mystery, however.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The bugbears have littered this room with 
as many traps as possible. If the goblins seek to take 
their final hidden refuge (Room B68), the bugbears 
plan on exacting a heavy toll.
Scattered around the room are six different 
traps, each placed in such a way that the PCs cannot 
avoid them all if they move between the doors on 
the western and northeastern walls. The GM is free 
to trigger as many or as few of the following traps 
as he likes.
The basic arrow and spear traps occur three times 
throughout the room and the dart traps occur twice.
 '
Spear Trap. Running perpendicular to the walls are 
3 spear traps with simple 5-ft. wide tripwires placed 
in their line of fire. Each launches its payload at the 
unfortunate PC who triggers it, dealing 1d8 damage 
if they fail a DC¬†15 Dexterity saving throw. Should 
they succeed, the next PC that would be behind 
them must succeed the save or be struck instead. 
Disarming it is as simple as knocking it over, where 
the tension will be undone safely.
 '
Poisoned Darts. Tiny clusters of darts sit loaded 
into a pair of crude launchers in each of the far 
corners of the room. When their awkwardly strewn 
triggers are depressed a spray of darts snap across 
the room. Starting from the east wall, in a 15-ft. 
cone pointing towards the center of the room, any 
creature not completely obscured by another must 
succeed a Dexterity (DC¬†13) saving throw or take 1d6 
piercing damage and be poisoned until their next 
long rest.
The launchers can be found with a DC¬†13 In-
telligence (Investigation) check, and disabled with 
a further DC¬†9 Sleight of Hand check. Failing the 
check launches the darts. Undoing this mechanism 
leaves the darts open for the taking. The first time 
a dart deals damage it loses its poison and poisons 
the damaged creature if they fail a Constitution 
(DC¬†14) save.
 '
Swinging Block. Directly in the center of the room 
is a single 10-ft. tripwire that can be noticed if a 
PC rolls higher than a 14 on an Intelligence (Inves-
tigation) check. Triggering the trap causes a heavy 
stone block to swing towards the trigger‚Äôs location, 
requiring a DC¬†15 Dexterity saving throw to avoid. 
Failure to do so deals 3d8 bludgeoning damage. 
If the save succeeds, any creature occupying that 
space in the next few seconds must save again or 
take 2d8 bludgeoning damage as the block swings 
back through. This repeats once more, with one less 
damage die.
 '
Arrow Trap. Pointed randomly about the room are 3 
arrow traps. Within their line of fire are numerous 
crossed and web-like triggers. They are obvious, 
intentionally so, painted with bright colors. To navi-
gate their zone of fire PCs must succeed an Dexter-
ity (Acrobatics) or Strength (Athletics) check (DC¬†15). 
No traps have triggers that intersect these as they 
are meant to drive victims into the range of the less 
obvious traps. Failure to avoid the trigger requires 
a DC¬†14 Dexterity saving throw to avoid taking 1d6 
piercing damage. Disarming any of these traps 
requires simply knocking it over.
Tactics: The object of this room is to introduce the 
PCs to the traps of the Region. The bugbears are 
not likely to invite strangers in and this room is 
designed to encourage PCs to find another way 
in. Getting to Room B68, the PCs find it a dead-
end and now have to move across the room again. 
Unless 1d4 hours have passed since they moved 
through this room, the bugbears have not reset 
this trap.
Unlike other trapped rooms in this section, 
there are no dead goblins here. If the PCs enter this 
room from the secret door to the south, it is not as 
important to ‚Äúhurt‚Äù the PCs with this room, since 
they are more than aware of the region‚Äôs dangers. It 
is recommended the PCs feel discouraged, but are 
not killed by this room.
The door to the south leads to a secret door that 
requires a DC¬†17 Intelligence (Investigation) check 
to locate. The secret door is locked, but a simple 
DC¬†15 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check allows the 
PCs to spin the door open on its central axis.
Scaling: To increase the challenge, allow two traps to 
go off at the same time. To decrease the challenge, 
have each trap occur only once.

162
B68. REFUGE
Lined with empty supply racks, this room feels safe 
and secure. Currently, there is nothing in the room 
aside from the empty shelves.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: If the goblins ever overrun the bugbear 
encampments, the bugbears plan to fall back to this 
room. Guarded by the traps in Room B67, they can 
wage a war of attrition against the goblins to the 
very end. They know that if things become this dire 
they are doomed, but they plan on taking as many 
goblins as they can with them.
Encounter Condition: Safe
Tactics: If the PCs admit to the bugbears that they 
have entered the refuge, it shifts their attitude one 
step closer to Hostile. Once Hostile, the bugbears 
attack the PCs on sight in all future encounters, 
having spread the word.
Treasure: There are a few daggers, arrows, and the 
like, but nothing of value. Allow the PCs to resupply 
up to 1d20 arrows, bolts, darts, and 1d6 spears.
Scaling: N/A

163
B69-B91 . THE HOLY GOBLIN EMPIRE
These rooms encompass the might of the goblin em-
pire that has recently been forged by their new king, 
Argliss in the name of their new god.
Musty smells and dampness unknown in the rest 
of the dungeon fill the air here. The traps laid by the 
celestials still work, and the goblins learned long ago 
to avoid the rooms that contain them.
From these rooms, the goblins have unleashed a 
vicious war of conquest and retribution against the 
bugbears and rebel goblin faction. Had the hobgob-
lins not accepted the offer to join Argliss, no doubt 
they too would have felt the goblins‚Äô wrath.
If the PCs have allied themselves with the bugbears 
(Rooms B51-B68), they will have a difficult time con-
cealing their activities from the goblins. The goblins 
are highly suspicious of newcomers and attack any 
on sight. Only a command from their king stays their 
hand. Argliss does not give the PCs free passage if 
he has any reason to believe that the PCs have allied 
themselves with any group other than his fledg-
ling empire.
Bugbears occasionally enter the goblin empire to 
wreak havoc. If the PCs have allied themselves with 
the bugbears and do not assist them here, word gets 
back and any inroads the PCs have with the bugbears 
are shattered.

B69 . THE SENTRIES
Most likely, the goblins spot the PCs long before they 
spot the goblins. If for some reason they do not and 
sneak up on the patrol, read the following.
The hallway stretches before you, a group of 
goblins stands guard. They are strangely well 
organized, and well equipped. Each came with a 
short spear and buckler, methodically patrolling the 
hallway moving about 10 feet in each direction.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: A patrol has been stationed here to 
prevent bugbears from entering the empire by the 
most obvious route. Due to their darkvision, they 
can see enemies coming and due to the darkness 
of the halls, they are more than likely to see PC 
torches. As a result, the six goblin fighters who 
rotate their patrol with the goblins in Room B70 
prepare to ambush the PCs, sending for reinforce-
ments while they wait inside the various nearby 
hiding places.
Encounter Condition: Ambush (darkness), Cover
Tactics: As soon as the goblins spot the PCs, they take 
up defensive positions in the nearby halls, while the 
smallest two run to Room B70 for reinforcements. 
Depending on how the PCs approach, they either 
wait for the PCs to pass (coming from the west) or 
head straight there (coming from the south or east). 
Room B70 is approximately 50 ft. away, and it takes 
one turn for them to make it there, and 3d6 seconds 
for the goblins inside to get their gear together.
These goblins have been trained by the hobgob-
lins. Instead of swarming the PCs, they form up 
into ranks, four goblins abreast. They advance on 
the PCs stabbing the closest with their spears. The 
goblins hold their bucklers facing forward, offering 
more protection (+1 AC) to the goblin on their left. 
The goblins allow the PCs to rush them, fighting 
better close in.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
give the goblins total cover for the first 3 rounds of 
combat. To decrease the challenge, reinforcements 
arrive in double the time.
TACTICS OF THE 
HOLY GOBLIN EMPIRE
Under the guidance of the hobgoblins, 
the goblin forces loyal to Argliss the 
Goblin King are quite formidable. They 
wield short spears & wooden bucklers, 
attacking foes in well-coordinated 
phalanx maneuvers. They advance on 
their enemies with the cold precision 
that has been drilled into them by their 
hobgoblin taskmasters.
The hobgoblins, for their part, have 
formed an effective cavalry unit. 
Mounted on trained worgs, they dart 
in and out of their foes, flanking them 
with rapid attacks. The bugbears and 
rebel goblins have not had success 
against these new tactics. The lightning 
attacks of the hobgoblins, coupled with 
the relentless ones of the foot soldiers 
have proved an effective combination.

165
B70 . FORWARD OUTPOST
If the goblins did not assist the patrol in Room B96, 
read the following.
This long room is an outpost for goblin patrols, 
who are going through the grind of cleaning 
weapons, and so on.
If the goblins did assist the patrol in Room B69, 
read the following.
This long room is an outpost for the goblins. The 
goblin reinforcements spilled out of this room, 
leaving nothing behind. A few hides are laid out 
in precise rows for sleeping. Now empty weapon 
racks rest against the western wall of the room. 
These aren‚Äôt typical chaotic goblins. They are 
well-disciplined.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: If the ten elite goblins in this room did 
not assist the goblin patrol in Room B69, they are 
present. They gather their equipment (requiring a 
turn of not moving) and attack the PCs. If the gob-
lins did assist the patrol, then this room is empty.
Encounter Condition: Cover (soft)
Tactics: These goblins have been trained by hobgob-
lins. Instead of swarming the PCs, they form ranks, 
four goblins abreast, two rows deep. The smallest 
two escape through the north door, to get rein-
forcements from Rooms B71, B72, and B73. Alterna-
tively, they throw javelins from the rear ranks.
They advance stabbing the closest PCs with their 
spears. They hold their bucklers facing forward, of-
fering more protection (increasing the AC by +1) to 
the goblin on their left. They allow the PCs to rush 
them, fighting most effectively in close proximity.
This is not an easy encounter and should be an 
indication of this Section‚Äôs difficulty. These gob-
lins are not pushovers and challenging them may 
be harder than the PCs thought (which is why the 
bugbears have trouble fighting them).
Treasure: 1d20 javelins and 1d6 spears survive the 
battle. If the PCs did not fight the goblins here, 
double the number of weapons found. There are 
also four suits of leather armor (goblin-sized).
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
have Haglar Quickwhip (Room B71) arrive 4d6 sec-
onds later (without the goblins retrieving him). To 
decrease the challenge, remove four goblins.
B71 . HAGLAR QUICKWHIP
The door opens slowly. The air reeks of unpleasant 
odors, but the room itself is laid out neatly. A 
simple cot is placed against the southern wall, 
while a desk with various maps and notes sits near 
the western wall.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Haglar Quickwhip is the taskmaster for 
the forward outpost. He also is in charge of the 
small jail in Rooms B72 and B73. He is a formidable 
opponent and a tireless leader. He trains the gob-
lins constantly. He drives the strong to be strong 
and the weak to grow up or move on. He has no 
patience for those who cannot keep up. Even while 
the patrols sleep, Haglar trains, does push-ups, and 
generally stays alert. He‚Äôs the quintessential elite 
single-minded warrior.
Encounter Condition: Ambush, Concealment, Echoes 
2, Fearless
Tactics: If Haglar hears the PCs coming, he prepares 
for an ambush, attacking from the shadows. Haglar 
stays out of reach of melee combat, deftly using his 
whip to both attack and drive back the PCs. He ma-
neuvers around the room as best as he can, despite 
the limited space. Since he is not above hurting 
those weaker than him, a spellcaster foolish enough 
to expose himself is an easy target.
If forced into melee combat, he disarms the 
nearest PC and uses their weapon or a scimitar 
from his back scabbard (which he wields with two 
hands). Haglar does not call for help until he‚Äôs 
reduced to half hit points or less, at which point the 
patrols in Rooms B69 and B70 are allowed Wisdom 
(Perception) checks to see if they hear him. Due to 
the nature of the walls in this room, the goblins 
suffer disadvantage to their checks.
Treasure: On the desk are notes and maps referring 
to various enemy patrols in this Section. The notes 
are written in a scrawling hand, and succeeding a 
DC¬†22 Intelligence (Investigation) check is necessary 
to make any sense of them.
If deciphered, the notes mention an increase in 
bugbear raids, as well as an ill-fated raid by rebel 
goblins. The last patrol captured a rebel, who is now 
locked in Room B73. The goblin king has ordered 
that the rebel be sacrificed to their god in two days.

166
In addition to his personal possessions, Haglar 
carries a sturdy ring of three keys. One key leads 
to the locked door at Room B72. Another leads to 
Room B73. Finally, the third leads to the worg sta-
bles in Rooms B77 through B82.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase the number of goblins affected by Com-
mander of the King‚Äôs Horde from 1d3 to 1d6. To 
decrease the challenge, lower it to one.
B72 . THE GOBLIN JAIL
The door to this room is locked. A DC¬†17 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand) check picks the door successfully. 
However, there is a 15% chance that the door is also 
barred, requiring a DC¬†18 Strength (Athletics) check 
to break open (DC¬†22 when locked).
Strong chains and manacles hang from the walls 
and a cell is set in the northern wall. Faint, fearful 
moaning issues forth from the cell.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room serves as the detention area 
for anything captured by the goblin patrols in this 
Section of the dungeon. This jail is overseen by 
Haglar Quickwhip (room B71). If the PCs make too 
much noise in this room, allow Haglar a (DC¬†18) 
Wisdom (Perception) check to notice, and arrive 4d4 
seconds later.
Encounter Condition: Drafty
Tactics: The jail is empty. The door to the north is 
sturdier than most but has a patchwork lock cut

B73 . CAPTURED REBEL
The door to this cell is locked, requiring a DC¬†17 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check (or the key from 
Haglar‚Äôs belt) to unlock.
Huddled far in the corner is a frightened goblin. 
He is startled by your presence and yelps when he 
notices you.
Initial Attitude: Friendly
Encounter: This wounded goblin, named G‚Äôlp, was 
part of a failed raiding party on the part of the rebel 
goblin factions. Once he has been assured that the 
patrols, especially Haglar, have been dealt with, he 
blubbers incoherently, attempting to explain the 
current situation and how the usurper who sits on 
the goblin throne has wronged his people.
If the PCs don‚Äôt know what or who Haglar is, he 
assumes the hobgoblin is still alive and cries out for 
help (in goblin), in the hopes of currying favor with 
his jailer. Haglar arrives 1d3 rounds later.
The PCs make out that there is a deep schism 
between the goblins, and the majority of them 
worship a newfound god. The current goblin 
king, who is also the leader of their new religion, 
has formed an alliance with the hobgoblins and 
is training an army to conquer the entire Region 
in the name of his deity. Any goblins that do not 
follow his commands are considered traitors and 
hunted mercilessly. The lucky ones die in combat. 
The unfortunate ones are captured and sacrificed in 
the name of this new god.
Encounter Condition: Stagnant Air
Tactics: If the PCs release him, G‚Äôlp flees the area 
entirely, making his way back to the rebel encamp-
ments on the far side of the Region. If the PCs do 
not release G‚Äôlp, he curses the PCs vehemently, 
invoking the names of every stone spirit he can 
muster. If the PCs welcome him into their party, he 
joins, trying to lead the PCs to the rebels. Oth-
erwise, he is glad to be a ‚Äúpart of the team‚Äù and 
does his best to carry his weight. Whenever the 
PCs enter a room with G‚Äôlp, there is a 35% chance 
that he‚Äôs been here before and knows how to ‚Äúby-
pass‚Äù the room.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: N/A

B74. ANTECHAMBER OF THE GOBLIN KING
If the PCs killed Hammerfist in Room B85, he is not 
present here.
This large, rectangular room (almost a hallway) is 
polished brightly. Eighteen fierce-looking goblins, 
each wielding a spear, stare at you coldly. Behind 
them, a tall, wide-shouldered hobgoblin carries a 
fist-shaped mallet.
If the goblins heard the PCs coming, read this:
With quick precision, they form a tight phalanx 
and move with deadly intent. The hobgoblin rushes 
madly, swinging his mallet with abandon.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: As the PCs enter the antechamber, they 
are attacked by eighteen goblin warriors and the 
captain of the king‚Äôs elite guard, a huge hobgoblin 
named Hammerfist. Because the goblins are train-
ing with Hammerfist, their adrenaline is up and the 
impending fight is just an excuse to cut loose.
After three rounds of combat, Argliss enters 
from Room B75, flanked by two hobgoblin guards. 
If the fight isn‚Äôt going too poorly for his men, he or-
ders his guardsmen to stand down and invites the 
PCs into his throne room. The goblin king is articu-
late and polite, unusual for a goblin of any stature.
THE GOBLIN KING
Some time ago the doppelganger Argliss 
entered the Region. He was amused by the 
goblinoids trapped here. Out of boredom, 
he assumed the guise of a goblin and slowly 
worked his way into the good graces of the 
reigning goblin king, Sug‚Äôkt. Soon he became a 
chief advisor. He relished the role of bringing a 
culture out of the shadows to suit his whims.
When word of the new ‚Äúdeity‚Äù arrived, Argliss 
saw a chance to improve his position amongst 
the goblins. He recently discovered the goblin 
king kept a powerful artifact hidden in his pos-
session. Wanting it for himself, Argliss knew he 
would have to be the goblin king‚Äôs confidante. 
Hoping to ingratiate himself with the goblins, 
he urged the king to embrace this new deity. 
The goblin king was incensed. Sug‚Äôkt felt he 
alone was ruler of the goblins, as decreed by 
the ancient stone spirits his ancestors wor-
shiped. Popular support was behind the new 
deity, however, and Argliss seized his chance to 
advance his position by staging a coup.
He declared Sug‚Äôkt a heretic, sacrificed the 
former king, and claimed the throne in the 
name of the new god of the goblins, Noren-
dithas Stoneshaper the Quickthinking, Smiter 
of Foes. Argliss began his quest to not only 
uncover the hidden artifact, but to establish his 
rule over the entire Region.
Unable to locate the artifact, he enlisted the 
help of a halfling who had entered the Section 
(see The Halfling). Argliss believes that Bartleby 
will return the artifact to him, in exchange for 
the goblin‚Äôs protection and any trinkets he may 
find. While he awaits Bartleby‚Äôs success, he has 
made strides toward ruling the dungeon.
Argliss approached the beleaguered hobgob-
lins, offering them a prime place in his empire. 
Wishing to seek revenge upon the bugbears 
that had tormented them for so long, the hob-
goblins accepted his offer. They now serve as 
elite guards and trainers of the goblin army.
Upon encountering the PCs, Argliss tries to 
ally with them. He feels their power and knows 
they could be very disruptive to his efforts. He 
is willing to assist the PCs in their mission, as 
long as they return the favor and help him wipe 
out the bugbears and rebel faction of goblins.
If the PCs do not accept his offer, all goblins 
loyal to him attack the PCs on sight.
TACTICS
Argliss is not a fighter. In the event of conflict, 
he orders his guards to attack while he runs off. 
Once the battle is engaged he changes shape 
to something inconspicuous and flees the area, 
returning to his throne room.
If Argliss is cornered and cannot escape, he 
uses the rod of wonder and necklace of fireballs 
liberally until he causes enough of a distraction 
that he can flee.

168
If more than five goblins have been slain, how-
ever, he directs the hobgoblins to join him as he 
bars the door and prepares for the PCs. In this case, 
the PCs are in for a tough fight. Additionally, if 
the PCs do not wish to speak with the goblin king, 
the battle continues until either the guards or the 
PCs are dead.
Encounter Condition: Fearless (save for the 
goblin king).
Tactics: These elite goblins are just now starting their 
training with Hammerfist. The others are either 
on patrol or standing guard in another area of 
the dungeon.
In combat, instead of swarming the PCs, they 
form up into ranks, six goblins abreast, three rows 
deep. They advance on the PCs stabbing the closest 
PCs with their spears. They hold their bucklers fac-
ing forward, offering more protection (+1 bonus to 
AC) to the goblin on their left. The goblins allow the 
PCs to rush them, gaining attacks of opportunity as 
the PCs move into their threat range.
Hammerfist on the other hand, hunts the PCs. 
He does not draw attacks of opportunity if he can 
help it, but he does try to push past anyone who 
leaves an opening. Hammerfist, hates clerics and 
targets those openly displaying holy symbols. He is 
also fond of crippling attacks and targets PCs with 
little to no armor when he can.
Treasure: The weapon racks are filled with spears. All 
the spears are small, however, designed for goblins. 
Their size means for creatures larger than small size 
they lose reach and gain thrown (40/80).
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
increase each goblin‚Äôs hit points by +5. To reduce 
the challenge of this encounter remove six goblins.
B75. THRONE ROOM OF THE GOBLIN KING
If the PCs accepted the goblin king‚Äôs offer to negoti-
ate, read the following.
This room is large and opulently decorated. Hides 
from various animals are layered on the floor, while 
others hang as trophies or tapestries from the walls. 
Two large braziers cast a sinister, yet regal glow on 
a throne of bone and stone standing prominently in 
the room, and it is where the goblin king sits.
He wears a bright leather vest and pants. A velvet 
cloak hangs from his shoulders. On his head 
rests a light, silver crown, and he wields a multi-
hued scepter in his left hand. ‚ÄúWelcome friends, 
I am Argliss, King of the Goblins and Voice of 
Norendithas Stoneshaper the Quickthinking, Smiter 
of Foes. The Stoneshaper has brought us together 
for great things I‚Äôm sure. Please, hear what I have to 
say,‚Äù the goblin king intones as you approach him.
If the PCs declined the goblin king‚Äôs offer to parlay, 
or have snuck in, read the following.
The room is large, and well-appointed for goblins 
but without the pomp and circumstance of the 
goblin king, his court, and his guards, it looks like 
any room that‚Äôs been covered in hides. A pair of large 
braziers cast a ruddy glow about the room, playing 
off the brightly polished walls. In the center is a 
throne of rubble and bones, a scepter resting upon it.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent
Encounter: If the PCs choose to continue the bat-
tle in Room B74, this encounter does not happen 
and they are free to explore the room as long as 
they wish.
The goblin king, Argliss, who is interested in the 
PCs‚Äô services, informs them of the new destiny of 
the goblins. Their god, Norendithas Stoneshaper 
the Quickthinking, Smiter of Foes, has finally ar-
rived and promises to lead them to power and glory.
‚ÄúAny who serve the will of the Stoneshaper shall be 
greatly rewarded, in this life and the next!‚Äù the goblin 
king proclaims.
The goblin king only wishes for more patsies 
to serve his whims. Argliss is very good at hiding 
this truth though; only a successful DC¬†24 Wisdom 
(Insight) check lets the PCs know the goblin king is 
being less than truthful.
If the PCs agree to assist the goblin king, he 
tasks them with killing the rebel chieftain Guk 
(Room B95). They must return with proof of his 
death. If they do so, the goblin king welcomes 
them as members of the glorious empire of the 
Stoneshaper.
Once the PCs agree to ally with the goblin king, 
the elite hobgoblin guard files out of the room and 
returns to their barracks (Room B84). Hammerfist 
snarls at the PCs one last time before he too leaves 
and returns to his quarters (Room B85).

169
If the PCs refuse the goblin king‚Äôs offer, he be-
comes enraged. ‚ÄúNone defy the will of the Stone-
shaper!‚Äù he shouts. Hammerfist lets loose with a 
bellowing war cry and is ready to charge the PCs. 
The goblin king halts his advance however and of-
fers the PCs one last chance to see the error of their 
ways and join him.
A second refusal is all it takes. ‚ÄúMay the Stone-
shaper have mercy on your wretched souls,‚Äù the 
goblin king says as Hammerfist and the elite guard 
attack the PCs.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The goblin warriors move on Hammerfist‚Äôs 
command. Instead of swarming the PCs, they form 
up into ranks, six goblins abreast, three rows deep. 
They advance on the PCs, stabbing the closest to 
them with their spears. They hold their bucklers fac-
ing forward, offering more protection (+1 bonus to 
AC) to the goblin on their left. The goblins allow the 
PCs to rush them, gaining attacks of opportunity as 
the PCs move into their threat range.
Hammerfist goes after the weakest PC first, 
targeting spellcasters first. He also has a fond 
hatred for clerics and abuses them at every turn. 
He fights as intelligently as possible, stepping back 
when overwhelmed and taking full advantage of 
prone PCs.
If the goblin king is in danger, he flees to Room 
B74, and from there heads to Room B77. In the 
meantime, he uses his rod of wonder on whatever 
PC presents the biggest threat and his necklace of 
fireballs if too many goblins fall.
Treasure: If the PCs choose not to listen to the goblin 
king, and he is forced to flee, he leaves behind his 
royal scepter (laying on his throne) on a failed DC¬†16 
Intelligence save. The scepter is a rod of wonder.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add three fighter levels to Hammerfist. To reduce 
the challenge of this encounter, remove one fighter 
level from Hammerfist.
B76. PRIVATE ROOM OF THE GOBLIN KING
The door leading to Region A is locked and barred, 
requiring a DC¬†30 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check, 
followed by a DC¬†18 Strength (Athletics) check to 
open. A small chest rests against the door as well, 
making it difficult to open the door all the way.
The doors from Room B75 are also locked and 
require a DC¬†25 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to 
open. In both cases, the goblin king carries keys to 
these doors.
After you dispatch the last of the goblins, you 
enter this room, the private quarters of the goblin 
king, Argliss. The room is very befitting of a king. 
Exquisite hides are piled as a comfortable bed, 
while others adorn the walls as tapestries. A good-
sized strongbox is tucked into the northeastern 
corner of the room.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: If the PCs made an alliance with the gob-
lin king and attempt to enter this room, they are 
warned that it is off-limits. If they persist the goblin 
king calls off the alliance and orders his guards to 
attack the PCs. The goblin king flees before the PCs 
can capture or kill him, returning in 2d6 minutes 
with reinforcements to drive the PCs out.
This room is luxuriously furnished with a thick 
layer of hides forming a comfortable sleeping area 
in the northwestern corner. The walls are decorated 
with tapestries made of similar hides. They depict 
the conquests and glories of the new goblin king 
and his god.
A small chest is situated against the northeast-
ern wall. A DC¬†15 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check 
is required to unlock it. It contains the room‚Äôs trea-
sure (see below).
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: +1 shortsword, +1 leather armor (made for a 
goblin), +1 buckler. It is possible the PCs may wish 
to take the hides as well for their own personal use, 
or for future sales. They are large, made of worg 
hide, and carrying more than one proves to be 
cumbersome.
Scaling: N/A

B77. ENTRANCE TO THE WORG STABLES
The door to this room (leading from the eastern hall) 
is locked, requiring a successful DC¬†19 Dexterrity 
(Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. The door leading 
from Region A is also locked, requiring a DC¬†22 Dex-
terity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock.
Pungent smells and keening wails saturate the air. 
The floor is covered, stained, and scratched. Even 
the walls are not devoid of claw marks. Along the 
southern wall are a series of iron doors, much like 
cell doors. The room quiets for a brief moment, 
then it erupts into loud howls and barks. Whatever 
is in these cells, knows you‚Äôre here.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: These cells are the goblins‚Äô worg sta-
bles, the home of their vicious worg mounts. This 
hallway leads to the ‚Äúcells‚Äô‚Äô where the elite worg 
mounts are kept. The stables themselves are large. 
Most are noisy, except the one at the west end, 
which is deathly quiet. Due to their Scent ability, 
it is nearly impossible for the PCs to surprise the 
worgs in these cells.
Encounter Condition: Distracting Noises, Echoes 2, 
Unhallowed
Tactics: This series of cell doors are sturdy and are all 
locked. The keys to these doors are kept by Haglar 
(B71), the Goblin King‚Äôs (B75) bodyguards, and a 
handful of elite goblins.
The ‚Äúcells‚Äù were used (long ago) to house 
demons, an effect that has caused the worgs to 
become even more bestial than they already were.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: N/A
B78 . WORG STABLE
Four large wolves sleep comfortably in this cell. 
Despite the barking and howling coming from 
other cells, these animals are not as crazed. One 
of the wolves looks up as you enter the room but 
quickly lies back down again.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent
Encounter: These four worgs have just returned from 
a successful patrol and are tired. Although the PCs 
represent a threat, they are satiated from hunting 
and want to rest. The worgs have enough energy to 
defend themselves if the PCs attack them but suffer 
from a level of exhaustion.
Encounter Condition: Fearless, Unhallowed
Tactics: These worgs fight like a typical pack, tripping 
and grounding the weakest PC and then mauling 
them while prone. If a single PC gets separated 
from the party, or the PC attacks too quickly, the 
worgs surround and flank them.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this en-
counter, change the worgs‚Äô initiative roll to 
exactly 1 lower than the highest PC, allowing 
them to ambush the ‚Äúimpulsive PC.‚Äù Alternately, 
add two worgs. To decrease the challenge, re-
move one worg.

B79 . THE BLACK WORG
The barks issuing from this cell are louder than 
from any other cell. With a successful DC¬†17 Wisdom 
(Perception) check, the PCs can discern a single loud 
bark, deeper and more aggressive than any of the 
other cells.
From the darkness, a large black wolf stands at 
least five feet at the shoulder. Its powerful muscles 
ripple under its sleek, black coat. At first, it doesn‚Äôt 
notice you. Suddenly its hackles raise, and it turns, 
snarling. With a mighty howl, it bursts free of its 
meager enclosure and leaps at you.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: A black worg (worg alpha) is stabled here. 
It is twice as large as any other worg in the gob-
lin‚Äôs possession. It is also twice as feral. Worgs may 
have some measure of intelligence, but this one is 
bestial. When the PCs enter the room it breaks free 
of its inadequate holding pen and lunges at the 
nearest one. The PCs have no choice but to defend 
themselves.
Encounter Condition: Ambush, Distracting Noises, 
Echoes 2, Fearless, Unhallowed
Tactics: The black worg attacks like an animal, vicious 
and unrelenting. It uses its trip attack every round, 
taking advantage of weak PCs. It knows no fear and 
does not respond to pain.
Killing the black worg earns the ire of Hammer-
fist (Room B85) should he find out; he was break-
ing in the worg to be his personal mount. There 
is little choice for the PCs in this matter, however, 
and they must deal with Hammerfist‚Äôs wrath. Any 
explanation the PCs offer is not good enough for 
the hobgoblin.
Treasure: The black worg wears a heavy leather collar, 
set with three discolored gems, none of which 
match. The collar is worth 25 gp to a jeweler who 
can salvage the stones.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add two Hit Dice to the black worg. To reduce the 
challenge of this encounter, replace the black worg‚Äôs 
stats with that of a worg.
B80 . FILTHY STABLE
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†25 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock.
A pack of four, miserable-looking wolves, larger 
than normal, are penned up in this stable. Whether 
they are being punished or neglected is difficult to 
say. They growl and snap at you, but otherwise 
remain behind their enclosure.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: Four worgs are being punished for dis-
obeying their riders‚Äô instructions during a recent 
patrol. They do not attack the PCs first but defend 
themselves if provoked. While not chained, they 
lack the ability to open the locked door.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: If a fight ensues, the worgs gang up on 
the weakest PC first followed by other opponents 
without visible metal armor. They concentrate all 
their attacks until the victim is down. Like all pack 
animals, the alpha male delivers the coup de grace 
before the pack moves on to the next PC. If the 
victim fails a DC¬†10 Dexterity saving throw their 
attacks knock creatures they damage prone.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge, add one worg. To 
decrease the challenge, remove one worg.

Like the other holding pens, this stable is shoddily 
constructed. This stable is empty, save for some

Initial Attitude: N/A

B82. THE GOBLIN KING'S MOUNT, THE YETH HOUND
A sleek hound with a dull, black coat and glowing 
cherry-red eyes pads around in the most luxurious 
pen in the stables. This is the mount of the goblin 
king, and the king takes very good care of it. With 
a lazy turn of its head, the yeth hound takes you 
in‚Äîand promptly dismisses you.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent
Encounter: The yeth hound is the pride of the goblin 
king. Serving as his personal mount, it is not only 
effective in combat, but the goblin king considers 
the hound a symbol of his power and divine rule. 
For its part, the yeth hound could care less about 
the PCs. It is confident in its combat abilities and 
knows its master‚Äôs loyal servants are nearby.
The yeth hound only attacks if provoked.
Encounter Condition: Fear 14, Fearless, Unhallowed
Tactics: If the PCs attack the yeth hound, it flees and 
seeks out the goblin king (Room B75), unleashing 
a series of Bay attacks if cornered. If the PCs are 
stunned, the yeth hound slips by, continuing to Bay 
until it has escaped or is killed by the PCs.
Regardless of the outcome, the goblin king 
undoubtedly surmises the PCs killed his mount 
(unless he has yet to meet them, in which case he 
assumes it was bugbear raiders). Any alliance they 
forged is now broken. From this point on, all initial 
attitudes in encounters with the goblin king‚Äôs sol-
diers are considered Hostile.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
have eight goblins arrive after 6d3 seconds to assist 
the yeth hound. To decrease the challenge, reduce 
the yeth hound‚Äôs hit points by -20.
B83. SOUTHWESTERN OUTPOST
If the PCs have allied with the goblin king in Room 
B75, read the following.
This squat, spartan room serves as the 
southwestern most outpost of the goblin empire. 
The dozen goblins in this room stare blankly at you 
as you enter. The goblin king has ordered his army 
to treat you with respect, but these goblins seem 
to be waiting for you to make a misstep; it is quite 
obvious they do not want you here.
If the PCs have not allied with the goblin king in 
Room B75, read the following.
This squat room is an outpost, guarding against 
incursions. Nearly a dozen goblins are messing 
about and get into formation as you enter.
If the goblins are not surprised, read the following.
They await you with their sharp spears pointing 
menacingly in your direction. They form a perfect 
phalanx and advance upon you.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly or Hostile
Encounter: There are twelve goblin warriors stand-
ing guard here in various stages of readiness. If 
surprised, they take a round to form up into ranks. 
If they heard the PCs coming, they are already in 
formation when the door opens, whether the PCs 
are allies or not.
If the PCs formed an alliance with the goblin 
king, the initial attitude of the goblins is Unfriendly. 
They allow the PCs to wander through the barracks 
as long as they do not disturb anything. If the PCs 
take any actions the goblins perceive as a threat, 
their attitude becomes Hostile and they attack.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: In combat, instead of swarming the PCs, they 
form up into ranks, four goblins abreast, three rows 
deep. They advance on the PCS stabbing the closest 
PCs with their spears. They hold their bucklers 
facing forward, offering more protection (+1 AC) to 
the goblin on their left. The goblins allow the PCs to 
rush them.
Two of the goblins are not Fearless and bail at 
the first sign of trouble (e.g., three goblins fall, they 
suffer at least 1 point of damage, overtly powerful 
magic is displayed, etc.). They head for Room B84 
to retrieve reinforcements, taking 4d6 seconds to 
get there and 4d6 seconds to return.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add six goblins. To reduce the challenge of this 
encounter, remove six.

B84. KING'S ELITE GUARD BARRACKS
If the PCs have formed an alliance with the goblin 
king in Room B75, read the following.
These barracks are simple and minimalist. These 
goblins have no requirement for comfort; they are 
hardened soldiers ready to die for their king and 
their god. They stare at you but do not make any 
aggressive moves. The king has granted you his 
protection, and they will not violate his orders.
If the PCs have not formed an alliance with the 
goblin king in Room B75, read the following.
These barracks are simple and minimalist.
If the goblins are not surprised, read the following.
You are confronted by twelve zealous and well-
trained goblins. They form one cohesive unit 
and raise their spears above their heads with a 
massive war cry.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent or Hostile
Encounter: There are twelve elite goblins standing 
guard here in various stages of readiness. If sur-
prised, they take a round to form up into ranks. If 
they heard the PCs coming, they are already in for-
mation when the door opens, whether the PCs are 
allies or not. They gain a +2 to their initiative rolls if 
the PCs make noise before entering.
If the PCs formed an alliance with the goblin 
king, the initial attitude of the goblins is Indifferent. 
They allow the PCs to wander through the barracks 
as long as they do not disturb anything. If the PCs 
take any actions the goblins perceive as a threat, 
their attitude becomes Hostile and they attack.
The room itself is a spartan affair with a weap-
on rack along the western wall and a precise layer 
of sleeping hides on the floor. If the PCs defeated 
the elite guard in Room B74, this room does not 
contain any goblins.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: As soon as the goblins spot the PCs, they take 
up defensive positions in the nearby halls, while the 
smallest two run to Room B86 for reinforcements.
These goblins have been trained by the hobgob-
lins. Instead of swarming the PCs, they form up 
into three ranks, four goblins abreast. They advance 
on the PCs stabbing the closest with their spears. 
The goblins hold their bucklers facing forward, 
offering more protection (+1 to AC) to the goblin on 
their left. The goblins allow the PCs to rush them, 
as they fight more efficiently at close range.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
give each goblin +5 hp. To reduce the challenge, 
remove four goblins.
B85. HAMMERFIST, CAPTAIN OF THE KING'S GUARD
If the PCs have formed an alliance with the goblin 
king in Room B75, read the following.
The large hobgoblin from the king‚Äôs antechamber 
angrily paces back and forth in this room. He 
wields the same fist-shaped club, swinging wildly 
at the room‚Äôs walls. As he notices you, he violently 
spits at the ground. ‚ÄúCome to try and finish what I 
started, have you?‚Äù he taunts.
If the PCs have not formed an alliance with the 
goblin king in Room B75, read the following.
A large hobgoblin angrily paces back and forth in 
this room, he wields a fist-shaped club, swinging 
wildly at the room‚Äôs walls  A feral grin sprouts 
across his scarred face and he turns to face you 
‚ÄúFinally!‚Äù he shouts.
After the PCs have cleared the room of any hostile 
creatures, or if they defeated Hammerfist in Room 
B74, read the following.
Hammerfist‚Äôs room is very spartan. A simple 
sleeping hide lies in a corner of the room. A map 
of the goblin empire is nailed to the southern 
wall. The western wall features a small collection 
of skulls, obviously war trophies the hobgoblin 
claimed from his foes.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: Regardless of the PCs and their relation-
ship with the goblin king, Hammerfist‚Äôs attitude 
towards them is never better than Unfriendly. If 
the PCs killed the black worg in Room B79 (and he 
knows about it), Hammerfist becomes Hostile and 
attacks them, screaming about revenge.

174
As long as Hammerfist is merely Unfriendly 
towards the PCs, he doesn‚Äôt initiate combat against 
them. He does, however, taunt, threaten, and other-
wise provoke them into attacking him. Hammerfist 
does not like the PCs and wishes to see them dead.
Encounter Condition: Fearless, Negative Energy, 
Unhallowed
Tactics: Hammerfist thinks no one is stronger than 
he is. To prove it, he calls the strongest PC out to 
fight one-on-one. He goes toe to toe, never giving 
an inch. Because of his ego, he fights to the death.
If the PCs do not fight fair, neither does he. He 
finishes off unconscious PCs and helpless PCs have 
their fingers and hands broken under his boot or 
with his war club.
While fighting, he shouts obscenities and 
other unsavory things at the PCs but does not 
call for reinforcements. His aggressive and bois-
terous mannerism is sure to unnerve even the 
strongest PCs.
If reinforcements do arrive, it is of their own 
initiative. Hammerfist is immune to the Negative 
Energy in this room.
Treasure: Hammerfist keeps a strongbox. It is un-
locked as no one is foolish enough to tamper with 
his belongings. Inside the box is a sling, a handaxe, 
450 gp, 51 pp, a silver and gold ring with detailed 
filigree, an inlaid design of an owl (600 gp), six 
arrows, four bolts, and two healing potions.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
have the elite goblins in Room B84 arrive 3d6 
seconds later. To decrease the challenge, increase 
Haymaker‚Äôs movement penalty to -30¬†ft., and 
remove the hit die based damage from Maim.
B86. DRILL ROOM
If the PCs have allied with the goblin king in Room 
B75, read the following.
A huge hobgoblin barks commands and mercilessly 
drills a group of goblins. He glances over at you 
but says nothing. You get the distinct impression 
that treaty or no, this hobgoblin is looking for any 
excuse to test his men against your mettle.
If the PCs have not allied with the goblin king in 
Room B75, read the following.
A mighty bellow erupts as you enter this room. ‚ÄòAt 
last! Fresh meat!‚Äù roars a huge hobgoblin wielding 
a wicked great axe. Upon his command, the goblins 
in the room form up and advance on you with 
calculating precision. The hobgoblin, however, 
charges at you with wild abandon.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: There are twelve goblin warriors in various 
stages of training in this room. If surprised, they 
take a round to form into ranks. If they heard the 
PCs coming, they are already in formation when the 
door opens, whether the PCs are allies or not.
If the PCs formed an alliance with the goblin 
king, the initial attitude of the goblins is Indifferent. 
They allow them to wander through the barracks 
as long as they do not disturb anything. If the PCs 
take any actions the goblins perceive as a threat, 
their attitude becomes Hostile and they attack.
Their leader, Goblinbane, is a wicked taskmas-
ter and the chief trainer under the goblin king. 
He earned his name for his brutal methods and 
callous disregard for whoever could not withstand 
the training. As long as the PCs do not disrupt his 
training, he is content to let them watch and learn 
how a true master creates an army.
Of course, if the PCs have not allied with the 
goblin king, Goblinbane and his goblin trainees at-
tack the PCs as soon as they step foot in the room.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: These goblins have been trained by Goblin-
bane. Instead of swarming the PCs, they form up 
into ranks, four goblins abreast, three rows deep. 
They advance on the PCs stabbing the closest with 
their spears. They hold their bucklers facing for-
ward, offering more protection (+1 AC) to the goblin 
on their left. The goblins allow the PCs to rush them 
forming a defensive line of spears.
Goblinbane seeks out the most prominent PC 
and engages them in close combat, swinging his 
powerful greataxe mercilessly. Occasionally Gob-
linbane barks commands to the goblins, adjusting 
their tactics to keep up with the PCs‚Äô movements.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase challenge, goblin warriors from 
Room B83 arrive in 6d6 seconds. To lessen it, re-
move Goblinbane‚Äôs Martial Advantage and lower the 
number affected by the Commander of the King‚Äôs 
Horde to one.

175
B87 . PATROL BARRACKS
If the PCs have allied with the goblin king in Room 
B75, read the following.
This barracks is a long room with simple weapon 
racks and hides on the floor. You are met with some 
cold stares and toothy grimaces but are otherwise 
left alone by the goblins.
If the PCs have not formed an alliance with the 
goblin king in Room B75, read the following.
A patrol, recently returned, stops in their tracks as 
you enter the room. With uncanny precision, they 
return to formation and set their sights on you.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: This room is a holding area. Returning 
patrols rest here before going back out. There is a 
staging area towards the east where the patrols de-
part from. There are twelve goblin warriors stowing 
gear and relaxing. If surprised, they take a round to 
form up into ranks. If they heard the PCs coming, 
they are already in formation when the door opens, 
whether the PCs are allies or not.
If the PCs are allies of the goblin king, the initial 
attitude of the goblins is Indifferent. They allow the 
PCs to wander through the barracks as long as they 
do not disturb anything. If the PCs take any actions 
the goblins perceive as a threat, their attitude be-
comes Hostile and they attack the PCs.
The barracks itself resembles others in the gob-
lin empire. The weapons racks and sleeping hides 
are precisely arranged and the crude map in the 
middle of the room accurately details the goblin 
patrols in this area of the dungeon.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: If the PCs engage the goblins they have to 
deal with reinforcements. After 6d6 seconds, an-
other phalanx of twelve goblin warriors arrive from 
Room B88. Their tactics are identical to the goblins 
already engaged with the PCs, but they attempt to 
flank the PCs currently engaged.
These goblins have been trained by Goblinbane 
(Room B86). Instead of swarming the PCs, they 
form up into three ranks, four goblins abreast. 
They advance on the PCs stabbing the closest with 
their spears. The goblins hold their bucklers facing 
forward, offering more protection (+1 AC) to the 
goblin on their left. The goblins allow the PCs to 
rush them, fighting better close in.
Treasure: The footlockers are filled with personal 
(worthless) trinkets, only valuable to the goblins.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
have the goblin warriors from Room B88 join the 
battle one turn after rolling initiative. To decrease 
the challenge, the goblins from Room B88 arrive 
after 36 seconds.

If the PCs have allied with the goblin king in room

This outpost serves as a forward observation

goblins prepare themselves for their next patrol as 
you enter. Your presence is ignored, as the goblins 
have more pressing concerns. Reports of a large 
upcoming raid are circulating amongst the troops, 
and each wants to be a member of the patrol that 
crushes the rebel scum.
If the PCs have not allied with the goblin king in 
Room B75, read the following.
As you enter this outpost, a dozen bloodthirsty 
goblins turn and face you. They quickly grab their 
weapons and form an impressive phalanx. Their 
spear points drop and they attack.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: This room is a transitional chamber. 
Returning patrols rest here before going back out. 
There is a staging area towards the east where the 
patrols depart from. There are twelve goblin war-
riors stowing gear and relaxing. If surprised, they 
take a round to form up into ranks. If they heard 
the PCs coming, they are already in formation when 
the door opens, whether the PCs are allies or not.

initial attitude of the goblins is Indifferent. They al-
low the PCs to wander through the barracks as long 
as they do not disturb anything. If the PCs take any 
actions the goblins perceive as a threat, their atti-
tude becomes Hostile and they attack the PCs.
The barracks itself is much like the others con-
tained in the goblin empire. The weapons racks and 

176
sleeping hides are arranged precisely and the crude

the goblin patrols in this area of the dungeon.

combat, another phalanx of twelve goblin warriors 
arrive from Room B87. Their tactics are identical to
