B89 . HAUNTED TOMBS
The hallways intersect, again and again. It would 
seem as though a door could appear somewhere. 
But there is none. Just the same clean corridor over 
and over again. And then the realization that the 
silence is heavy hits you. Something is amiss.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: A sense of dread should overcome the 
PCs at this point. Feel free to spook them at ev-
ery turn with shadows and intermittent sounds of 
chains rattling. Have the command, suggestion, and 
cause fear spells be cast on them randomly. Lastly, a 
deep, allip-like moan is sure to scare them straight.
In addition to any other effects going on, there 
is a blanket of silence that pervades the tomb and 
affects the PCs 50% of the time, severely hamper-
ing their ability to communicate and cast spells. 
While there is no noise, treat this as Distracting 
Noises for the purposes of spellcasting.
hAUnTED ToMb ConTEnTs
For every tomb the PCs open, roll on this table:
D20encounter
1A hot wind escapes from the tomb. Drafty.
2
A swarm of rats run past the PCs and out the door. While they are no threat and deal no damage, if 
they run west or south they are sure to find the goblins who send scouts to investigate.
3A small earthquake rumbles through the section. Tremors 15.
4-12Nothing.
13
The tomb is worn by time and falling apart. If the PCs decide to enter despite this it begins to crumble 
and fall inward on them. Any PCs who fail a Dexterity (DC¬†15) saving throw receive 6d4 bludgeoning 
damage as the stone collapses onto them.
14A fire trap (Room B18) has been cast on the threshold to keep grave robbers at bay.
15
The door unseals and a deluge of water pours forth. PCs within 10¬†ft. have their torches doused and 
are soaked.
16
When the threshold is crossed, a spray of darts fly out of the tomb. Any creature not completely 
obscured by another must succeed a Dexterity (DC¬†13) saving throw or take 2d8 piercing damage 
and be poisoned until their next long rest. The trapped tiles can be found with a DC¬†16 Intelligence 
(Investigation) check, and disabled with a further DC¬†16 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand).
17
When the seal on the tomb breaks, centuries of death fumes (a 5th-level cloudkill, spell save DC¬†14) roll 
forth from the tomb.
18The PCs are attacked by 1d3+1 wights.
19The PCs are attacked by 1d4+1 vargouilles. Ambush.
20The PCs are attacked by 1d6+1 ghouls.

177
While the map does not show secret doors, 
there is a way to enter each tomb. The mecha-
nism is complicated and to date, the goblins have 
not found it.
Located at the two-foot-high mark on the north 
wall of each tomb is a small unholy sigil. While each 
is designed differently, the key to opening the tomb 
is through this sigil. There are three different ways 
to open the tomb. One is for a lawful good PC (or 
one you determine sufficiently demonstrates those 
values) to completely trace the entire surface of the 
sigil. Another is to cast knock directly onto the sigil. 
Finally, the PCs can smear the blood of an angel 
into the sigil, covering the surface.
If any of these actions are taken, a 5-ft-by-5-ft 
section of wall slides open and up into the ceiling. 
If the PCs open a tomb, roll on the table in the pre-
vious page to see if they encounter anything:
Encounter Condition: [Ambush], Cursed 3, [Distract-
ing Noises], Drafty, Fear 16, Haunted, Negative 
Energy, [Spell Resistance], Unhallowed
Tactics: Once the tomb is open, the creatures (if 
present) lunge at the PCs. These beasts have been 
entombed for centuries and are eager to escape, 
most likely fighting in a crazed and wild manner. 
The actual details are left up to the GM, but these 
creatures are interested in feeding on the flesh of 
one PC and escaping soon after. Killing them all is 
not possible.
The ghouls attack the lead PCs, the vargouilles 
use their Kiss attack, and the wights swipe at the 
PC with the least armor on. They do not put them-
selves in harm‚Äôs way to get to the PCs but do not let 
the PCs box them in either.
Treasure: None of these creatures were buried with 
treasure, but the GM is welcome to drop a trin-
ket here and there, so the PCs don‚Äôt feel cheated. 
The largest treasure should be no bigger than 
a +1 dagger or a healing potion.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
roll twice per tomb. To decrease the challenge, roll 
once for every 2 tombs opened.
B90 . ABANDONED BARRACKS
The hallway leading to this room is trapped. Allow 
the PCs Wisdom (Perception) checks to notice, but 
since there are four traps in various locations, the GM 
should feel free to use them as they see fit.
 '
Portcullis Trap. When 15 lbs. of weight are applied to 
the pressure plate on either side of the arch a port-
cullis slams down. Creatures underneath are skew-
ered and crushed and must succeed a Dexterity 
saving throw (DC¬†13) or take 2d8 piercing and 2d8 
bludgeoning damage. Additionally, creatures that 
fail to save are pinned underneath, preventing 
movement until freed. Any creature that can lift 
200¬†lbs. of weight can reliably lift the gate 1¬†ft. off 
the ground, with the weight requirement doubling 
for each additional foot of distance desired.
While not subtle, the trap still requires active at-
tention to notice. Once found the plate can simply 
be stepped over, or disabled by wedging it.
 '
Spring-loaded Darts. When the tripwire is pulled a 
spray of darts snap across the hall. Starting from 
the east wall any creature not completely obscured 
by another must succeed a Dexterity (DC¬†13) saving 
throw or take 2d8 piercing damage and be poisoned 
until their next long rest.
The trap holes and tripwire can be found with 
a DC¬†16 Intelligence (Investigation) check, and 
disabled with a further DC¬†16 Dexterity (Sleight 
of Hand). Undoing this mechanism leaves the 
darts open for the taking. The first time a dart 
deals damage it loses its poison and poisons the 
damaged creature if they fail a DC¬†14 Constitution 
saving throw.
 '
Crude Spear Trap. Any PC rolling higher than 12 on 
a Wisdom (Perception) check in the hall easily spots 
the spears. These spears spring forward if the trig-
ger (a weave of wooden poles hidden under a hide 
on the floor, spanning the hall) is activated. Dis-
arming it is as simple as knocking each of the two 
spears over, where their springs engage and disarm 
themselves.
PCs that fail to notice the spears or charge in 
heedlessly and trigger the trap, must succeed a Dex-
terity save (DC¬†15) or receive 1d8 piercing damage.
 '
Tripping Chain. Strung across the path is a thin 
chain. Robust enough to be a tripping hazard, and 
acting as a setup for a much nastier chain. Both 
are simple and crudely concealed (DC¬†11 Wisdom 
(Perception) required to spot). Stepping on the first 
chain will knock the victim prone unless they pass a 
Dexterity or Strength saving throw (DC¬†12), wherein 
they must succeed a second Dexterity saving throw 
(DC¬†14) to take half damage from falling onto the 
spiked chain.

178
Creatures that step onto the spiked chain receive 
2d8 piercing damage as the wicked hooks and 
barbs rend at them. They may also trip from this, 
requiring the same saves as above but done with 
advantage this time. Reduce this damage by 1 for 
every point of AC the creature possesses over 12. 
Creatures that fall onto the chain receive an addi-
tional 1d8 damage for each size category they are 
above small (medium +1d8, large +2d8, huge +3d8).
Outside of adverse circumstances, small and tiny 
creatures are not tall enough to fall onto the spiked 
chain and simply faceplant into the floor.
Disarming the chains requires pulling the inter-
locking pins that keep them taut and tossing them 
aside. No check is needed once spotted. However, 
the mechanism isn‚Äôt completely intuitive. Less 
mechanically inclined PCs might require a suc-
cessful Intelligence (Investigation) (DC¬†10) check to 
understand.
A long wide room stretches before you. Abandoned, 
disheveled, and broken bunks and cots line the 
walls and floor. Someone or something has 
ransacked these chambers. The thick layer of dust 
suggests it was not recently cleaned.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Long ago, the goblins controlled most of 
the Region. Now, with the bugbear raiding parties 
and goblin rebels, it is difficult to control the outly-
ing sections. The hobgoblins convinced the goblin 
king it would be easier to defend a smaller area, and 
pulled back to Room B69 through B88 (hence the 
concentration of manpower in such a small area).
As a result, they often send patrols up here to 
‚Äúcheck things out,‚Äù but the recent ‚Äútossing‚Äù of the 
room has caused them to rethink their strategy. If 
a goblin Random Encounter is rolled in the vicinity 
of Rooms B90 and B91, there is a 50% chance the 
Encounter is ‚ÄúNothing.‚Äù
Encounter Condition: Fearless, Hazardous Footing 14
Tactics: There is nothing here now, but if the PCs 
insist on rummaging through the debris, feel free 
to have a bugbear patrol happen upon them.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add a pit trap (Room B40). To reduce the challenge, 
remove the portcullis trap.
B91 . NORTHEASTERN OUTPOST
This box-like room smells of charcoal and smoke. 
The blackened walls and burned furniture indicate 
only one culprit‚Äîfire. Along the back wall, resting 
on a small ledge, is a red and black urn, apparently 
unscarred by all the chaos.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Another abandoned outpost, this room 
has been set ablaze and sacked several times, leav-
ing the goblins wondering what the bugbears‚Äô true 
tactics are. On the far wall is a small ledge with a red 
and black urn. On its face is written ‚ÄúThe Unnamed 
Law‚Äù in Goblinoid. The bugbears hope that the 
goblins will inspect it or at least assume an import-
ant bugbear was killed. So far no one has fallen for 
it, but should anyone touch the urn, a trap triggers 
and darts fly from the north and south walls.
 '
Spring-loaded darts. When the urn is touched darts 
spray across the room. Starting from the traps‚Äô re-
spective walls any creature not completely obscured 
by another must succeed a Dexterity (DC¬†13) saving 
throw or take 2d8 piercing damage and be poisoned 
until their next long rest. This occurs twice, once for 
the north and once for the south.
The trap-holes and hair trigger beneath the urn 
can be found with a DC¬†16 Intelligence (Investiga-
tion) check, or a Wisdom (Perception) roll over 18 
in the room, and disabled with a DC¬†16 Dexterity 
(Sleight of Hand). Undoing this mechanism leaves 
the darts open for the taking. When used as weap-
ons, the first time a dart deals damage it loses its 
poison and poisons the target if they fail a DC¬†14 
Constitution saving throw.
Encounter Condition: Ambush
Tactics: This room is patrolled by the bugbears often. 
They hope the goblins will believe the room was an 
important outpost and its loss drove them deeper 
into the dungeon, or that an important bugbear 
was killed here. Either way, its presence baffles the 
goblins and sooner or later a patrol will get antsy 
and grab the urn. To add insult to injury, if the trap 
goes off, there is a 25% chance that bugbears from 
Room B66 arrive to investigate in 3d6 rounds.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge, add a loud 
alarm to the trap that guarantees bugbears from 
room¬†B66 investigate. To reduce the challenge, 
lower the Wisdom (Perception) check to 14.

B92 . THE MAZE
No Random Encounters occur inside or near the Maze. Instead, see Special Encounter instructions below.
spECiAl EnCoUnTERs
D20encounter
1
The path is trapped with spring-loaded Darts. When the tripwire is pulled a spray of darts snap across 
the hall. Pick d3 PCs, they must succeed a Dexterity (DC¬†13) saving throw or take 2d8 piercing damage 
and be poisoned until their next long rest. The trap holes and tripwire can be found with a DC¬†16 
Intelligence (Investigation) check, and disabled with a further DC¬†16 Sleight of Hand. Undoing this 
mechanism leaves the darts open for the taking. The first time a dart deals damage it loses its poison 
and poisons the damaged creature if they fail a Constitution (DC¬†14) save.
2
A whittled wooden duckling lies off the path. Touching the duckling soaks the PC and casts lightning 
bolt (spell save DC¬†13) at 3rd level towards them. This happens only once, and dispel magic will remove 
the hostile enchantment without harming the item. Any creature who holds the duckling is rapidly 
soaked, conferring resistance to fire damage and vulnerability to lightning damage while held. 
Dropping the duck dries them off instantly.
3
A glyph of warding (3rd level, explosive, fire) is inscribed in the hallway. Circumventing this takes 
10 minutes.
4
An illusory beast stalks the hallway. The PC that witnesses it first is harried by the phantasmal 
killer spell once every hour, for the next 10 hours or until it is slain. The beast runs but if chased is 
ultimately cornered. It has the stats of a wolf but is resistant to nonmagical damage.
5
A fire trap (Room B18) is cast on a tile in the hallway. It can be spotted with a Wisdom (Perception) 
check roll of 14 or greater. PCs that can sense magic have advantage on this roll. Failure of any party 
member to spot the trap sets it off.
6-12Nothing.
13A dead blink dog lies in the hallway, covered in blood and stinger holes (stirges). Stagnant Air.
14The air is alive with 2d8+1 stirges. The stirges buzz loudly and dart back and forth across the hall.
15
A lone wight wanders the hall, seeking refuge from the infernal maze. As it spots the PCs it lets out a 
blood-curdling scream and attacks.
16
Vines cloak the walls, choking the torchlight and cutting vision in half. Lurking amongst the greenery 
are 2d6 assassin vines lying in wait for unsuspecting prey. Ambush.
17
1d4+1 vargouilles screech and whine as they corner a lone rebel goblin. The goblin is curled up in 
a ball, crying and shrieking, but the vargouilles are too loud. They are enjoying their torment of the 
goblin and suffer disadvantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks to notice the PCs.
18
A group of 2d6+3 goblins stumble across the PCs. These are rebel goblins making a foray into the 
goblin king‚Äôs territory and do not expect to find anyone in the maze. Confused, and unsure of the 
PCs, they do not attack. Their attitude is Friendly unless attacked.
19
One hobgoblin, mounted on a worg, and six goblin warriors hunt for rebel goblins. They are loyal and 
obedient to the goblin king but patrol the maze fearfully. If the PCs have an alliance with the goblin 
king their attitude is Indifferent (unless attacked). Otherwise, their attitude is Hostile.
20
Bartleby (Room B28) races through the maze. He knows the maze is not a safe place to be and he 
appears to be dancing around stone to stone, trying to avoid particular spots in the maze. If the 
PCs work out a deal with Bartleby, he guides them through the maze, cutting in half the number of 
random encounters the PCs must experience. Nonetheless, he does not know the way out and uses 
Survival to look for drafts and other tell-tale signs of an exit.

180
You enter a long, winding tunnel. The walls are 
covered in moss and vines and a pungent stench 
fills the air. Off in the distance, you can hear the 
sounds of various creatures, their echoes playing 
tricks along the snaking corridor.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The maze is a unique feature in the Re-
gion. No groups claim it and most avoid it if possi-
ble. It is a very dangerous, ever-changing trap. The 
bugbears and hobgoblins are smart enough to avoid 
the dangers of the maze, while the goblins have 
developed a number of superstitions regarding it.
The goblin rebels use the maze to their advan-
tage. Situating themselves on the other end of the 
maze, they have a nearly impassable barrier be-
tween them and their rivals. This, coupled with the 
wild passages in the northeast, has allowed them 
to continue their existence in the Region. A few of 
the leaders of these goblins are starting to turn 
their superstitions into a counter-religion. If the 
new god is all-powerful, wouldn‚Äôt he have destroyed 
the maze for his followers? Since he has not, these 
rebel goblins believe the maze is the home of their 
old gods, the spirits in the rock their grandfathers‚Äô 
grandfathers worshiped.
As the PCs make their way through this maze, its 
denizens and a series of traps confront them. Every 
30 minutes spent in Room B92, roll on the Special 
Encounters table, then roll on the second table for 
any special Encounter Conditions.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: Unless treasure is rolled, the maze is empty 
of anything but debris and blood stains.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
roll for a Random Encounter every 15 minutes. To 
decrease the challenge, roll for a Random Encoun-
ter every hour.

B93-B108 . HEATHEN GOBLIN REBELS
Not all goblins fell in love with the new god. A small 
group held tight to the old ways, worshiping the 
power of the rock spirits as their ancestors had done 
for countless centuries before them. Once their king 
had been usurped, these rebellious goblins had no 
choice but to flee.
Fear of persecution overruled their fear of the 
dreaded maze to the east of the goblin lands. The 
goblins fled into its dangerous, confusing hallways 
eluding capture or other unsavory fates. Only two-
thirds of the goblins made it through the maze, but 
that was a far larger number than any of the fleeing 
rebels anticipated.
With the maze between them and their rivals, the 
goblins quickly went to work setting up a new home 
for themselves. They claimed the area in the south-
east corner of the dungeon as their own. The maze 
protects their western flank, while the wild treach-
erous passages to the north provide ample defense 
against raids by the goblin empire.
A chieftain named Guk leads these goblins. While 
not as clever as Argliss, he is smarter than most 
goblins. He is starting to think that the new deity is 
not as powerful as his supporters claim. Why has this 
deity not destroyed the maze? Why were the followers 
of the old ways allowed to escape? Guk believes the 
answer lies with his gods. The stone spirits are watch-
ing over his people and are rewarding their loyalty.
To Guk‚Äôs people the maze is not something to be 
scared of or frightened by; it is the home of their 
gods. They see now they were too ignorant to realize 
it before. Only the unwary are punished for tres-
passing in the home of the gods. Those truly devout 
and loyal can pass through as they wish. The rebels 
have used the maze to their advantage, both for 
protection and as a place from which to strike at the 
usurper‚Äôs empire.
RAnDoM EnCoUnTERs
Roll for a Random Encounter once per hour.
D20encounter
1
The ground is littered with rubble and other 
detritus. Whether a trap caused this, or the 
earthquake that shook the dungeon so long 
ago, is unclear. What is apparent however is 
that the debris makes walking through this 
area very difficult. Hazardous Footing 15.
2-14Nothing.
15
A group of 1d3+1 ethereal marauders are 
exploring the dungeon and chance upon 
the PCs. Their attitude is Indifferent unless 
attacked. The ethereal marauders are curious 
about the PCs, they are used to goblinoids 
but not much else on two legs.
16
A pack of four blink dogs lazily make their 
way through the dungeon. Their attitude is 
Indifferent unless attacked.
17
A patrol of 2d4+2 rebel goblins, led by a 
goblin mounted on a worg, wind their way 
through the dungeon. These goblins are 
rebels, fighting the goblin king‚Äôs forces. 
If the PCs are allied with the goblin king, 
their attitude is Hostile. If the PCs are allied 
with the rebel goblin faction, their attitude 
is Indifferent. Otherwise, their attitude is 
Unfriendly.
18
A hobgoblin, mounted on a wounded worg, 
is being followed by 3d6+3 weary goblins. 
They have been raiding the rebel faction, and 
have suffered casualties. They are wary of an 
ambush and receive advantage on Wisdom 
(Perception) checks.
19
An ear-piercing shriek fills the dungeon as 
a pack of 2d4+1 howlers rounds the corner. 
They have been hunting goblins, but the PCs 
will serve their purpose equally well.
20
Bartleby enters the room just before the PCs 
do. Not wishing to be seen by the meddling 
PCs he ducks behind an outcropping. 
Bartleby receives advantage on Dexterity 
(Stealth) checks. Cover.

B93. THE WATCH ROOM
When the PCs enter Room B93, read the following.
This room is filled with goblins. They stare at you 
blankly for a brief moment, before attacking.
After the PCs have dealt with the goblins, read this:
This room is small and cramped. It contains only 
an empty weapon rack against the eastern wall. 
The rebel goblins use this room as a staging area 
to launch attacks against the goblins in the west.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: The rebel goblins are confused by the 
appearance of the PCs. They were planning a raid 
against the goblin king when the PCs entered the 
room. Thinking the PCs are agents of Argliss, they 
attack the PCs regardless of their true standing with 
the goblin king.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The goblins simply swarm the PCs, attacking 
them en masse. They attack the PCs closest to them 
without regard for their personal safety. They will 
not stop until either the PCs or they are subdued.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add four goblins. To decrease the challenge, remove 
two goblins.
B94 . THE SECRET ENTRANCE
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†25 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock.
This small room is empty. The slate gray walls 
are blank and unadorned. On the far wall hangs 
a banner with a crude goblin sigil on it, perhaps 
defiantly opposing the goblin king.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This secret entrance is the only way into 
the rebel goblins‚Äô new home. The rebel goblin chief-
tain, Guk, guided by the stone spirits, brought his 
people here. While Room B95 serves as their main 
hall, the goblins wisely decided to hide their new 
homes behind this hidden passage. The entrance 
is not guarded so it does not call attention to itself. 
The goblins rely on the dangers of the maze and 
the spiked pit trap (Room B1) in this room to defend 
against serious incursions from their cousins.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: A secret door in the eastern wall leads to 
Room B98. A DC¬†20 Intelligence (Investigation) 
check is required to locate the door‚Äôs latch, which is 
hidden behind the goblin banner. The secret door 
isn‚Äôt locked and opens easily. In the center of the 
room is a pit, carefully disguised to look like stone.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add 10 feet of depth to the spked pit trap. To reduce 
the difficulty, double the amount of temporary hit 
points granted to players caught in the trap.

183
B95. HALL OF THE REBELS
This room is huge and filled with goblins. 
Everywhere you turn you see them. Their cold, hate-
filled eyes stare back at you. A number hiss and 
spit, gripping their spears tighter. Just when you 
think the goblins will attack, a large goblin near the 
back of the room raises a hand and utters a simple 
command. The mass of goblins steps aside, forming 
a perfect aisle from the door to their chieftain.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: This is the main room of the rebel 
goblins. Twenty rebel goblin warriors make their 
home here. From the hall, they meet and plan their 
raids, and the chieftain, Guk, holds what passes for 
his court. It is a simple room without ornamenta-
tion, save for a low, makeshift table in the center of 
the room and a single stool, used by Guk.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: Guk stops the goblins from attacking the PCs 
on sight. The chieftain is curious about them and 
wishes to know if they are in league with the goblin 
king, Argliss (Room B75). If the PCs convince Guk 
they are not allied with Argliss, he grants them safe 
passage through his encampment, provided the 
PCs do not disturb anything.
Guk also tries to enlist the PCs aid in his war 
against Argliss. He believes they have been brought 
to him by his gods. Why else would they be here if 
not to combat the usurper and restore order?
If Guk suspects the PCs of being allied with 
Argliss, he and the other goblins instantly turn 
Hostile and attack the PCs.
Like all rebels, these goblins lack hobgoblin 
training and the complex tactics their cousins use. 
The rebels use standard swarm tactics to over-
whelm and subdue the PCs.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge, add six goblins. To 
decrease the challenge, remove six.
B96 . STOREROOM
Constructed simply of gray stone, this room looks 
mostly like a makeshift storeroom. Dried rushes 
litter the floor, and the weapon racks are filled 
with spears. A few barrels are stacked against one 
wall. The remaining barrels reek of something 
unpleasant.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Located at the end of the hall, this room 
marks the beginning of the hidden goblin encamp-
ment. The rushes strewn around on the floor func-
tion as an early trespassing system. The door to the 
Rebel Barracks (Room B97) is thin, and the sound 
of anyone walking over the rushes alerts the goblins 
stationed there to potential intruders.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: Allow goblins in Room B97 Wisdom (Per-
ception) checks, with advantage if the PCs walk on 
the rushes.
Treasure: A dozen short spears are stacked on 
the weapons rack and the barrels are filled with 
flammable oil.
Scaling: N/A
B97 . REBEL BARRACKS
If the goblins hear the PCs coming from Room B96, 
they fall into a defensive position, adding +4 to their 
initiative checks.
A small barrack houses a few dozen goblins, their 
spears are pointed menacingly in your direction, 
and they look ready to pounce on you at a 
moment‚Äôs notice. One goblin, dressed in a leather 
jerkin, with a badge of office affixed to its front, 
approaches you, demanding to know what you are 
doing here.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: This is the first, and last, line of defense 
the rebel goblins have for their new home. Twelve 
goblins stand guard, at the ready to defend them-
selves from danger. If the PCs can convince the 
goblins they have made a pact with their chief-
tain, Guk, their attitude shifts to Indifferent. If the 
goblins believe the PCs are in league with Argliss‚Äô 
goblins, their attitude shifts to Hostile and they 
immediately attack. If the PCs failed their Dexterity 
(Stealth) checks in Room B96, the goblins attack 
them as soon as they enter the room.
Encounter Condition: Fearless

184
Tactics: Like all rebels, these goblins lack hobgoblin 
training and the complex tactics their cousins use. 
They rely on standard swarm tactics to overwhelm 
and subdue the PCs. If given a chance, they flank a 
PC, but almost as if by accident.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge, add four goblins. 
To decrease the challenge, remove four.
B98 . REBEL ARMORY
Similar to the rest of the rooms in this section of 
the dungeon, this simple room is lined with weapon 
racks. Each rack holds simple, crudely crafted short 
spears. Along the back wall, a single, ornate brass-
and-iron long spear hangs by itself on the wall.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room serves as the main armory for 
the rebel goblins. Like their cousins, they still wield 
traditional spears. The weapon racks are filled with 
numerous spears, as well as an ornate long spear.
This room also contains a secret door on its 
eastern wall, requiring a DC¬†16 Intelligence (Inves-
tigation) check to locate. The door can be opened 
by pressing the top and bottom stones (pressure 
triggers) simultaneously. Goblins usually require a 
‚Äúboost‚Äù to open this door when passing through.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: Aside from two dozen short spears, 
this room contains a masterwork longspear 
(+1 nonmagical spear).
Scaling: N/A
B100 . WEAPONSMITH
This square cell of a room is filled with long, 
straight sticks and bits of stone. In the middle of 
all this is a lone goblin, feverishly working on a new 
short spear. He does not appear to notice you... but 
maybe he does.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent
Encounter: The weaponsmith working here is Kr‚Äôn‚Äôg 
(a normal goblin). As long as the PCs do not dis-
rupt him, they can stay and watch him work. If they 
communicate with him he replies with grunts and 
gestures. He has work to do and cannot be both-
ered. If the rebel goblins see the PCs as enemies, he 
signals an alarm as soon as they enter. He lunges 
at the PCs with a half-made spear. 16 seconds later 
a squad of nine goblins arrive from Room B101 to 
assist the smith.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: Kr‚Äôn‚Äôg defends himself against the PCs to 
the best of his ability, using the half-completed 
masterwork spear he is holding as his weapon. He 
goes on full defense each round, taking the Dodge 
action and waiting for reinforcements. After a few 
turns, Kr‚Äôn‚Äôg assumes reinforcements are on their 
way and fights less defensively. When the rein-
forcements arrive, they use standard rebel goblin 
swarm tactics.
Treasure: The room is filled with the parts to make 
three dozen masterwork spears, but nothing else.
Scaling: To increase the challenge, have 1d4 extra 
goblins arrive in the first round of combat. To 
decrease the challenge, have only five goblins arrive.
B99. SHRINE OF THE STONE SPIRITS
This room is dark and cool. The walls are dark, but 
somehow inviting as well. Scattered, seemingly 
at random, on the floor are a wide variety of 
carved stones.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This room has been set up by Guk (Room 
B95) to honor the stone spirits the rebel goblins 
worship. If the PCs leave the room as they found 
it, they earn a measure of respect with the rebel 
goblins. Any alteration to the room is viewed as a 
crime and any alliance with the rebels is instantly 
terminated. Should word spread of the PCs‚Äô actions, 
all further encounters with the rebels instantly have 
initial attitudes changed to Hostile.
Encounter Condition: Hallowed 2
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: Numerous carved stones line the floor. 
While they are valuable to the goblins, they are 
nearly worthless to anyone else. Argliss (Room B75) 
may find some use for them, however, and is will-
ing to offer a small reward for their retrieval.
Scaling: N/A

185
B101 . MEETING HALL
Wooden benches and tables line the walls and 
fill the room. Ten goblins, previously talking 
boisterously, grow quiet as you enter the room. 
This simply furnished room serves as the goblins‚Äô 
communal room.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: Unwelcome intruders, the PCs earn 
the glare of ten rebel goblin warriors, who have 
stopped their conversation to determine the fate of 
the PCs. As long as the attitude toward the PCs is 
not Hostile (in relation to the rebels), they are left 
alone. The goblins do not speak as long as the PCs 
are around. If the initial attitude toward the PCs 
is Hostile, or if they attack the goblins, the rebels 
assault the PCs immediately.
Encounter Condition: Fearless
Tactics: These goblins have not been trained by 
the hobgoblins and do not have a handle on the 
complex tactics their cousins do. They fight with 
conviction (gaining +2 to Wisdom saving throws) 
but lack the tactical acumen of the goblins from 
the previous Section. The rebels swarm tactics and 
overwhelm the PCs, in an attempt to subdue them 
and hold them hostage.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encoun-
ter, add four goblins. To decrease the challenge, 
remove four.
B102 . CROWDED WORG STABLE
Growls, snapping jaws, and the stink of live 
animals, saturate the air. Four large, shaggy beasts 
are confined behind shaky-looking wooden pens. 
The wooden slats strain and buckle as the worgs 
try to free themselves. How the goblins ride these 
monsters into battle is unimaginable; the thought 
of taming them seems laughable enough.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Inside the pens, chained to the walls, are 
four worgs. They are vicious animals, slowly being 
turned mad by the Fear in this room. The goblins 
have placed them here, unsure why their tempera-
ment is so chaotic, but remain unwilling to relocate.
Encounter Condition: Fear 14, Fearless
Tactics: Since the worgs are chained up, it‚Äôs an easy 
kill if the PCs want to finish them. If the PCs get too 
close, the worgs attack. They cannot coordinate their 
attacks, however, and snap at anything in range.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
unchain the worgs. To decrease the challenge, have 
the worgs sleeping.
B103 . EMPTY WORG STABLE
The empty stable is devoid of anything of use 
to you. Hay bales line the wall and the floor 
is scattered with debris. The air is heavy and 
oppressive.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Whether it was the death of a beast that 
lived here, or something else, the air in this room is 
impossible to breathe. The smell is foul and oppres-
sive, stinging the PCs‚Äô eyes.
Encounter Condition: Negative Energy, Stagnant Air
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: If the PCs brave the odor and search the 
room, allow DC¬†15 Intelligence (Investigation) 
checks to find a +1 silver dagger.
Scaling: N/A
B104 . SECRET PASSAGE
This room contains a secret door on both its east-
ern and western walls, requiring a successful DC¬†17 
Intelligence (Investigation) check to locate. The doors 
can be opened by pressing the top and bottom stones 
(pressure triggers) at the same time. Goblins usu-
ally require a ‚Äúboost‚Äù to open this door when pass-
ing through.
The door on the eastern wall has a stack of barrels 
behind it, in the hopes of barring entry. A DC¬†14 
Athletics check is required to push it open from 
the outside.
This long, narrow corridor stretches along the 
southern end of the rebel encampment. From 
what you can tell it simply leads from one end to 
the other.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This passage is used frequently by the 
goblins, but is often kept locked or barred because 

186
whatever is living in Region C should be avoided. 
The goblins spent a great deal of time digging up 
stones and adding a spiked pit trap (Room B1) in the

Tactics: N/A
Treasure: N/A

B105 . REMEMBERER'S HOVEL
Quaintly appointed, for a goblin‚Äôs home, this room 
is the most impressive in the encampment. The 
floor is covered with a rug made of some animal‚Äôs 
hide. Small carvings and markings adorn the walls. 
In the middle of the room sits a very old goblin. His 
skin is dull, leathery, and spotted.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent
Encounter: This room is the living quarters of the 
oldest goblin in the rebel faction. His name is 
Rememberer, and at nearly 15 years old, he is an-
cient. He is the last repository of the goblin culture 
before the coming of the new god. He remembers 
the stories and ways of his people, and gladly tells 
the PCs what he knows, hoping to find an heir for 
his knowledge before he passes into the rock. The 
PCs can learn much of the history of the goblins 
from the Rememberer. As long as the initial attitude 
does not shift to Hostile or the PCs threaten the 
Rememberer, he imparts his knowledge.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The Rememberer is quite old, and in no 
condition to fight off the PCs. Instead of fighting, 
he begins singing a song to fascinate the PCs. Allow 
the goblins in Room B101 a Wisdom (Perception) 
check each turn to hear the song. If they succeed, 
they arrive in 6d6 seconds to aid the Rememberer, 
fighting the PCs as if they had just harmed a goblin 
child. Once reinforcements arrive, they draw the 
PCs away from the Rememberer, allowing him to 
escape the room. Once safe, he flees to Room B95, 
while the goblins lead the PCs towards Room B97. 
If forced to remain in the room, the Rememberer 
aids the fighting goblins in battle. If he must escape 
he casts, expeditious retreat, and then pass without 
trace to disguise the direction he ran in.
Treasure: The Rememberer is familiar with the oral 
histones of his people. In addition, he wears a coral 
necklace (the origins of which are unknown to him) 
worth 50 gp. It is actually an Amulet of Proof against 
Detection and Location, but he doesn‚Äôt know that, 
because it doesn‚Äôt radiate magic.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
the reinforcements arrive at the end of the Remem-
berer‚Äôs first turn. To decrease the challenge, the 
reinforcements arrive at the end of the Remember-
er‚Äôs third turn.
B106 . THE REBEL CHIRURGEON
This room is a grisly mess. A few forlorn cots line 
the back wall. The lumpy shapes under the rotten 
cloth blankets leave little to the imagination. In 
the center of the room, standing over the lifeless 
body of a goblin, is the rebel‚Äôs chirurgeon, sewing 
together what is left of the dead soldier.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: The goblin chirurgeon has just per-
formed surgery on a rebel goblin, to no avail. 
While Guk (Room B95) calls upon the power of the 
stone spirits, he‚Äôs not adept at healing. This young 
goblin chirurgeon has been tasked with fixing the 
raiders that return to the encampment, which is 
becoming more and more of a losing proposition. 
He is frightened and skittish and does not like the 
presence of the PCs one bit. Black, his bat familiar, 
is here too.
If attacked the chirurgeon flees, crying for help. 
If he alerts the guards housed in Room B97, they 
arrive a turn later.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: The chirurgeon does everything in his power 
to escape the PCs. While he has a few spells at his 
disposal, he casts burning hands if cornered and 
sleep if he sees someone casting spells. Once the 
guards arrive they assist the chirurgeon and attack 
the PCs. Like all rebels, these goblins lack hobgob-
lin training and the complex tactics their cousins 
use. The rebels use standard swarm tactics to over-
whelm and subdue the PCs. They guard the adept 
as best as they can, and look menacing if necessary.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge, add four goblins. 
To decrease the challenge, remove four goblins.

187
B107. GUK'S QUARTERS
Large and empty, this room is much nicer than 
others in the area. While spartan, a large sleeping 
area has been made up in the middle of the 
room, and various hides and weapons cover 
the walls. Leaning against the back wall is a 
club, with a wicked-looking spike of iron driven 
through its head.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Guk (Room B95) and the majority of 
rebels, aside from those in the secret encampment, 
are still in Room B95. If the PCs have gotten this far 
they either have Guk‚Äôs trust, or the PCs have already 
dealt with the rebel chieftain.
The hides and weapons on the walls are testa-
ments to the goblin kings of the past. They are all 
Guk could smuggle out during his exodus from 
Argliss‚Äô regime. Guk‚Äôs personal greatclub is here; he 
does not feel he needs to wield it in the safety of his 
own hall and leaves it in this room when he is not 
raiding his cousins to the west.
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: If the PCs have somehow yet to meet Guk, 
there is a 50% chance he is here alone, and startled 
to find strangers in his quarters. His initial attitude 
is Unfriendly, as he does not trust foreigners.
Treasure: Guk‚Äôs +1 greatclub is the only significant 
treasure in the room. The weapons on the walls are 
standard spears and short swords. They are all old 
and rusty, however.
Scaling: N/A
B108. REBEL GUARD ROOM
This room, like many in this area, is filled with 
spear-wielding goblins. Along the north wall is a 
weapon rack filled with sharpened wooden spears 
and javelins. Apparently nothing has threatened 
them recently, as they look quite bored and eager 
for a fight.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: This room is staffed by ten of Guk‚Äôs 
goblin warriors. They monitor the northern passag-
es for incursions by the goblin king‚Äôs forces. Occa-
sionally they hunt the creatures that wander into 
these halls from the untamed rooms (Rooms B109 
through B131).
Encounter Condition: N/A
Tactics: These goblins are bored and agitated with 
their assignment. They are looking for anything 
distracting. If their attitude with the PCs is anything 
but Hostile, they strike up a conversation (in Goblin) 
or offer to play knucklebones or cards. If the PCs 
have Guk‚Äôs favor, they even offer them places to sit 
and relax, eager for company.
If the attitude is currently Hostile, the rebel 
goblins tear into the PCs, fighting with a fierceness 
they have not seen in goblins. Treat the goblins as 
enraged (per the barbarian rage class ability) and 
give them a +2 to their initiative.
Like all rebels, these goblins have not been 
trained by the hobgoblins and do not have the 
complex tactics their cousins do. However, they are 
fond of flanking and poking the PCs at every turn. 
One of them has a vial of acid and another one has 
dragon bile smeared on his blade (3 doses). Any 
goblin that cannot get in to fight the PCs, throws a 
spear (increase their ‚Äúshortbow‚Äù damage to 1d8 to 
represent this) overhead in an attempt to harm PC 
spellcasters and those hanging back. They move to 
the weapon‚Äôs rack to retrieve more if necessary.
Treasure: There are three spears and three javelins for 
every goblin in a weapons rack along the north wall. 
It requires a bonus action to grab one. Large or 
larger creatures can grab two in one go.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add four goblins. To decrease the challenge, remove 
four goblins.

188
B109-B119 . THE UNTAMED ROOMS
None of the goblinoid races lay claim to this rub-
ble-filled expanse. The earthquake hit this part of 
the dungeon hardest. A number of the traps orig-
inally laid down have been destroyed. Blink dogs, 
dire wolves, howlers, and other monsters make their 
home in this rough expanse. Howls, high-pitched 
whining, and growls echo throughout the hallways.
The hallways are strewn with rubble and debris. 
Most of the rubble is the facing of the walls that came 
loose. Some of it is the remains of walls. The footing 
is treacherous and the wild monsters make the area 
dangerous. There are good reasons the goblinoids 
have not settled the area previously.
With the shrine to their new deity in the northeast-
ern section of this expanse, Argliss and his goblins be-
gan entering the area more frequently. They even set 
up a way station for pilgrims and scouts to stay during 
the arduous trip from their empire to the shrine.
The bugbears have used the long, dangerous trip 
of the goblins to their advantage. They too have set 
up a small bivouac. From it, they harass the goblin 
pilgrims and scouts. Their presence, coupled with the 
naturally wild monsters, makes this perhaps the most 
volatile area in the entire Region.
Each room is assumed to have Poor Footing 3 in 
addition to any other Encounter Conditions.
RAnDoM EnCoUnTERs
Roll for a Random Encounter once per hour.
D20encounter
1
The PCs have walked into an area that is pitch black. The air is oppressive and a chill runs up the 
spines of the PCs. Deep Darkness, Fear 14.
2
Shadows jump across the hallway. The briefest of movement plays just at the corner of the PC‚Äôs vision. 
Exactly what it is may not be evident, however. Distracting Visions.
3
Something is not right about the expanse ahead. The lead PC is convinced it is a perfect spot for an 
ambush (whether or not this is true is up to the GM). Cursed 4.
4-10Nothing.
11
A dire wolf stalks the halls. This room is strewn with debris; damage from the earthquake. The wolf 
lies in wait for the PCs, attacking when they are in range. Ambush, Cover.
12
Two ethereal marauders investigate this room. Rubble and broken bits of some ancient trap cover 
the floor and the marauders are digging through them. They suffer disadvantage on Wisdom 
(Perception) checks.
13
Hovering over three goblin corpses is a lone howler. Since the goblins were not a challenge, the 
howler unleashes its fury on the PCs. Fearless.
14
A pack of three blink dogs moves slowly through the hall. They are wounded (-5 hp), having just 
concluded an encounter with dire wolves. Unfriendly unless attacked.
15
A pack of four dire wolves limp along. They are wounded (-10 hp), having just fought a rival pack of 
blink dogs They are on the alert for any attack, despite their wounds. Ambush.
16
A goblin hunting party is engaged in a fight with a pair of vargouilles. Seven goblins remain‚Äîthe 
corpses of five of their compatriots clog the battlefield. The goblins and vargouilles are too distracted 
to notice the PCs. They suffer disadvantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks.
17
Three wights lurk in the halls, searching for easy prey. They encounter the PCs in this rubble-strewn, 
dark room, attacking the PCs from the safety of the shadows. Ambush, Concealment, Cover.
18
A pit trap (Room B40) has been constructed in the path the PCs are taking. Should they decide to 
avoid the trap, it takes 30 minutes to find a path around.

Bartleby stands over the corpse of a dire wolf. He is fatigued from the encounter. Reduce Bartleby‚Äôs 
hp by 10. He does not ask the PCs for assistance and leaves as soon as he spots them.

B109. PASSAGES OF DEATH
The door on the northern wall is open. Rubble and 
broken, armored skeletons, and other detritus litter 
the hall. Ominous sounds emanate from the west 
of the room, echoing off the cavernous walls. To the 
east is a small passage leading away into darkness.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: When the demon Falortuligo broke from 
its prison in Room C21, he broke into Region B 
through the doors here and finally into Room B111 
where he was killed. The skeletons are a few of the 
paladins who died fighting him.
Encounter Condition: Distracting Noises, Haunted, 
Hazardous Footing 15, Unhallowed
Tactics: Just being here should unnerve the PCs. 
The sights, sounds, and sensations of these dead 
soldiers combine to create an aura of uneasy death. 
These men died horribly. Close examination of the 
bodies shows parts of bone missing from the ribs, 
legs, jaws, and arms as if some great force tore 
them away before they died.
Treasure: There are a total of three skeletons, each 
wearing a +1 chain shirt, with masterwork long-
swords (+1 nonmagical longswords) on their belts, 
and tabards of the Order of Myrunn still hanging 
on their broken frames. One of the bodies wears a 
generic signet ring (with a cross) that can double as 
a silver holy symbol, should a PC require one.
Scaling: N/A
B110. FRIGHTENED AND ALONE
The northern door to this room is locked, requiring a 
DC¬†24 Dexterity (Thieves‚Äô Tools) check to unlock. The 
southeastern door to this room is locked, requiring a 
DC¬†27 Dexterity (Thieves‚Äô Tools) check to unlock.
Unless the PCs succeed at a DC¬†25 Dexterity 
(Stealth) check while opening the lock, read the 
following.
Sitting in the corner of this dark and empty room 
is a single goblin. His eyes are streaked with tears 
as he shakes fearfully, barely managing to hold a 
sharpened stick to defend himself.
If the PCs succeed in picking the lock quietly, read 
the following.
The room is dark and empty. In one of the comers, 
a single goblin whimpers and cries to himself. His 
hands tremble as he stares at the sharpened stick 
in his hand.
Initial Attitude: Indifferent
Encounter: This rebel goblin, Klibb (a normal, if 
somewhat pathetic goblin possessing an above-av-
erage Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) of +6), has been 
locked inside this room for 3 days. Fearing whatever 
is in Room B111, he locked himself in this room. 
However, in doing so, he broke off his pick in one 
of the locks and has been unable to escape. To 
make matters worse, the room is haunted and he‚Äôs 
been unable to sleep with the noises, chattering, 
and unexplained shadows hovering around him all 
night long. He‚Äôs down to one last candle for light 
but refuses to use it for fear that he may be in this 
room for a long while yet.
Encounter Condition: Haunted
Tactics: Klibb does not want to fight and gladly 
throws himself at the mercy of the PCs. If they in-
tend to kill him he greets death willingly, though if 
they leave an opening for escape he takes it. If they 
offer to let him join, he gladly accepts and escorts 
them wherever they want to go.
This is a perfect opportunity to drop a new PC 
into the group. If a goblin is not on the menu of 
acceptable races for players, replace Klibb with just 
about anything that fits, including an elf deserter 
from Region H. It makes the most sense for Klibb 
(or his replacement) to be a rogue, but if another 
goblin lies dead in the room who actually locked 
the doors from the inside, Klibb can be any class.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: Do not increase or decrease the challenge of 
this encounter.

190
B111. KILLING GROUNDS
This room is evil; you can feel it in your bones. 
The floor is covered in debris and is slightly tacky. 
Any sound you make, as well as a few others, echo 
throughout the chamber loudly. To say you have 
a bad feeling about this cavernous room is an 
understatement.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: This is perhaps the most dangerous room 
in the entire Region. An epic battle took place here 
ages ago (see Region C) and the effects of the battle 
still linger. The conditions of the room are tough 
to handle, but that is not the worst of it. Soon 
after the PCs enter the room, six corrupted ghoul 
paladins‚Äîdressed in magical chain mail, carry-
ing unholy swords, and wearing the tabards of the 
Order of Myrunn‚Äîattack the PCs. They are fearless 
and descend without hesitation, merely waiting for 
the appropriate moment to strike.
They do not look like typical ghouls. While their 
skin is tight, eyes hollow, and claws sharpened to 
razor-like perfection, they carry themselves with re-
gal authority and wield swords as though they were 
born to. Their helmets hide everything but their 
fangs and empty eyes. Their weapons gleam with 
unnerving energy.
Encounter Condition: Ambush, Concealment, Cursed 
5, Desecration 6, Echoes 10, Fear 14, Fearless, 
Haunted, Hazardous Footing 16, Negative Energy, 
Unhallowed
Tactics: The ghouls alternate between bite, claw, and 
longsword attacks. They know that a paralyzed vic-
tim is easier to subdue, but they cannot deny their 
paladin heritage. They maintain an aura of fear, in 
addition to the Fear effect of the room.
The ghouls work like a team, ganging up on 
stragglers and distracting the weak. They have a 
strong hatred for clerics and wizards (seeing Arum 
as the cause of their death). They do not put them-
selves in harm‚Äôs way but do their best to kill spell-
casters before they can ‚Äúboost‚Äù the PCs.
If the PCs cannot dispatch the ghouls quickly 
enough, they run the risk of drawing the atten-
tion of other nearby monsters. After 11 rounds of 
combat, roll for a Random Encounter. If the result 
is odd, the Random Encounter occurs, forcing the 
PCs to deal with even more foes. If not, roll again 
on the 12th round of combat. If the result is even, 
the Random Encounter occurs. Do not roll for fur-
ther encounters beyond this point.
Treasure: Having rotted their magical weapons and 
armor from their caustic and unholy touch, their 
swords and chain shirts turn to dust when the 
ghouls die.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one corrupted paladin. To decrease the chal-
lenge, remove the magical arms and armor from 
the corrupted paladins.

B112-B115 . PRISON CELLS
While part and parcel of the surrounding Section, these four rooms have specific significance. They are prison 
cells that at one time or another held demons, devils, and undead. Some of the rooms still have occupants
B112 . DARKNESS AGAIN
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†25 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. Unlike 
the other rooms in this area, the glyph on this door 
triggers the door to open when read.
This simple room is empty and dark. Light recedes 
and dissipates, almost swallowed by the darkness. 
The floor, from what you can see, is strangely 
free of dust.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Whatever once lived here is gone, having 
escaped when a foolish goblin read the glyph on the 
door. Most likely a wight, it either escaped into the 
dungeon or was killed by the ghouls in Room B111.
Encounter Condition: Deep Darkness, Desecration 3, 
Negative Energy
Tactics: N/A
Treasure: If the PCs spend 30 minutes searching the 
room (and have adequate light), allow a DC¬†20 In-
telligence (Investigation) check to find a loose stone 
in the floor. A DC¬†11 Strength (Athletics) check lifts 
the stone from its perch. The stone is nearly 200 
lbs. and covers a small area the size of a halfling. 
Buried under the stone is a suit of +1 unholy splint 
mail, obviously hidden away so it could never be 
used against the forces of good. It radiates evil and 
afflicts good-aligned PCs who don it with a Har-
rowing Curse.
Unholy armor grants resistance to damage 
dealt by good-aligned creatures. In addition, when 
the wearer is struck, the attacker must succeed a 
Charisma saving throw (DC¬†14) or be afflicted with a 
Harrowing Curse.
 '
Harrowing Curse. Until it is removed, or one week 
passes, cursed creatures that roll initiative must 
succeed a Wisdom saving throw (DC¬†14) or be 
frightened of all undead for 10 turns. The save may 
be repeated at the end of each of their turns. Crea-
tures already in combat when this curse is applied 
must immediately make the save again.
Scaling: N/A
B113 . TRAPPED WIGHT
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†24 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. In ad-
dition, the door is trapped with a glyph of warding, 
protecting the contents of the room from escape. 
Tampering with the door or lock in any manner 
triggers it.
A small tomb-like room rests to the northeast of 
the large circular room. The contents are spartan 
and darkness extends to every comer. Before you 
can think, something has crept from the shadows.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Two insane wights have been trapped in 
this room since its creation. Being undead, they 
do not understand the passage of time as humans 
do but nonetheless have maintained a semblance 
of reality that finally drove them mad. Insane, they 
howl with an allip-like moan.
Encounter Condition: Ambush (darkness), Distract-
ing Noises, Fear 15, Fearless, Unhallowed
Tactics: The insane wights attack immediately, taking 
advantage of surprised PCs. They babble incessant-
ly, as they attack each PC in turn.
Treasure: If the PCs have adequate light, allow a 
DC¬†20 Intelligence (Investigation) check to find a 
series of loose flagstones in the floor. Buried under 
the stones is a +1 unholy morningstar, obviously 
hidden away so it could never be used against the 
forces of good. A DC¬†10 Strength (Athletics) check 
lifts the stones.
Unholy weapons deal an extra 1d4 necrotic dam-
age to good-aligned creatures. In addition, when a 
creature is struck by the weapon, it must succeed a 
Charisma save (DC¬†14) or be afflicted with a Har-
rowing Curse (Room 112). Good-aligned creatures 
touching unholy weapons are instantly afflicted 
with the curse.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one wight. To decrease the challenge, remove 
the allip-like babbling ability from the wights.

and all the doors are locked and guarded by glyphs. GMs can describe the doors while the PCs stand in 
Room¬†B111, but until they touch them, there is no chance of knowing what will happen.
B114 . HELL ON EVERY EARTH
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†25 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. In addi-
tion, the door is trapped with a glyph of warding (3rd 
level, explosive, thunder), protecting the contents of 
the room from escape. Tampering with the door or 
lock in any manner triggers it.
From the darkness, you can hear an unhealthy 
moan, something sinister and decrepit. The 
darkness cuts your torchlight and the moan grows 
louder as you peer into the shadows.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: A ghast of unusual strength has been 
trapped in this room since the dungeon‚Äôs creation. 
Once shackled, it broke those bonds long ago. Now 
the manacles and chains hang from a metal ring in 
the wall. The floor is littered with sepsis and slime, 
making walking difficult.
The ghast has no love of the living and attacks 
immediately.
Encounter Condition: Ambush (darkness), Conceal-
ment, Fearless, Poor Footing 4, Unhallowed
Tactics: Taking advantage of the darkness, the ghast 
rushes the first PC, in an attempt to pin him. Using 
the darkness to his advantage he gains a +4 to 
his Strength check to grapple them. Once on the 
ground, he attacks ferociously, biting and clawing 
until the victim is paralyzed. He then moves on to 
the next victim using the same tactics, paralyzing 
the PC and moving on to the next.
The ghast is a fearsome predator and uses its 
mechanisms to finish off the PCs.
Treasure: If the PCs spend 30 minutes searching the 
room (and have adequate light), they can find a bro-
ken stone in the floor. A DC¬†9 Strength (Athletics) 
check lifts the pieces of broken stone easily. Noth-
ing is buried here, having been taken by the ghast.
Scaling: To increase the challenge, give the ghast +3 
AC. To reduce the challenge, remove the ghast‚Äôs 
teeth, forcing it to fight only with its claws.
B115 . SEVERED VARGOUILLES
From outside the door, the PCs can hear the muf-
fled shriek of something far off. In actuality, the 
vargouilles inside are shrieking at a fever pitch, but 
the walls of the dungeon suppress the volume of 
their screams. As soon as the door is opened, the 
shriek hits them at full volume.
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†25 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. In addi-
tion, the door is trapped with a glyph of warding (3rd 
level, explosive, fire), preventing the contents of the 
room from escaping. Tampering with the door or lock 
in any manner triggers it.
As soon as the door opens a feverish shriek 
blasts your senses, striking your psyche with an 
impossibly loud sound. The room, shrouded in 
darkness, shows no signs of occupants, but the 
shrieks cannot be ignored.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: From the darkness, four vargouilles shriek 
and scream. The PCs cannot see them because it‚Äôs 
dark, but if they can get closer, they see four heads 
spiked to iron rods in the wall, some ten feet above 
the floor. Striking them should be easy enough, 
should the PCs have a weapon that can reach them.
Encounter Condition: Concealment, Distracting 
Noises, Deep Darkness, Fear 14
Tactics: The vargouilles are spiked to the walls, un-
able to move, but unwilling to die. They have been 
shrieking for thousands of years, trapped in this 
constant state of agony. Unable to deny their un-
holy heritage, they scream continuously, no matter 
what the PCs do. They cannot move, and want noth-
ing more than to be free of this living hell they are 
trapped in. Death is the most obvious answer, but 
escape is their goal.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge, do not have the 
vargouilles spiked to the wall but flying about at 
will. To decrease the challenge, reduce each var-
gouille to 1 hit point each, representing the con-
stant state of near death that they ‚Äúlive‚Äù in.

B116 . ISOLATED REBELS
As the PCs approach this room, allow Wisdom 
(Perception) checks to overhear the goblins inside, 
counting and bickering. While not hostile toward 
one another, or shouting, they are busy dividing up 
their loot.
There is a 50% chance one goblin stands guard in 
front of the door. Otherwise, everyone is inside, with 
one goblin watching the door from the back wall.
This small, cramped room is filled with rebel goblin 
warriors, sitting down and sifting through a small 
pile of coins and gems. Before you can do anything, 
they grab their spears and attack.
Initial Attitude: Hostile
Encounter: Nine goblin warriors left Room B108 out 
of boredom. Wishing to explore the dungeon, they 
braved the maze, snuck passed the goblins in Room 
B86 and so on, and made their way through the 
trapped rooms in the center of the Region.
None of this was difficult, but the goblin keeping 
track of where they were going died under a port-
cullis trap and they have been stuck in this Section 
for weeks now. The other goblins in the rebel en-
campment presume they are dead. Since they have 
been gone for so long, they do not know whether 
the PCs are loyal to the rebels or not. As such, they 
are treated no better than their traitorous cousins. 
Unless the PCs can show some sign of their alle-
giance to the rebel goblins (and quickly), they are 
attacked as soon as the PCs enter the room.
Encounter Condition: Distracting Noises
Tactics: These goblins are ragged and frazzled, their 
mental state shaken for the duration of this fight. 
They attack with an intense need to kill. The PCs 
should be allowed a chance to calm them down 
(spells work, for instance). If 50% of the goblins 
come to their senses, they all stop fighting and in-
vite the PCs in, hoping they can guide them home.
The goblins have encountered the blink dogs in 
Room B117 but keep to themselves, knowing better 
than to antagonize the beasts.
Treasure: While exploring, they were able to collect 
a small pile of treasure that they were divvying up 
(for the 40th time) when the PCs interrupted. There 
are 116 sp, 23 gp, an uncut sapphire (350 gp), and a 
potion of gaseous form.
Scaling: To increase the challenge, add three goblins. 
To decrease the challenge, remove two.
B117 . BLINK DOG DEN
The door to this room is open, its lock broken.
In the midst of all the chaos in this section of 
the dungeon, this room feels safe. An easy calm 
washes over you and the room itself seems to be 
an enticing place to rest. The peace is broken as a 
series of low growls fill the air.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: The PCs have entered a blink dog den. 
Resting from the rigors of the Section, four blink 
dogs (hp 40, 32, 24, 14) rest on beds of cloth and 
adventuring gear. They do not attack the PCs initial-
ly, but they make their dislike of the PCs‚Äô invasion 
clear. The blink dogs bare their fangs, growling 
and yapping at the PCs. If the PCs do not leave, the 
blink dogs slowly advance, hoping to drive them off. 
If any PCs attack, they immediately retaliate.
Any ranger or druid amongst the PCs can at-
tempt a DC¬†20 Wisdom (Animal Handling) check 
to calm the dogs. Success allows the PCs to remain 
and rest in the room though the blink dogs are 
obviously not pleased with the PCs‚Äô presence.
Encounter Condition: [Safe]
Tactics: The three largest blink dogs launch them-
selves at the PCs, with the alpha male protecting 
the smallest and youngest blink dog. They focus on 
the most aggressive PCs first, concentrating on one 
enemy at a time. They use their limited blink ability 
to flank the PCs.
If the alpha male is killed, the second largest 
takes command of the pack. If it dies, the remain-
ing blink dogs cower in a comer until the PCs leave 
or finish them off.
The smallest is too old to train at this point, 
having been feral too long to be of use to animal 
trainers. However, since blink dogs are lawful 
good creatures, they prefer not to fight. But be-
ing trapped in the dungeon, they grow more and 
more feral with the passage of time. Rangers and 
druids may attempt to calm the blink dogs, requir-
ing a Wisdom (Animal Handling) check in place of 
Charisma (Diplomacy) checks. If the PCs remain for 
2 hours or more, another check is required, lest the 
alpha male grow restless.
If the PCs clear the goblins out of B116 and keep 
the portcullis in Room B118 down, this room is 
considered Safe.

194
Treasure: Among the adventuring gear the blink dogs 
were resting on are two coils of 50¬†ft. rope, a back-
pack, six candles, a tinder box, a rusty carving knife, 
and a waterskin filled with holy water.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encoun-
ter, add one blink dog. To decrease the challenge, 
remove one.
B118 . MOSS-FILLED GUARD 
CHAMBER
The portcullis blocking the PC‚Äôs path is down. In or-
der to open it, the PCs must pull the lever (inside the 
room) down.
Deep green moss covers the walls and ceiling of 
this room. The only bare stone is the floor. The 
moss is rich and thick, taking on the appearance 
of an expensive carpet. The air in this room is 
thick and pungent as well. The moss appears to be 
sucking all the freshness out of the room. Along the 
west wall, a lever juts out.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: The walls and ceiling of this room are the 
remnants of an ancient celestial trap that was dam-
aged in the earthquake. Touching the lever triggers 
a poison dust trap, but opens the portcullis.
 '
Poison Dust Trap. Hidden inside the lever compart-
ment is a glass vial (visible with a DC¬†15 Wisdom 
(Perception check)). Pulling the lever crushes the 
vial releasing a puff of noxious gas. Creatures 
within 5¬†ft of the lever must succeed a Constitution 
saving throw (DC¬†15) or be poisoned for 1 hour. If 
the poison is not cured before that time the victim 
receives 5d10 poison damage when it ends. A DC¬†14 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check is required to 
pull the vial out without dropping it, which would 
set it off.
Encounter Condition: Stagnant Air
Tactics: Along the western wall is a lever that, when 
pulled down, raises the portcullis in the hallway. 
When pushed up, the portcullis lowers.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
replace the poison dust trap‚Äôs effect with insanity 
mist vapor (Room B8). To decrease the challenge, 
remove the trap and raise the portcullis.
B119 . ABANDONED OUTPOST
The door to this room is locked, requiring a DC¬†30 
Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check to unlock. The door 
can be locked from the inside or outside.
This room was once an outpost of some sort; that 
much is obvious at least. A rotted framework, 
probably for bunk beds, leans against one wall. A 
large, stained table takes up the center of the room. 
On the eastern wall, there is a slight discoloration 
in the center from a map that once hung there. 
Along the back wall is a weapons rack.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: This outpost has been abandoned for 
a long time. The furniture is old, and the floor is 
littered with rubble and debris.
No matter how long the PCs search the room, 
they cannot determine who used the room, or what 
they used it for; it dates back to the time of the 
battle that took place in Room B111. The map that 
hung on the wall has long since been destroyed, 
and the only things on the table are dark stains. The 
weapon rack in the back of the room seems to be in 
decent repair and still holds a few weapons.
Encounter Condition: Hazardous Footing 5, [Safe]
Tactics: If the PCs lock the door from the inside, 
nothing can get in to disturb them. The locals con-
sider this room unreachable anyway.
Treasure: At first glance, the weapon‚Äôs rack appears 
trapped, but a DC¬†14 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) 
check reveals that the trigger is fake, designed to 
trick would-be thieves. Over the years the ‚Äútripline‚Äù 
has rotted and nothing resembling a trap remains.
The weapons of a long-dead soldier hang on the 
weapon rack, holding a +1 longbow and a +1 buckler 
in addition to a few mundane odds and ends. The 
GM should place a few javelins and arrows on the 
rack for PCs to replenish their supplies.
Scaling: N/A

B120-B132 . RUINS
The fallout from the earthquake can still be felt here. 
Doors are broken open from the inside. Unholy 
screams fill the corridors. And everywhere the PCs go, 
the smell of death follows them. This place is unfit for 
the living... let alone the dead.
Unlike the majority of the Region, this expanse suf-
fered real damage. The halls are strewn with rubble 
and debris that make traversing them an adventure 
in and of itself. Doors are broken from the inside, 
hanging on their hinges, allowing a glimpse into the 
shadowy confines of the rooms beyond. On top of 
all the damage, there is still the matter of the inhabi-
tants wandering the halls.
The goblins and bugbears may have control over 
their respective sections, but this section is ruled by 
wild creatures and untamed monsters. This makes 
pilgrimages to the shrine that much more difficult as 
beasts threaten the goblins at every turn. This Section 
is not safe.
To add to the disturbing nature of the Section, the 
stench of death and decay permeates the very air. The 
creatures here do not coexist peacefully and between 
their encounters with each other and the goblins that 
enter this area surreptitiously. The results of various 
conflicts have saturated the dungeon. Dark stains, 
scattered bones, and broken weapons mark the vio-
lence of these meetings. Compared to the relatively 
spartan and benign rooms in the other areas, this 
entire section radiates a dangerous aura.
The GM should add the following Encounter Con-
ditions as he sees fit: Echoes 4, Poor Footing 4, and 
Stagnant Air.
Every room‚Äôs door is either open or broken off.
RAnDoM EnCoUnTERs

B120 . THE CROSSROADS
The enormity of this room astounds you. Its sheer, 
white walls and bleached granite ceiling are truly 
impressive. Less impressive are the red scrawled 
runes carved and painted on the walls. The writing 
is hard to decipher, but it appears to be a series of 
taunts and proclamations from one group to the 
other. The center of the room is likewise stained. 
Upon closer inspection, it appears to be blood.
In addition to the room‚Äôs decor, there is an 
unmistakable smell of rot. While the smell isn‚Äôt 
overpowering, it isn‚Äôt comfortable either.
Initial Attitude: N/A
Encounter: Bugbears use this room to lure their en-
emies into a series of traps, all simple but effective. 
Typically, the bugbears run through the room, and 
exit through any one of a number of doors, press-
ing hidden triggers as they go. In actuality, this trick 
has worked nearly a dozen times, and each time the 
bugbears reset the traps, they prepare for another 
wave of gullible victims.
Pressure-sensitive plates underneath the floor 
trigger the first trap, which in turn triggers two 
more. PCs stepping across the floor require a DC¬†12 
Strength (Athletics) or Dexterity (Acrobatics) check 
to avoid triggering the first hail of needles trap. PCs 
that are moving quickly suffer disadvantage on 
this check.
After the hail of needles trap (Room B35), a poison 
dust trap (Room B118) goes off, followed by a spiked 
pit trap (Room B1) in the floor (with a 6-second gap 
between each trap). To make matters worse, the pit 
is lined with spikes. Presently three dead goblins 
line the bottom of the pit, all of which are decom-
posing and covered in maggots.
Encounter Condition: Stagnant Air
Tactics: To safely cross the room the PCs need to lo-
cate the reset mechanism, which is located beneath 
a chipped tile in the northwestern corner of the 
room. There are three separate triggers, each to a 
different trap. A fourth trigger leads to the delay 
between the traps, allowing the PCs the opportunity 
to alter the intervals between the traps from 1 round 
to 6 rounds. This requires a DC¬†13 Dexterity (Sleight 
of Hand) check.
There is a 10% chance that two bugbears are in 
this room resetting and rearming the traps. If so, 
they are Unfriendly to the PCs, having never seen 
humans (etc.) before.
Treasure: Tucked in the southwest corner are two 
dead goblins, maybe 2 or 3 days old. They are cov-
ered in needles and their clothing is torn to shreds. 
The PCs require a DC¬†20 Wisdom (Perception) or 
DC¬†16 Intelligence (Investigation) check to find 
these bodies. They have 1d4¬†sp each in their mauled 
pockets, but the bugbears have stripped everything 
else away.
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add a fire trap (Room B18) that goes off at the bot-
tom of the pit. To decrease the challenge, remove 
the fungal dust vapor trap.
B121 . BUGBEAR BIVOUAC
This small room has been taken over by a group of 
bugbears. They bark and growl at you as you enter, 
tightening their grip on their clubs. The bugbears 
seem wary and tired, waiting for you to make the 
first move.
Initial Attitude: Unfriendly
Encounter: Three bugbear soldiers use this location 
to harass the goblin pilgrims traveling to the shrine 
(Room B134). Any disruption of the goblin king‚Äôs 
minions is seen as a victory to the bugbears and 
they take full advantage of the long trip many gob-
lins make to visit their deity.
If the PCs can convince the bugbears they are 
friends, their attitude shifts to Indifferent and they 
allow the PCs to make use of the room to rest. If 
the bugbears believe the PCs are allied with either 
faction of goblins, their attitude instantly becomes 
Hostile and they attack the PCs.
Encounter Condition: [Safe]
Tactics: The bugbears know they are outmatched, and 
avoid a fight if possible. They gang up on the near-
est PC and use them as a human shield if possible. 
They stay close together, making sure they cannot 
be flanked, engaging the PCs en masse only when 
safe, and taking down opponents as quickly as pos-
sible‚Äîthey know the cost of a protracted fight.
Treasure: N/A
Scaling: To increase the challenge of this encounter, 
add one bugbear and change their initial attitude to 
Hostile. To decrease the challenge, have the bug-
bears out on patrol, only to return in 1d6 minutes.
